Voluntary Prayer While Sitting and on a Mount
Ruling on voluntary prayer while sitting and on a mount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on offering nafl prayer while sitting and on a mount, and explain the reward implications using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Sitting during nafl prayer is permissible even without excuse, but the reward is half—standing is better.

Many Muslims wonder whether voluntary prayer can be offered while sitting, especially when tired or traveling. This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling with clear proof from the Sunnah, showing that Allah has made worship easy while maintaining the virtue of standing. Let's explore how the Prophet ﷺ taught us flexibility in voluntary acts.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (nafl prayer) and the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) to pray sitting even if able to stand.
The text says 'يجوز النفل قاعدا مع القدرة على القيام'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn which explicitly compares standing, sitting, and lying down.
Hadith: 'من صلى قائما فهو افضل ومن صلى قاعدا فله نصف اجر القائم'.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies permissibility because it assigns reward to sitting; if it were invalid, no reward would be given. The phrase 'half the reward' indicates validity but lesser virtue.
4
Consider prayer on a mount
The passage also permits nafl on a mount during travel, facing the direction of travel if qibla is not possible.
Hadith of Jabir and Amir ibn Rabi'a.
5
Note the preferred posture
In the preferred school, one sits like in tashahhud (mukhtar madhhab).
Text: 'ومختار مذہب میں یہ ہے کہ جس طرح تحیات میں بیٹھتے ہیں اس طرح بیٹھے۔'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

صففت انا و اليتيم ورائه و العجوز من ورائنا فصلى لنا رسول الله له ركعتين ثم انصرف ۔ (بخاری شریف، باب الصلاة على الحصیر ، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۸۰) اس حدیث میں بغیر کسی بلاوہ کے چار آدمیوں نے جماعت کے ساتھ نفل پڑھی۔
فصل : بیٹھ کر اور جانور پرنفل نماز کا بیان
ضروری نوٹ : نفل نماز سہولت کے طور پر ہے اس لئے اس بات کی گنجائش دی گئی ہے کہ قیام پر قدرت کے باوجود بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے، البتہ عذر نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر نفل پڑھنے سے آدھا ثواب ملے گا ، اور اس کی بھی گنجائش دی گئی ہے سواری پر بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے اور جس جانب سواری جارہی ہو، اگر قبلے کی جانب متوجہ ہو نا ممکن نہ ہو تو سواری کے منہ کی طرف رخ کر کے نماز پڑھتا جائے۔
صلى الله
وجه : ( ا ) عن . عمران بن حصين قال سألت النبي الله عن صلوة الرجل وهو قاعد فقال من صلى قائما فهو افضل ومن صلى قاعدا فله نصف اجر القائم ومن صلى نائما فله نصف اجر القاعد (بخاری شریف، باب صلوة القاعد بص ۱۵۰ نمبر ۱۱۱۶ارترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء ان صلوة القاعد على النصف من صلوۃ القائم ، ص ۸۵ نمبر ۳۷۱) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفل نماز قدرت کے باوجود بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے، البتہ اس کو ثواب کھڑے ہونے والے سے آدھا ملے گا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے جابر بن عبد الله اخبره ان النبی الا الله كان يصلي التطوع وهو راكب في غير القبلة . (بخاری شریف ، باب صلوۃ التطوع على الدواب حيثما تو جھت به ،ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۰۹۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث تو جهت ، ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۶۱۰/۷۰۰) (۳) عامر بن ربيعة اخبره قال رأيت النبي وهو على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله لم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة . (بخارى شريف، باب بیزل للمكتوبه ص ۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۷ر مسلم شريف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث توجهت ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۶۱۸/۷۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کے رخ کے خلاف نفل نماز پڑھ لے تب بھی جائز ہوگی۔ ترجمه : (۶۲۸) قیام پر قدرت ہوتے ہوئے بھی بیٹھ کر نفل نماز جائز ہے لیکن بلا عذر نصف اجر ہوگا۔ تشریح : اوپر حدیث گزرچکی ہے۔
صلى الله
ترجمه : (۶۲۹) اور مختار مذہب میں یہ ہے کہ جس طرح تحیات میں بیٹھتے ہیں اس طرح بیٹھے۔
Section on performing voluntary prayer while sitting and prayer on a mount. (628) It is permissible to perform voluntary prayer while sitting even if one is able to stand, but he receives half the reward of the one who stands, except with an excuse. (229) And he sits... Evidence: From Anas ibn Malik that his grandmother Mulayka invited the Messenger of Allah for food she had prepared... The Messenger of Allah stood, and I and the orphan lined up behind him, and the old woman behind us. The Messenger of Allah prayed two rak'ahs for us, then left. (Bukhari, Chapter of prayer on a mat, p. 68, no. 380) In this hadith, four people performed voluntary prayer in congregation without being summoned. Section: Explanation of voluntary prayer while sitting and on an animal. Essential note: Voluntary prayer is based on ease; therefore, concession is given that one may pray sitting even if able to stand. However, if there is no excuse, praying sitting will earn half the reward. And concession is also given that one may pray sitting on a mount, and if facing the qibla is not possible, one may pray facing the direction the mount is headed. Evidence: (1) From Imran ibn Husayn: I asked the Prophet about a man praying while sitting, and he said: 'Whoever prays standing, that is better; whoever prays sitting, for him is half the reward of the one who stands; and whoever prays lying down, for him is half the reward of the one who sits.' (Bukhari, Chapter of the prayer of a sick person sitting, p. 150, no. 1116; Tirmidhi, Chapter of the prayer of a sitting person being half of the standing person's prayer, p. 85, no. 371) This hadith shows that voluntary prayer can be performed sitting even with ability, but the reward is half that of standing. (2) Another hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah informed him that the Prophet used to perform voluntary prayers while riding, not facing the qibla. (Bukhari, Chapter of voluntary prayer on mounts wherever they face, p. 138, no. 1094; Muslim, Chapter of the permissibility of voluntary prayer on an animal during travel wherever it faces, p. 244, no. 1610/700) (3) Amir ibn Rabi'a informed him: I saw the Prophet on a mount performing nafl, bowing his head in which direction he faced, and the Messenger of Allah never did that in the obligatory prayer. (Bukhari, Chapter of what is permissible for the obligatory prayer, p. 48, no. 1097; Muslim, Chapter of the permissibility of voluntary prayer on an animal during travel wherever it faces, p. 244, no. 1618/700) This hadith shows that even if one prays voluntary prayer in a direction other than the qibla, it is permissible. Translation: (628) Voluntary prayer is permissible while sitting even if able to stand, but without excuse, half reward. Explanation: The hadith has passed above. (629) And in the preferred school, one should sit in the same manner as sitting in the tashahhud.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage consists of rulings with proof regarding voluntary (nafl) prayers performed while sitting or on a mount. It begins by stating the basic ruling: it is permissible to offer nafl prayers while sitting even if one is able to stand, but the reward is half that of standing, unless there is an excuse (such as illness). The author then provides several hadith proofs. The first hadith (from Anas) illustrates that nafl can be performed in congregation. The crucial hadith from Imran ibn Husayn explicitly establishes the reward differential: standing is best, sitting gives half reward, and lying down gives half of that. The passage also addresses prayer on a mount during travel: it is permissible to pray nafl on a mount, and if facing the qibla is impossible, one may pray in the direction of travel. The final note mentions that in the preferred school (mukhtar madhhab), the sitting posture for nafl should be like that of tashahhud (sitting between prostration). This section highlights the leniency of the Shariah regarding voluntary acts.

Key Terms
نفل (nafal): Voluntary, supererogatory prayers performed for extra reward beyond obligatory prayers.
اجر (ajr): Spiritual reward from Allah for performing acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the reward for a person who offers nafl prayer sitting without any excuse compared to one who stands?
A) Full reward
B) Half reward
C) No reward
D) Double reward

Key Takeaway
Sitting during nafl prayer is permissible even without excuse, but the reward is half that of standing.

Preferred Sitting Posture for Nafl Prayer
Ruling with proof for preferred sitting posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred sitting posture for nafl prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence for it.

Core Idea
Sit for nafl like tashahhud: left foot spread, right foot erect.

The sitting posture during nafl prayer is a sunnah, not a fard. The Hanafi school recommends the same posture as that adopted during tashahhud in the obligatory prayer. This lesson presents the textual evidence from the Prophet's practice and clarifies the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening line: 'And he should sit like the mutashahhid in the chosen (position).' This is the core ruling.
The word 'al-mukhtār' indicates the relied-upon position of the school.
2
Understand the posture
The commentary describes the posture: right foot erect, left foot spread, sitting on it. This is the iftirāsh posture.
This is the same as the sitting for tashahhud in a two-rak'ah prayer.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: one from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi and one from Wa'il ibn Hujr. Both describe the Prophet's sitting posture during tashahhud.
The hadith are from Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, and Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
4
Determine the legal force
The text says this is the most excellent way, but sitting otherwise due to necessity is still valid. This shows it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard.
The ruling anatomy below clarifies the hukm level.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقعد كالمتشهد فى المختار
ترجمه : (۶۲۹) اور مختار مذہب میں یہ ہے کہ جس طرح تحیات میں بیٹھتے ہیں اس طرح بیٹھے۔
تشریح : مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ جس طرح تشہد پڑھتے وقت بیٹھتے ہیں اس طرح بیٹھ کر نفلی نماز پڑھے۔ کیونکہ بیٹھنے میں یہ سب سے افضل طریقہ ہے۔ لیکن مجبوری کی وجہ سے دوسرے طریقے پر بیٹھا تب بھی جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) تشہد میں بیٹھنے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ دایاں پاؤں کھڑا کرے اور بایاں بچھائے اور اس پر سرین رکھ کر بیٹھ جائے ۔ اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فقال ابو حميد الساعدي.... فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمني واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب سنتہ الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ۱۴، نمبر ۸۸۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفته الصلوة وما ينفتح به ص۱۹۴ نمبر ۱۱۱۰٫۴۹۸) (۲) عن وائل بن حجر قال قدمت المدينة قلت لانظرن الى صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما جلس يعنى للتشهد افترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى يعنى على فخذه اليسرى ونصب رجله الیمنی۔ (ترمذی شریف، باب کیف الجلوس في التشهد ص ۶۵ نمبر ۲۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بایاں پاؤں بچھائے اور اس پر سرین رکھ کر بیٹھ کر جائے اور دایاں پاؤں کھڑا کرے ، یہی زیادہ مختار ہے۔
And he should sit like the mutashahhid (one reciting tashahhud) in the chosen (position). Translation: (629) And in the preferred madhhab, he should sit in the same manner as he sits in tashahhud. Explanation: The preferred madhhab is that he should sit for nafl prayer in the same manner as when reciting tashahhud, because that is the most excellent way of sitting. However, if he sits in another way due to necessity, it is still permissible. Proof: (1) The manner of sitting in tashahhud is: erect the right foot, spread the left foot, and sit on it. For this, there is the hadith: Abu Humayd al-Sa‘idi said: ... When he sat in the two rak‘ahs, he sat on his left foot and erected the right; when he sat in the final rak‘ah, he put forward his left foot, erected the other, and sat on his buttocks. (Bukhari, Chapter on Sunnah of Sitting in Tashahhud, p.14 no.828; Muslim, Chapter on Description of Prayer and Its Opening, p.194 no.1110/498) (2) From Wa’il ibn Hujr: He said: I came to Medina and said: I will surely look at the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). When he sat—meaning for tashahhud—he spread his left foot, placed his left hand on his left thigh, and erected his right foot. (Tirmidhi, Chapter on How to Sit in Tashahhud, p.65 no.292) In these hadiths, it is stated that he should spread the left foot, sit on it, and erect the right foot; that is the more chosen (method).
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage clarifies the preferred (mukhtār) sitting posture for performing nafl prayers. The text states that the person should sit in the same manner as when reciting tashahhud in the obligatory prayer—that is, sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect. This is derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Abu Humayd al-Sa‘idi and Wa’il ibn Hujr. The commentary in Urdu emphasizes that this is the most virtuous way, but if one sits differently due to necessity (e.g., pain or lack of space), the prayer remains valid. The hadith evidence is presented to show that the Prophet's sitting in tashahhud was consistent with this posture. The Hanafi school considers this sitting posture as recommended (sunnah) for all prayers, both fard and nafl, when sitting is required. However, for nafl prayers where one is sitting voluntarily, this posture is especially preferred.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtār): The chosen or preferred ruling in the Hanafi school, often the mufta bihi.
كالمتشهد (ka’l-mutashahhid): Like the one reciting tashahhud; refers to the sitting posture during the tashahhud in salat.
الافتراش (al-iftirāsh): Sitting on the left foot, right foot erect; the sunnah posture for tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the status of the nafl prayer if one sits in a posture other than the described preferred way?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the person has committed a sin.
C) The prayer is valid but the person has missed a sunnah.
D) The prayer is valid and the action is mubah.

Key Takeaway
The preferred sitting posture for nafl prayer is the same as for tashahhud (iftirāsh); other postures are permissible but less meritorious.

Permissibility of Sitting in Nafl Prayer: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on completing a nafl prayer sitting after starting standing, explain the Sahibayn's objection, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Starting a nafl standing does not bind you to finish standing—permissibility is the relied-upon view, though standing is better.

This passage addresses a practical situation: you begin a voluntary prayer standing, but later feel like sitting. Is that allowed? The matn says yes, without dislike. However, the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—disagree, holding it makruh if there is no excuse. This intra-madhhab dispute illustrates how different principles (permissibility vs. sticking to initial intention) can yield different rulings. The chosen view (mufta bihi) is the permissive one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
Specifically: completing nafl sitting after starting standing. Position A (matn/Imam): permissible without dislike. Position B (Sahibayn): makruh if no excuse.
2
State the proof for each position
The matn's proof: hadith of Aisha showing the Prophet changed posture. Sahibayn's probable proof: principle that one should adhere to the initial intention unless excused.
The text does not quote Sahibayn's proof directly; it is inferred from their general methodology.
3
Examine the hadith's application
The hadith shows the Prophet going from sitting to standing, not standing to sitting. How does it support the opposite? By qiyas (analogy): if changing from sitting to standing is allowed, the reverse is also allowed.
This is a standard extension of the evidence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: a person who starts standing may sit without sin according to the matn; but if he follows the Sahibayn, he should not sit unless he has an excuse.
5
Identify the tarjih
The matn declares it 'ala sahh (on the correct narration). This indicates the preferred position is the permissive one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز اتـمـامـه قـاعدا بعد افتتـاحـه قـائـمـا بلا كراهة على صح
ترجمه : (۱۳۰) اور نفل کو بیٹھ کر پورا کرنا جائز ہے اس کے بعد کہ کھڑا ہو کر شروع کیا ہو، بغیر کراہیت کے صحیح روایت میں۔
تشریح : نفل کھڑا ہو کر شروع کیا ہو اس کو بیٹھ کر پورا کرنا چاہتا ہو تو صحیح روایت میں یہ ہے کہ بغیر کراہیت کے جائز ہے۔ صاحبین کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ کھڑا ہو کر شروع ہوا اور کوئی عذر نہ ہو تو کھڑا ہو کر ہی پوری کرے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلى جالسا فيقرأ وهو جالس فاذا بقى من قرأتـه نـحـو مــن ثـلثين آية او اربعين آية قام فقرأها وهو قائم ثم ركع ثم سجد يفعل في الركعة الثانية مثل ذلک . (بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اصلی قاعد اثم صبح او وجد خفته تم مابقی ص ۱۵۰ نمبر ۱۱۹ار مسلم شریف ، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۳۱ ۱۷۰۴/۷) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیٹھ کر بھی نماز پڑھی اور کھڑے ہو کر بھی جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھڑے ہوکر شروع کیا تو بیٹھ کر پوری کر سکتا ہے۔ اگر چہ کھڑا ہو کر ہی پوری کرنا بہتر ہے۔
And it is permissible to complete it while sitting after having begun it while standing, without dislike, according to the correct (narration). Translation: (130) And completing the nafl prayer while sitting after having begun it while standing is permissible without dislike, in the correct narration. Explanation: If one begins nafl while standing, and then wishes to complete it sitting, the correct narration states it is permissible without dislike. The position of the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that if he began standing and has no excuse, he should complete it standing. Proof: (1) In a hadith from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray while sitting and recite while sitting; then when about thirty or forty verses remained of his recitation, he would stand and recite them standing, then bow and prostrate. He would do likewise in the second rak‘ah. (Bukhari, Chapter on If One Prays Sitting Then Becomes Active or Feels Lightness, p.150 no.1119; Muslim, Chapter on Permissibility of Nafl Prayer Standing and Sitting, p.252, no.1704/7) In this hadith, he prayed both sitting and standing, implying that if one begins standing, he may complete sitting. However, completing standing is still better.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person begins a nafl prayer while standing, then decides to complete the remaining rak‘ahs while sitting. According to the correct narration (al-ṣaḥīḥ), this is permissible without any dislike (karāhah). The text then notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if one started standing without an excuse, he should complete it standing; abandoning standing without reason is makruh. However, the preferred view (as per the matn) is that it is permissible even without excuse, though standing is better. The hadith of Aisha is cited as evidence, showing the Prophet sometimes sat and sometimes stood in the same prayer, changing posture. This demonstrates flexibility. The Hanafi ruling is based on this apparent permissibility, while the Sahibayn emphasize the principle of sticking to the initial intention if no excuse arises. The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, one may change to sitting even if healthy, but it is more meritorious to complete standing.

Key Terms
بلا كراهة (bilā karāhah): Without dislike; the act is permissible and not blameworthy.
صاحبين (al-ṣāḥibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
على صح (‘alā ṣaḥḥ): According to the correct narration; indicates the preferred reliable transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Nafl Prayer on a Riding Animal Outside the City
Ruling on nafl prayer while riding outside the city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for performing nafl prayer on a riding animal according to the Hanafi school and apply the hadith proof to justify the concession.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a mount outside the city is permissible with gestures, facing any direction; inside the city, qibla is required.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that allows a traveler to perform voluntary (nafl) prayer while riding an animal outside the city limits, making head gestures instead of full prostrations, without facing the qibla. The concession is based on the Prophet's practice and is limited to non-obligatory prayers during travel. We will analyze the conditions, the evidence, and the practical application of this sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
State the ruling: it is permissible (jā’iz) to perform nafl prayer while riding outside the city. Note the conditions: nafl prayer only, outside the city (khārij al-miṣr), on a riding animal (dābbah), and making gestures (īmā’) instead of full ruku‘ and sujud.
The ruling does not apply to obligatory prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence: the narration of ‘Āmir ibn Rabī‘ah who saw the Prophet gesturing with his head while on his mount, facing any direction, and the Prophet did not do that for obligatory prayers. This hadith is reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophetic action of gesturing and not facing qibla indicates permissibility for nafl. The explicit exclusion of obligatory prayers shows the ruling is limited to voluntary prayers.
The absence of qibla requirement is a concession specific to travel.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any scholarly differences: all major schools agree on the permissibility of nafl on a mount during travel, but conditions vary. The Hanafi school emphasizes the restriction to 'outside the city'.
This ruling is muttafaq alayh in essence, with minor differences in details.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
Apply the ruling: outside the city, one may pray nafl facing any direction with gestures. Inside the city, even if riding, one must face qibla and perform full postures.
This affects travelers in transit, such as on buses or planes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتنفل راكبا خارج المصر مؤميا الى اي جهة توجهت دابته
ترجمه : (۶۳۱) اور سوار پر شہر سے باہر جس جہت کی طرف چوپایہ متوجہ ہو اشارہ سے نفل پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
تشریح : شہر سے باہر سواری جس طرف جا رہی ہو اسی طرف رخ کر کے نفل پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ شہر سے باہر نہ ہو بلکہ شہر کے اندر ہو اور سواری پر نہ ہو تو قبلے کی طرف توجہ کئے بغیر نفل نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ قبلہ فرض ہے یہ تو حدیث کی بنا پر یہ سہولت دی گئی ہے۔
وجه : (ا) عامر بن ربيعة اخبره قال رأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة . (بخارى شريف، باب صلوة التطوع على الدواب حيثما تو جھت به ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۰۹۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث توجهت ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۶۱۰/۷۰۰)
And he should perform nafl prayer while riding outside the city, making gestures (with the head) towards whichever direction his mount faces. Translation: (631) And while mounted, outside the city, it is permissible to perform nafl prayer with gestures towards whichever direction the animal is headed. Explanation: Outside the city, it is permissible to pray nafl facing the direction the ride is going. If he is not outside the city but inside the city, and not on a mount, then nafl without facing qibla is not valid, because qibla is obligatory. This concession is given on the basis of hadith. Proof: (1) Amir ibn Rabi‘ah reported: He said: I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) on his mount, making tasbih (nafl prayer), gesturing with his head towards any direction he faced, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not do that in the obligatory prayer. (Bukhari, Book of Supererogatory Prayer on Animals, p.138 no.1094; Muslim, Book of Permissibility of Nafl Prayer on Animals in Travel, p.244 no.1610/700)
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage grants a concession for nafl prayer while riding outside the city limits. The ruling states that one may perform nafl prayer on a riding animal (or vehicle) while traveling outside the city, making gestures (īmā’) with the head instead of full bowing and prostrating, and facing any direction the animal faces—even if not toward the qibla. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this concession is only for outside the city; inside the city, one must face qibla and cannot do nafl on a moving animal without proper posture. The basis is the practice of the Prophet as reported by Amir ibn Rabi‘ah. This ruling applies to voluntary prayers (nafl) only, not obligatory prayers, which require qibla and proper postures even on a journey. The Hanafi school maintains that the concession is for travel outside inhabited areas, and the gesture must be minimal—slightly bowing the head for ruku‘ and more for sujud.

Key Terms
مؤميا (mu’miyan): Making gestures; nodding the head for ruku‘ and sujud instead of full movement.
خارج المصر (khārij al-miṣr): Outside the city; beyond the built-up area.
دابة (dābbah): Riding animal; includes horse, camel, mule, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Anywhere, including inside the city.
B) Only outside the city limits.
C) Only if there is fear or rain.
D) Only for obligatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer while riding outside the city is permissible with gestures without facing qibla, but this concession does not apply inside the city.

Ruling on Nafl Prayer While Sitting: Posture and Completing Standing Prayer Sitting
States ruling on nafl prayer while sitting and manner of sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred sitting posture for nafl prayer and explain the permissibility of completing a standing nafl while sitting, citing the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows completing a standing nafl while sitting without dislike, though standing is better.

This lesson examines two related rulings on voluntary (nafl) prayer while sitting: the recommended sitting posture and the permissibility of completing a standing-nafl while sitting. The text presents the Hanafi position supported by hadith, alongside the differing view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Understanding these rulings helps the student apply the school’s methodology in deriving practical fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-issues
The passage addresses two distinct rulings: (1) the preferred sitting posture for nafl prayer (like tashahhud), and (2) whether it is permissible to complete a nafl prayer while sitting if it was started standing.
2
State the Hanafi position on each
For sitting posture: the chosen (mukhtar) position is to sit as in tashahhud (left foot spread, right foot raised). For completion: it is permissible without dislike to finish sitting, even if started standing.
3
Identify the proof (dalil) for each ruling
The posture ruling is based on hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi and Wa'il ibn Hujr describing the Prophet's sitting. The completion ruling uses the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet praying partly sitting and partly standing.
These ahadith are ahad (non-mutawatir) but accepted as evidence.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn hold that if there is no excuse, one must complete standing. The text favours the view that it is permissible without excuse, but completing standing is better.
The mufta bihi position is the mukhtar view of general permissibility.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A person who begins a nafl prayer standing may validly complete it sitting without needing an excuse. However, to follow the more virtuous (afdal) practice, they should complete standing if able.

Source Text

في صلوة النوافل جالسا كالمتشهد فى المختار (٦٣٠) وجاز إتمامه قاعدا بعد افتتاحه قائما بلا كراهة على صح . تشریح : مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ جس طرح تشہد پڑھتے وقت بیٹھتے ہیں اس طرح بیٹھ کر نفلی نماز پڑھے۔ کیونکہ بیٹھنے میں یہ سب سے افضل طریقہ ہے۔ لیکن مجبوری کی وجہ سے دوسرے طریقے پر بیٹھا تب بھی جائز ہے۔ وجه : (١) تشہد میں بیٹھنے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ دایاں پاؤں کھڑا کرے اور بایاں بچھائے اور اس پر سرین رکھ کر بیٹھ جائے ۔ اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فقال ابو حميد الساعدي.... فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمني واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب سنتہ الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ١٤، نمبر ٨٨٢٨ مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفته الصلوة وما ينفتح به ص۱۹۴ نمبر ١١١٠٫٤٩٨) (٢) عن وائل بن حجر قال قدمت المدينة قلت لانظرن الى صلوة رسول الله ﷺ فلما جلس يعنى للتشهد افترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى يعنى على فخذه اليسرى ونصب رجله الیمنی۔ (ترمذی شریف، باب کیف الجلوس في التشهد ص ٦٥ نمبر ٢٩٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بایاں پاؤں بچھائے اور اس پر سرین رکھ کر بیٹھ کر جائے اور دایاں پاؤں کھڑا رکھے ، یہی زیادہ مختار ہے۔ ترجمه : (٦٣٠) اور نفل کو بیٹھ کر پورا کرنا جائز ہے اس کے بعد کہ کھڑا ہو کر شروع کیا ہو، بغیر کراہیت کے صحیح روایت میں۔ تشریح : نفل کھڑا ہو کر شروع کیا ہوا اس کو بیٹھ کر پورا کرنا چاہتا ہو تو صحیح روایت میں یہ ہے کہ بغیر کراہیت کے جائز ہے۔ صاحبین کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ کھڑا ہو کر شروع ہوا اور کوئی عذر نہ ہو تو کھڑا ہو کر ہی پوری کرے۔ وجه : (١) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلى جالسا فيقرأ وهو جالس فاذا بقى من قرأته نحو من ثلاثين آية او اربعين آية قام فقرأها وهو قائم ثم ركع ثم سجد يفعل في الركعة الثانية مثل ذلک . (بخاری شریف ، باب اذ صلى قاعد ثم صح او وجد خفته تم ما بقی ص ١٥٠ نمبر ١١٩١ مسلم شریف ، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ص ٢٥٢، نمبر ٣١ ١٧٠٤/٧) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیٹھ کر بھی نماز پڑھی اور کھڑے ہو کر بھی جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھڑے ہوکر شروع کیا تو بیٹھ کر پوری کر سکتا ہے۔ اگر چہ کھڑا ہو کر ہی پوری کرنا بہتر ہے۔
On voluntary prayers while sitting: Like the tashahhud in the reliable position. (630) And it is permissible to complete it sitting after starting it standing, without dislike, according to the correct view. Commentary: The chosen school is that one should pray voluntary prayers sitting in the same manner as sitting during tashahhud. Because this is the most virtuous way of sitting. However, if due to necessity one sits in another manner, it is also permissible. Proof: (1) The manner of sitting in tashahhud is: raise the right foot, lay the left flat, and sit on it. The hadith: Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi said: When he sat in the two rak'ahs, he sat on his left leg and raised his right; when he sat in the last rak'ah, he put forward his left leg and raised the other and sat on his buttocks. (Bukhari, Muslim) (2) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I came to Madina and said: Let me see the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. When he sat for tashahhud, he spread his left leg and placed his left hand on his left thigh and raised his right leg. (Tirmidhi) In this hadith, placing the left foot flat and sitting on it, and raising the right foot, that is more chosen. Translation: (630) And it is permissible to complete a voluntary prayer while sitting after having started it standing, without dislike, according to a sound narration. Commentary: If one started a voluntary prayer standing and wants to complete it sitting, the correct narration says it is permissible without dislike. The position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that if one started standing and there is no excuse, one should complete it standing. Proof: (1) Hadith from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah used to pray sitting and recite while sitting, and when about thirty or forty verses remained, he would stand and recite them while standing, then bow and prostrate, and do similarly in the second rak'ah. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that he prayed both sitting and standing, meaning that if one started standing, he can complete it sitting, though completing it standing is better.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on voluntary prayers (nafl) while sitting. It covers two sub-issues: the preferred sitting posture for nafl, and the permissibility of completing a nafl prayer while sitting even if started standing. The ruling in the reliable position (al-mukhtar) is that the sitting posture for nafl should be like that of tashahhud—sitting on the left foot with the right foot raised. This is supported by hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi and Wa'il ibn Hujr. The second ruling states that if one begins a nafl prayer standing, it is permissible (without dislike) to complete it sitting, according to the correct narration (sahih). However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if there is no excuse, one should complete it standing. The proof is the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet would sometimes stand and sometimes sit during voluntary prayers. The Hanafi position is that completion while sitting is allowed, though completing standing is better.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer, not obligatory.
تشہد (tashahhud): The sitting for recitation of the testimony of faith in prayer.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two primary students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is not permissible at all.
B) It is permissible without dislike.
C) It is permissible only if there is an excuse.
D) It is wajib to complete standing.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, it is permissible without dislike to complete a standing nafl prayer while sitting, although completing standing is better.

Ruling on Nafl Prayer While Riding Outside the City
States ruling and proofs for nafl on mount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on offering nafl prayer while riding outside the city, cite the three hadith proofs, and distinguish the condition of being outside vs inside the city.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a mount facing any direction is permissible only outside the city; inside, qibla is obligatory.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents a practical concession for the traveler. The ruling is straightforward but includes an important spatial condition: the concession applies only outside the built-up area (al-misr). We will examine the proofs from the Sunnah that establish this ease and clarify the boundary condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? Offering nafl (voluntary) prayer while riding on a mount. The hukm level is mubah (permissible) under a specific condition.
The act is nafl, not fard; fard prayer must always face qibla and be performed with full postures.
2
Locate the condition
The passage explicitly limits the concession to being 'outside the city' (kharij al-misr). Inside the city, one must face qibla even for nafl. This is because qibla is obligatory (fard) and the concession is a dispensation for travel.
The term 'misr' here means the built-up area, not just the city limits.
3
Examine the dalil
Three hadiths are cited: (a) 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah saw the Prophet indicating with his head on a mount, (b) Jabir reported the Prophet prayed nafl while riding not facing qibla, (c) 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar's practice and his attribution to the Prophet.
All hadiths are from Bukhari and Muslim, indicating strong authenticity.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit actions of the Prophet and companion demonstrate permissibility. The hadiths show that the Prophet prayed voluntarily on his mount without facing qibla, and indicated with head movements. This is the proof for the Hanafi ruling.
The Imperative (amr) is absent; the proof is through the Prophet's actual practice (fi'l).
5
Note cross-madhhab nuance
Some other schools may restrict this concession to cases of necessity or to travel beyond a certain distance. The Hanafi school, however, follows the apparent meaning of the hadiths, making it permissible generally outside the city.
The Hanafi position is based on the zahir of the Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(بخارى شریف ، باب صلوۃ التطوع علی الدواب حيثما توجهت به، ص ١٧٦، نمبر ١٠٩٤ و مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حیث توجهت ، ص ٢٤٤، نمبر ١٦١٠/٧٠٠) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کے رخ کے خلاف نفل نماز پڑھ لے تب بھی جائز ہوگی ۔ (٣) اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ شہر سے باہر ، کیونکہ اس میں سفر کا لفظ موجود ہے۔ كان عبد الله بن عمر يصلي في السفر على راحلته اينما توجهت به یؤمى وذكر عبد الله ان النبى ﷺ كان يفعله . (بخاری شریف، باب الایماء علی الدابة ، ص ١٣٨، نمبر ١٠٩٦ و مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابۃ فی السفر ، ص ٢٤٤، نمبر ١٦١٤/٧٠٠) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر سفر میں قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ شہر میں ایسا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(631) And one may offer voluntary prayers while riding outside the city, indicating with head movements towards any direction the mount faces. Commentary: Outside the city, it is permissible to pray nafl facing the direction the mount is going. If one is not outside the city but inside the city and not on a mount, then nafl without facing qibla is not valid. Because qibla is obligatory; this concession is given based on hadith. Proof: (1) 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah reported: I saw the Prophet on a mount glorifying (praying) and he indicated with his head towards any direction he faced. (Bukhari, Muslim) (2) Jabir ibn 'Abdullah reported: The Prophet used to pray voluntary prayers while riding, not facing qibla. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that even if one prays nafl opposite to the direction of qibla, it is permissible. (3) From this hadith, it can be inferred that it is outside the city, because the word travel (safar) is mentioned. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar used to pray during travel on his mount, facing whatever direction it went, indicating with his head, and he said the Prophet used to do that. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar would pray during travel facing other than qibla. Meaning that doing so inside the city is not permissible.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on offering nafl (voluntary) prayers while riding a mount outside the city (i.e., during travel). The ruling states that one may pray nafl on a mount outside the city, facing any direction the mount is going, by indicating with head movements (ima') instead of full bowing and prostration. This concession is specific to travel outside the city (outside the built-up area). Inside the city, one must face the qibla. The proofs are three hadith: (1) 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah saw the Prophet praying nafl on a mount and indicating with his head; (2) Jabir reports the Prophet prayed voluntary prayers while riding not facing qibla; (3) Ibn 'Umar's practice during travel. The commentary emphasizes that this is a concession for travel, and it is not permissible inside the city.

Key Terms
مومیا (mu'min): Indicating with head movements instead of full bowing and prostration.
خارج المصر (kharij al-misr): Outside the city or settled area; during travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for offering nafl prayer on a mount without facing qibla?
A) The prayer must be at night.
B) The mount must be a camel.
C) The person must be outside the city.
D) The prayer must be offered in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer on a mount facing any direction is permissible only when one is outside the built-up area, as established by the Sunnah.

Building upon Descent vs. Mount in Nafl Prayer
States ruling on validity of continuing nafl after dismounting vs. mounting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on continuing a nafl prayer after dismounting versus mounting, and explain the reasoning based on the strength of tahrima and the principle that a weak act can be built upon a strong one.

Core Idea
A weak prayer can be built upon a strong one, but not vice versa.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a specific scenario in nafl prayer: can you continue your prayer after dismounting from a ride, or after mounting? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the two, basing its ruling on the strength of the initial commitment (tahrima) and the principle that a weaker form can be built upon a stronger one. Understanding this principle helps you avoid invalidating your prayer during travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two scenarios
Read the opening sentence: 'And he may continue upon his descent, not upon his mounting.' The act is continuing (bina) a nafl prayer after changing mode. Two scenarios: (i) starting on a mount and dismounting, (ii) starting on the ground and mounting.
The ruling is asymmetric.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
From the text: starting on mount → dismounting allowed (yabni). Starting on ground → mounting not allowed (la yabni). This is the mufta bihi position.
The hukm level is mubah (permissible) for descent, and makruh tahrimi or haram for mounting? The text says 'la yabni' meaning invalid, so building upon mounting invalidates the prayer.
3
Understand the first reason: nature of tahrima on the mount
When you recite the takbir while mounted, you commit to gesturing for bowing and prostration, but also to perform full postures if possible. So the tahrima includes both modes. Dismounting does not contradict this commitment.
This flexibility is the basis for allowing continuation.
4
Apply the principle: weak upon strong allowed
The text states: 'A weak act can be built upon a strong one, but a strong act cannot be built upon a weak one.' The prayer on the mount is weaker (gestures), on the ground stronger (full postures). Therefore, weak (mount) can be built upon strong (ground), but not the reverse.
This is the core usul principle (qa'ida) employed.
5
Note the third reason: amal kathir
Dismounting does not involve excessive movement (amal kathir), so the continuity is preserved. Mounting, however, involves climbing which is amal kathir and breaks the prayer.
This reinforces the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦٣٢) وبنى بنزوله لا بركوبه تشریح : سوار ہو کر نفل شروع کی اب ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد نیچے اتر کر اس پر بنا کرنا چاہتا ہے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر زمین پر نفل شروع کی اور ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد سوار ہو کر اس پر بنا کرنا چاہے تو بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔ وجه : (١) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سواری پر تحریمہ باندھا تو اپنے اوپر لازم کیا کہ رکوع سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا اور ہو سکے گا تو پورا رکوع اور سجدہ بھی کرے گا، تو گویا کہ اشارہ کر کے اور باضابطہ رکوع اور سجدہ کرے گا دونوں کا تحریمہ باندھا ہے۔ اسلئے سواری پر بھی نفل پڑھے اور نیچے اتر کر بھی بناء کرسکتا ہے (٢) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ سواری پر رکوع اور سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا اور قیام بھی نہیں کر سکے گا اسلئے سواری پر نماز کمزور ہے اور نیچے اترے گا تو رکوع اور سجدے کا اتمام کرے گا اور قیام بھی کرے گا اسلئے نیچے اترنے میں تحریمہ قوی ہے، اسلئے ضعیف کی بناء قومی پر ہو سکتی ہے، اسلئے بھی سواری سے اتر کر بناء کر سکتا ہے، (٣) تیسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ سواری سے نیچے اترنے میں عمل کثیر نہیں ہے اسلئے بھی بناء کر سکتا ہے۔ اصول: ضعیف کی بنا قوی پر ہوسکتی ہے۔ لیکن قومی کی بناء ضعیف پر نہیں ہوسکتی ہے۔ اور زمین پر تحریمہ باندھا اور ایک رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے اب سواری پر چڑھ کر بناء کرنا چاہے تو نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسکی وجہ یہ ہے (١) جب زمین پر تحریمہ باندھا تو اس بات کا التزام کیا کہ رکوع سجدے کا اتمام کرے گا اشارے کے ساتھ نہیں اداء کرے گا ، اور قیام بھی کرے گا ، اب سواری پر سوار ہو کر بناء کرے گا تو رکوع سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا اور قیام بھی نہیں کر سکے گا تو اکمل شروع کر کے اضعف سے پورا کرنا چاہتا ہے اسلئے اضعف کی بناء اقوی پر نہیں کر سکے گا۔ (٢) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ سواری پر سوار ہوتے وقت عمل کثیر ہوگا جس سے
(632) And he may continue upon his descent, not upon his mounting. Commentary: If one started a nafl prayer while mounted, and after one rak'ah wants to dismount and continue, he may do so. But if he started the nafl on the ground and after one rak'ah wants to mount and continue, he cannot. (1) The reason is that when he bound the tahrima on the mount, he obligated himself to indicate bowing and prostration with gestures, and if possible to perform full bowing and prostration. So it is as if he bound the tahrima for both indicating and full postures. Therefore, he can pray nafl on the mount and also continue after dismounting. (2) The second reason: On the mount he will gesture for bowing and prostration and cannot stand fully, so the prayer on the mount is weak (da'if). When he dismounts, he will complete bowing and prostration and also stand, so the prayer after descent has a strong tahrima. Therefore, a weak act can be built upon a strong one. (3) The third reason: Dismounting does not involve excessive action (amal kathir). Principle: A weak act can be built upon a strong one, but a strong act cannot be built upon a weak one. If he bound the tahrima on the ground and completed one rak'ah, then wants to mount and continue, he cannot. Reason: (1) When he bound the tahrima on the ground, he committed to performing full bowing and prostration, not gestures, and also standing. If he mounts, he will gesture and cannot stand, so he started with a complete act and wants to complete with a weaker one, so a weaker act cannot be built upon a stronger one. (2) The second reason: Mounting involves excessive action.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof by analogy (qiyas) on the permissibility of continuing a nafl prayer after dismounting (building upon descent) versus the impermissibility of continuing after mounting (building upon mounting). The ruling: If one starts nafl while riding, he may dismount and continue the prayer. But if one starts nafl on the ground, he may not mount and continue. The reasoning is based on the strength of the binding (tahrima) and the principle that a weaker act can be built upon a stronger one, but not vice versa. When starting on the mount, the intention (tahrima) includes both gesturing and possibly full postures, so the prayer is considered flexible. Dismounting does not involve excessive action (amal kathir) and transitions to a stronger form (full postures). However, starting on the ground commits one to full postures; mounting would replace them with gestures, which is a weaker form, and also involves excessive action. Therefore, building upon descent is allowed, but building upon mounting is not.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrima): The opening takbir of prayer that makes certain actions prohibited; also refers to the commitment to pray in a particular manner.
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive movement that invalidates or disrupts the continuity of prayer.
بناء (bina): Continuing a prayer after an interruption or change of state, building upon the previous part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is permissible?
A) Starting nafl on ground, then mounting to continue.
B) Starting nafl on mount, then dismounting to continue.
C) Both are permissible.
D) Neither is permissible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows continuing a nafl prayer after dismounting because the weaker form (mount) can be built upon the stronger form (ground), but not vice versa.

Building (Bina') in Supererogatory Prayer When Dismounting
Establishes rule of building by dismounting in nawafil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building (bina') in supererogatory prayer when a person dismounts from a riding animal, and explain the underlying principle that the weak can be built upon the strong.

Core Idea
In nawafil, continue on the ground what began on a mount; not the reverse.

Supererogatory prayers (nawafil) have greater flexibility than obligatory prayers. One example is the rule of building (bina') when changing between riding and standing. This passage from our matn explains when such continuity is valid and when it is not, providing both the ruling and its legal reasoning (wajh). Understanding this helps distinguish the unique rules of nawafil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the two scenarios: building by dismounting is allowed; building by mounting is not allowed.
The matn says explicitly: 'he may build by descending, not by mounting.'
2
Understand the reasoning based on strength of tahrimah
The prayer started on the mount is 'weak' (gestures for ruku' and sujud, no standing), while the prayer on the ground is 'strong' (full actions). The weak can be built upon the strong, but not vice versa.
This is a key principle: al-da'if yubna 'ala al-qawiyy.
3
Analyze the additional reasons
Descending does not involve excessive movement (amal kathir), while mounting does. Also, the initial tahrimah on the ground obligates perfect performance.
Three reasons are given for each direction.
4
Consider the exception for Fajr sunnah
A narration from Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the Fajr sunnah is too emphatic to be prayed on a mount or sitting; one must descend.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; other authorities may allow it.
5
Evaluate the evidence
The hadiths quoted show general permissibility for nawafil on a mount, while the Fajr sunnah hadiths emphasize its importance, supporting the exception.
The hadiths are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في صلوة النوافل جالسا
(۶۳۲) وبنى بنزوله لا بركوبه
توجه ولم يكن رسول الله الا الله يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة . ( بخاری شریف ، باب منزل للمكتوبة ، ص ۱۷۶ نمبر ۱۰۹۷ار مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة فى السفر حیث تو جھت ،ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۶۱۸/۷۰۰) (۲) جابر بن عبد الله اخبره ان النبى الله كان يصلى التطوع وهو راكب فى غير القبلة . (بخارى شریف ، باب صلوۃ التطوع علی الدواب حيثما توجهت به، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۱۰۹۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حیث تو جھت ، ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۶۱۰/۷۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کے رخ کے خلاف نفل نماز پڑھ لے تب بھی جائز ہوگی ۔ (۳) اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ شہر سے باہر ، کیونکہ اس میں سفر کا لفظ موجود ہے۔ کان عبد الله بن عمر يصلي في السفر على راحلته اينما توجهت به یؤمى وذكر عبد الله ان النبى الا الله كان يفعله . (بخاری شریف، باب الایماء علی الدابة ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۰۹۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابۃ فی السفر ، ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۶۱۴/۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر سفر میں قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ شہر میں ایسا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : (۶۳۲) اور بنا کر سکتا ہے نیچے اتر کر نہ کہ سوار ہو کر ۔ تشریح : سوار ہو کر نفل شروع کی اب ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد نیچے اتر کر اس پر بنا کرنا چاہتا ہے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر زمین پر نفل شروع کی اور ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد سوار ہو کر اس پر بنا کر نا چاہے تو بنانہیں کرسکتا۔

اصول: ضعیف کی بنا قوی پر ہوسکتی ہے۔ لیکن قومی کی بناء ضعیف پر نہیں ہوسکتی ہے۔ اور زمین پرتحریمہ باندھا اور ایک رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے اب سواری پر چڑھ کر بناء کرنا چاہے تو نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسکی وجہ یہ ہے (۱) جب زمین ر تحریمہ باندھا تو اس بات کا التزام کیا کہ رکوع سجدے کا اتمام کرے گا اشارے کے ساتھ نہیں اداء کرے گا ، اور قیام بھی کرے گا ، اب سواری پر سوار ہو کر بناء کرے گا تو رکوع سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا اور قیام بھی نہیں کر سکے گا تو اکمل شروع کر کے اضعف سے پورا کرنا چاہتا ہے اسلئے اضعف کی بناء اقوی پر نہیں کر سکے گا۔ (۲) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ سواری پر سوار ہوتے وقت عمل کثیر ہوگا جس سے تحریمہ باطل ہونے کا خطرہ ہے اسلئے بھی زمین سے شروع کر کے سواری پر بنا نہیں کر سکتا ۔ (۳) اور تیسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ زمین پر تحریمہ باندھا تو اکمل کاتحریمہ باندھا، اضعف کا نہیں باندھا، اسلئے اکمل کا تحریمہ باندھ کر اضعف ادارہ نہیں کرسکتا اسلئے کہ اسکاتحریمہ ہی نہیں باندھا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۶۳۳) اگر چه سنت مؤکدہ ہو۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ فجر کی سنت کے لئے نیچے اترے اس لئے کہ وہ دوسری سنتوں سے موکد ہے۔
تشریح : تمام سنت موکدہ بھی نفل کے درجے میں ہیں یعنی ان کو بھی بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور سواری پر پڑھ سکتا ہے، البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ فجر کی سنت بہت مؤکدہ ہے اس لئے اس کو بیٹھ کر نہ پڑھے، اور نہ اس کو سواری پر پڑھے۔ وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت : أن رسول الله له لم يكن على شيء من النوافل أشد معاهدة منه على الركعتين قبل الصبح (ابوداود شریف ، باب رکعتی الفجر، ص۱۸۸ نمبر ۱۲۵۴) (۲) عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا تدعوهما و ان طردتكم الخيل (ابوداود شریف، باب فى تخفيفهما. اى ركعتي الفجر، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۱۲۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر کی سنت اور سنتوں سے اہم ہے اسلئے اسکو سواری سے نیچے اتر کر پڑھے
لغت : الراتبة : دن رات میں جو بارہ سنت مؤکدہ ہیں ان کو نوافل را تبہ، کہتے ہیں۔
(632) And he may build [continue] by descending, not by mounting. ... He faced and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do that in the obligatory prayer. (Bukhari, Chapter on ...) (2) Jabir ibn Abdullah informed him that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray supererogatory prayers while riding, facing other than the qiblah. (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that if one prays supererogatory prayer facing other than the qiblah, it is permissible. (3) From this hadith it can be deduced that it is outside the city, because the word 'travel' is present in it. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar used to pray during travel on his mount facing wherever it faced, making gestures, and 'Abdullah mentioned that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do it. (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar used to pray facing other than the qiblah during travel. This means that doing so in the city is not permissible. Translation: (632) And he may build by descending, not by mounting. Explanation: He started supererogatory prayer while mounted, then after offering one rak'ah he wants to descend and build upon it; he may do so. But if he started supererogatory prayer on the ground and after one rak'ah wants to mount and build upon it, he may not build. Reasoning: (1) When he recited the tahrimah (opening takbir) while mounted, he obligated himself to perform ruku' and sujud by gesture, and if possible, he would perform them fully, so both aspects are included in the tahrimah. Therefore he may pray on the mount and then descend and build. (2) Second, on the mount he makes gestures for ruku' and sujud and cannot stand; thus the prayer on the mount is weak. When he descends, he completes ruku' and sujud and stands, so the tahrimah when descending is strong. The weak may be built upon the strong. (3) Third, descending from the mount is not a lot of action, so he may build. Principle: The weak may be built upon the strong, but the strong may not be built upon the weak. If he recited tahrimah on the ground and has prayed one rak'ah, and now wants to mount and build, he cannot. Reasons: (1) When he recited tahrimah on the ground, he committed to performing ruku' and sujud perfectly, not by gesture, and to standing. On the mount he would gesture and cannot stand, so he wants to complete a perfect start with an imperfect form, so the imperfect cannot be built upon the perfect. (2) Mounting involves a lot of action that risks invalidating the tahrimah. (3) The tahrimah on the ground is for complete prayer; he did not recite it for the imperfect form. Translation: (633) Even if it is an emphasized sunnah. And from Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) it is narrated that he should descend for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. Explanation: All emphasized sunnahs are in the category of supererogatory prayers, meaning one may pray them sitting or on a mount. However, one narration from Abu Hanifah is that the Fajr sunnah is very emphasized, so one should not pray it sitting nor on a mount. Proof: (1) In the hadith from 'A'ishah: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was not more committed to any supererogatory prayer than the two rak'ahs before Fajr.' (Abu Dawud) (2) From Abu Hurayrah: 'Do not leave them even if the horses trample you.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows the Fajr sunnah is more important than other sunnahs, so one should descend from the mount to pray it. Lexicon: al-ratibah: the twelve emphasized sunnahs during day and night are called nawafil ratibah.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule of building (bina') upon a supererogatory prayer when transitioning between riding and dismounting. The ruling: one may continue a supererogatory prayer started on a riding animal by dismounting after one rak'ah, but one may not continue a prayer started on the ground by mounting. The reasoning is based on the strength of the initial tahrimah. When praying on a mount, one gestures for ruku' and sujud and may not stand, so the prayer is considered 'weak'; when one dismounts, one performs full actions, making the subsequent part 'stronger'. The principle is that the weak can be built upon the strong, but not vice versa. The rule applies to all supererogatory prayers, even emphasized sunnahs (rawatib). However, Abu Hanifah has a narration that the Fajr sunnah is an exception due to its high emphasis; one should not pray it sitting or on a mount but should descend and pray it properly. This is supported by hadith emphasizing its importance.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Continuing a prayer after an interruption or change of state (here, from mount to ground or vice versa) without restarting.
الراتبة (al-ratibah): The twelve emphasized sunnah prayers accompanying the obligatory prayers (rawatib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah, what is the ruling on praying the sunnah of Fajr on a riding animal?
A) It is completely permissible like other nawafil.
B) One should descend from the mount to pray it due to its high emphasis.
C) It is not allowed even on the ground.
D) It is permissible only if one is traveling.

Key Takeaway
In supererogatory prayers, the Hanafi school allows building by dismounting but not by mounting, based on the principle that the weak can be built upon the strong, with a special exception for the Fajr sunnah according to one narration.

Leaning During Supererogatory Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on leaning during supererogatory prayer with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaning (ittika') during supererogatory prayer, identify the condition that changes the ruling, and apply the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Leaning in nafl prayer is only disliked if done without excuse; the Prophet's disapproval of the rope shows it is disrespectful.

This lesson examines a specific yet practical issue: is it permissible to lean on a wall, stick, or rope while performing supererogatory prayer? The Hanafi school distinguishes between a tired worshipper and one who leans unnecessarily. The ruling is based on a well-known hadith about Zaynab bint Jahsh. Understanding this ruling helps us appreciate the balance between ease and adab in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaning (ittika') during supererogatory (nafl) prayer. The ruling depends on the presence of an excuse: if tired, permissible without dislike; if not tired, makruh tanzih.
The ruling applies only to nafl, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Zaynab's rope recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari. The Prophet disapproved of the rope used for leaning, indicating that unnecessary leaning is disliked.
The hadith is a sahih ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command to untie the rope shows that leaning without a valid excuse is an act of disrespect to the prayer (isa'at al-adab). This yields the ruling of karaha.
The disapproval is explicit, not merely permissive.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school holds that leaning without excuse is makruh, some other schools may consider it permissible even without excuse, citing the general permissibility of actions in worship unless prohibited.
The ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of the hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that leaning is permissible if tired, otherwise makruh, as per the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). This balances adab with practicality.
No significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴) نفل پڑھنے والے کے لئے کسی چیز پر ٹیک لگانا جائز ہے اگر تھک گیا ہو، بغیر کراہیت کے، اور اگر بغیر کسی عذر کے ہو تو ظاہر روایت میں مکروہ ہے بے ادبی کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح : اگر تھک گیا ہو تو نفل پڑھنے والا کسی چیز پر ٹیک لگا سکتا ہے، یہ مکروہ نہیں ہے، اور اگر تھکا نہ ہواور کوئی عذر بھی نہ ہو تو ظاہر روایت میں مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ یہ نماز کے ساتھ بے ادبی ہے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے۔عن انس بن مالک قال دخل النبي عل فاذا حبل ممدود بين الساريتين فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم ما هذا الحبل ؟ قالوا هذا حبل لزينب فاذا فترت تعلقت فقال النبي عل : لا ، حلوه ليصل احدكم نشاطه فاذا فتر فلیقعد. (بخاری شریف، باب ما يكره من التشديد في العبادة ، ص ۱۸۴ نمبر ۱۱۵۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت زینب ٹیک لگا کر نفل پڑھا کرتیں تھیں، اور اسی حدیث میں حضور اس طرح کرنے سے کراہیت کا اظہار فرمایا ہے۔ لغت : متطوع نفل پڑھنے والا ۔ اتکاء: ٹیک لگانا۔ تعب : ٹھک جانا۔ اسائنۃ الادب: بے ادبی ہونا۔
Translation: (634) It is permissible for the one praying supererogatory prayer to lean on something if he is tired, without dislike; and if it is without excuse, then in the apparent narration it is makruh (disliked) due to disrespect. Explanation: If he is tired, the one praying supererogatory prayer may lean on something; this is not makruh. If he is not tired and has no excuse, then in the apparent narration it is makruh, because it is disrespectful to the prayer. Proof: In this hadith: Anas ibn Malik said: The Prophet entered and saw a rope stretched between two pillars. He asked, 'What is this rope?' They said, 'This is Zaynab's rope; when she feels tired, she holds onto it.' The Prophet said, 'No, untie it. Let each of you pray with energy, and when tired, let him sit down.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Dislike of Stringency in Worship) In this hadith, Zaynab used to lean while praying supererogatory prayers, and the Prophet expressed dislike for this action. Lexicon: mutatawwi': one performing supererogatory prayer. ittika': leaning. ta'b: becoming tired. isa'at al-adab: being disrespectful.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on leaning (ittika') during supererogatory prayer. The general rule: leaning on something during nafl prayer is permissible if one is tired, and there is no karahah (dislike). However, if there is no excuse (tiredness or other valid reason), then in the apparent narration of the school (zahir al-riwayah), it is makruh (disliked) because it shows disrespect to the prayer. The proof is the hadith of Zaynab bint Jahsh, who used to tie a rope to lean on when tired during prayer. The Prophet (peace be upon him) disapproved and ordered the rope to be removed, instructing that one should pray with vigor and sit when tired instead of leaning. This indicates that leaning without a valid excuse is discouraged. The ruling applies only to supererogatory prayers; for obligatory prayers, leaning is generally not allowed unless for a serious excuse.

Key Terms
اتكاء (ittika'): Leaning on something (e.g., a wall, stick, rope) for support during prayer.
متطوع (mutatawwi'): One who performs supererogatory (nafl) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaning during supererogatory prayer if the person is not tired?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is makruh (disliked) due to disrespect.
C) It is haram because it invalidates the prayer.
D) It is wajib to avoid leaning.

Key Takeaway
Leaning during supererogatory prayer is permissible if tired; otherwise it is disliked (makruh tanzih) due to disrespect.

Praying the Fajr Sunnah: Emphasized Nafl Requires Descending
Ruling on Fajr sunnah's exceptional posture requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying the Fajr sunnah while sitting or on a riding animal, identify the evidence from hadith, and explain the intra-madhhab difference regarding its performance.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is so emphasized that one should descend to pray it on the ground, unlike other nafl.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling regarding the regular sunnah prayers (nawafil ratibah). While the general rule allows praying sunan mu'akkadah while sitting or on a riding animal, Imam Abu Hanifa transmits a unique view concerning the Fajr sunnah. Based on hadith evidence showing the Prophet's exceptional commitment to this prayer, Abu Hanifa holds that one should dismount and pray it on the ground, highlighting its elevated status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Recognize that sunan mu'akkadah are at the level of nafl and can be performed while sitting or on a riding animal.
This is the default position in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the exception for Fajr sunnah
According to a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, one should descend for the Fajr sunnah because it is more emphasized than other sunan.
This exception is based on specific evidence.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadiths are cited: Aisha's report on the Prophet's intense commitment to the two rak'ahs before Fajr, and the command not to leave them even if horses trample.
These hadiths are from Abu Dawud.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's exceptional commitment and the explicit command indicate that the Fajr sunnah holds a special rank, warranting performance in the most complete manner (on the ground).
This reasoning supports Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other Hanafi scholars may allow praying the Fajr sunnah while sitting or on a mount, but Abu Hanifa's view is presented as the relied-upon position due to the strength of the evidence.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate within the school.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۶۳۳) اگر چه سنت مؤكده ہو۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ فجر کی سنت کے لئے نیچے اترے اس لئے کہ وہ دوسری سنتوں سے موکد ہے۔

لغت : الراتبة : دن رات میں جو بارہ سنت مؤکدہ ہیں ان کو نوافل را تبہ، کہتے ہیں۔
Regarding praying voluntary prayers while sitting. (633) And even if it is among the regular nawafil (rawatib), and from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that he descends for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. Translation (633): Even if it is sunnah mu'akkadah. And from Imam Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he descends for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than other sunan. Commentary: All sunan mu'akkadah are of the level of nafl, meaning they can be prayed sitting, and can be prayed on a riding animal. However, there is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the sunnah of Fajr is very emphasized, so one should not pray it sitting, nor on a riding animal. Evidence (1): From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was not more committed to any of the nawafil than the two rak'ahs before Fajr. (Abu Dawud, chapter on their lightness, i.e., the two rak'ahs of Fajr, p.188, no.1258) This hadith shows that the sunnah of Fajr is more important than other sunan, so one should descend from the riding animal to pray it. This is a ruling from the section on praying nafl prayers while sitting. The commentary explains that all sunan mu'akkadah are at the level of nafl in terms of flexibility, but for Fajr sunnah, due to its emphasis, it is better to pray it on the ground. Two hadiths are cited: one from Aisha showing the Prophet's commitment to Fajr sunnah, and another from Abu Hurairah emphasizing not to leave them even in dire situations. This shows the exceptional status of Fajr sunnah within the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah holds a special emphasis that requires one to descend and pray on the ground, unlike other sunan mu'akkadah.

Leaning During Nafl Prayer: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on leaning while praying optional prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaning during nafl prayer and distinguish between the cases with and without an excuse.

Core Idea
Leaning during nafl is makruh without excuse, but permissible if tired.

This passage addresses a common question about posture during optional prayers. While some might think that any support invalidates the prayer, the Hanafi school distinguishes based on necessity. The key is whether the worshipper is genuinely tired.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaning (ittika') on something during nafl prayer. The ruling depends on the presence of an excuse (tiredness).
2
Understand the two scenarios
Scenario 1: The person is tired – leaning is permissible without dislike. Scenario 2: No excuse – leaning is makruh (disliked) in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah).
3
Examine the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Zaynab (radiallahu anha) who used a rope for support while praying. The Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) ordered the rope to be removed, indicating dislike for such support without necessity.
Bukhari, hadith 1150
4
Note the authority level
The text refers to 'al-azhar' (most apparent) and 'zahir al-riwayah', indicating this is the preferred view within the Hanafi school.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah

Impurity on Riding Animal During Nafl Prayer
Ruling on impurity on the riding animal during nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on impurity on a riding animal during nafl prayer and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Impurity on a riding animal does not invalidate nafl prayer — it is excused by the Prophet's practice.

When praying on a mount, some impurity from the animal is almost unavoidable. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet, holds that such impurity is pardoned for voluntary prayers. This passage clarifies that impurity on the animal, saddle, or stirrups does not affect the validity of nafl prayer, providing ease for the traveler.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act in question? (Prayer on a riding animal) And what is the ruling? (It is valid despite the presence of impurity on the animal, saddle, or stirrups).
The ruling is stated explicitly: 'ولا يمنع صحة الصلوة على الدابة نجاسة عليها'.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet used to pray voluntary prayers while riding. This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove that impurity is excused? The Prophet's habitual practice of praying while riding implies that any impurities on the animal were naturally present and overlooked.
The commentary adds that since animals inevitably have urine and dung, such impurities are pardoned.
4
Note the istithna' (exception) and ikhtilaf
The text says 'على الاصح' (on the more correct view), indicating that there is a weaker opposing opinion within the Hanafi school that holds impurity invalidates.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that it does not affect validity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the correct view, the prayer is valid without any need to clean the impurity, providing ease for the traveler.
This ruling applies specifically to nafl prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۳۵ ولا يمنع صحة الصلوة على الدابة نجاسة عليها ولو كانت في السرج والركابين على الاصح
ترجمه : (۶۳۵) نماز صحیح ہونے کو نجاست نہیں روکتی چاہے، چوپائے پر ہو، یا زین پر ہو، یارکاب پر ہو سیج روایت میں ۔ تشريح : چوپائے پر نجاست ہو یا زین پر نجاست ہو، یا رکاب پر نجاست ہو پھر بھی اس چوپائے پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ حدیث کی بنا پر اتنی نجاست معاف ہے۔ وجه : (۱) جب جانور پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے تو یقینی بات ہے کہ جانور پیشاب پیخانہ کیا ہوگا، اور بہت ممکن ہے کہ اس کا پیشاب پیخانہ زین اور رکاب کو بھی لگا ہوگا، اس لئے اس کے باوجود اس پر نماز جائز ہے۔ (۲) حدیث یہ ہے۔ جابر بن عبد الله اخبره ان النبي كان يصلي التطوع وهو راكب في غير القبلة . (بخاری شریف، باب صلوۃ التطوع على الدواب حيثما تو جهت به ،ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۴ر مسلم شریف، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حیث تو جھت ،ص۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۶۱۰/۷۰۰)
لغت دابتہ جانور، چوپایہ۔ سرج: زین۔ رکابین رکاب کی تشنہ ہے رکاب، سوار جس پر پاؤں رکھتا ہے۔
(635) And impurity on the riding animal does not prevent the validity of the prayer, even if it is on the saddle or the stirrups, according to the more correct view. Translation: Impurity does not prevent the prayer from being valid, whether it is on the animal, on the saddle, or on the stirrups, in the sound narration. Commentary: If there is impurity on the animal or saddle or stirrups, praying on that animal is still permissible, because based on hadith, such impurity is excused. Evidence: (1) Since praying on the animal is permissible, it is certain that the animal has urine and dung, and it is highly possible that its urine and dung have reached the saddle and stirrups; despite that, prayer on it is permissible. (2) The hadith is: Jabir ibn Abdullah informed him that the Prophet used to pray the voluntary prayer while riding, facing a direction other than the qiblah. (Bukhari, chapter on voluntary prayer on animals facing any direction, p.148 no.1094; Muslim, chapter on permissibility of nafl prayer on a riding animal during travel facing any direction, p.244 no.1610/700) Lexicon: dabbah: animal, riding beast. sarj: saddle. rikabayn: dual of rikab, stirrup, where the rider places his feet.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of impurity on the riding animal during prayer. The ruling: impurity on the animal, saddle, or stirrups does not invalidate the prayer; it is excused. The commentary explains that since it is permissible to pray on the animal, and animals naturally have impurities, such impurities are overlooked. The proof is the hadith that the Prophet prayed voluntary prayers while riding, which implies the presence of impurities. This shows that in nafl prayer on a mount, minor impurities are excused.

Key Terms
دابة (dabbah): A riding animal, such as a horse, camel, etc.
سرج (sarj): Saddle, the seat placed on the animal's back.
ركاب (rikab): Stirrup, the footrest attached to the saddle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It makes the prayer makruh.
D) It requires making up the prayer later.

Key Takeaway
Impurity on a riding animal's saddle or stirrups does not invalidate nafl prayer and is excused by the Prophet's practice.

The Invalidity of Walking Prayer in the Hanafi School
Ruling on validity of prayer while walking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying while walking, identify the primary evidence, and evaluate the opposing view from fear prayer hadith.

Core Idea
Walking during prayer invalidates it by consensus – standing is a fundamental pillar.

In this lesson, we examine a clear-cut Hanafi ruling: prayer performed while walking is invalid (batil) by consensus (ijma'). The passage provides a key incident from the life of the Prophet ﷺ and addresses a counter-argument from the fear prayer hadith. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the essentiality of qiyam (standing) in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: 'And the prayer of one who walks is not valid by consensus.' Identify the act (prayer while walking) and the hukm level (batil) as explicitly stated.
2
Examine the Primary Evidence
Analyze the hadith of Jabir about the Battle of the Trench. Note how the Prophet and Umar did not pray while walking but made up the prayer later. This shows that walking prayer is not acceptable in normal circumstances.
3
Consider the Opposing Evidence
The passage mentions that some scholars use the fear prayer hadith (pray standing or riding) to permit walking prayer. Understand the basis of their argument.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
Although the passage does not explicitly refute the opposing hadith, the Hanafi position (implied by 'consensus') prioritizes the explicit prohibition from the Trench incident. Recognize that fear prayer has special concessions not applicable to general prayer.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, this means a person who walks even a few steps during fard prayer without an excuse (e.g., walking to align rows) may invalidate the prayer if it disrupts the required continuity and standing.
Walking for a necessary purpose, like moving forward to fill a gap, is often overlooked if done minimally, but deliberate walking nullifies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۳۶) ولا تصح صلوة الماشي بالاجماع.
ترجمه : (۶۳۶) اور چلتے چلتے نماز پڑھنا صیح نہیں ہے بالا جماع ۔
تشریح چلتے چلتے نماز پڑھنا درست نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (ا) عن جابر بن عبد الله قال جاء عمر يوم الخندق فجعل يسب كفار قريش و يقول يا رسول الله ، ما صليت العصر حتى كادت الشمس ان يغيب فقال النبى و انا و الله ما صليتها بعد قال فنزل الى بطحان فتوضاء و صلى العصر بعد ما غابت الشمس ثم صلى المغرب بعدها ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلاۃ عند مناهضة الحصون ولقاء العدو، ص ۱۵۲، نمبر ۹۴۵) اس حدیث میں چلتے ہوئے نماز نہیں پڑھی، بلکہ قضاء کی ۔ (۲) بعض حضرات کے یہاں چلتے چلتے نماز جائز ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ ابن عمر عن النبی و ان كانوا اكثر من ذالك فليصلوا قیامـا و ركبانا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة الخوف رجالا ور كہانا ص ۱۵۱ نمبر ۹۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پیدل چلتے ہوئے نماز پڑھے۔
(636) And the prayer of one who walks is not valid by consensus. Translation: And praying while walking is not valid by consensus. Commentary: Praying while walking is not correct. Evidence: (1) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: Umar came on the day of Khandaq, cursing the disbelievers of Quraish, and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have not prayed Asr until the sun almost set.' The Prophet said, 'By Allah, I have not prayed it either.' So he descended to Bathan, performed wudu, and prayed Asr after the sun set, then prayed Maghrib after it. (Bukhari, chapter on prayer at the time of besieging forts and meeting the enemy, p.152, no.945) In this hadith, they did not pray while walking but made it up later. (2) Some scholars hold that praying while walking is permissible, their evidence being the hadith: Ibn Umar from the Prophet: 'And if they are more than that, then let them pray standing or riding.' (Bukhari, chapter on fear prayer on foot and mounted, p.151, no.943) This hadith indicates praying while walking on foot.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that praying while walking (i.e., without standing still) is invalid by consensus (ijma'). The commentary mentions two proofs: first, the incident during the Battle of the Trench where Umar and the Prophet missed Asr and did not pray while walking but made it up later, showing that walking prayer is not acceptable. Second, some scholars use the fear prayer hadith to argue for permissibility, but the Hanafi position (as implied by the text) is that walking prayer is not valid for regular prayers, though the evidence from the fear prayer hadith is addressed. The text states 'by consensus' (bil ijma'), indicating it is a settled ruling.

Key Terms
الماشي (al-mashi): One who walks; here meaning one who performs prayer while walking without standing still.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Battle of the Trench hadith
C) Consensus of the Hanafi school
