Key Takeaway
Praying while walking is invalid (batil) by consensus in the Hanafi school; the key evidence is that the Prophet did not do so even when he missed Asr during battle, and the fear prayer hadith is a special concession.

Fard and Wajib Prayers Not Valid on a Riding Animal
Clear ruling on obligatory prayers on a riding animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school rules fard and wajib prayers as invalid on a riding animal and identify which prayers fall under this ruling (fard, witr, nadhr, and a broken nafl).

Core Idea
Obligatory prayers (fard/wajib) cannot be performed on a mount — only nafl is permitted.

We have learned that nafl prayers are permissible on a riding animal. But what about the obligatory prayers? This lesson presents the clear Hanafi ruling: fard and wajib prayers, including witr and vowed prayers, are not valid on a mount. Understanding this distinction is essential for a Muslim who may be traveling or in a situation where he cannot dismount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Praying fard or wajib on a riding animal. The ruling: it is not valid (batil).
The text explicitly says 'لا يصح' meaning it is not valid.
2
Distinguish from nafl
Why are fard and wajib different from nafl? Because they require conditions like standing still, facing qiblah, and stability, which cannot be fulfilled on a moving mount.
Earlier lessons established nafl is valid on a mount; this lesson shows the exception.
3
List the included prayers
The text explicitly includes: fard prayers, witr, nadhr (vowed prayers), and even a nafl prayer that one started and then invalidated (breaking it makes it wajib to make up).
The broken nafl is treated as wajib because completing it becomes obligatory.

The commentary begins but is cut off. This contrasts with the earlier ruling that nafl prayers are permitted on a riding animal. The key point is that obligatory prayers require standing and other conditions that cannot be fulfilled on a mount without disruption, so they are not valid.

Fard and Wajib Prayers Not Valid on Animal Unless Necessity
General rule that obligatory prayers are invalid on animals, with exception for dire necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on obligatory prayers on an animal and identify the exceptions for necessity.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayers on an animal are invalid unless dire necessity exists.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling concerning the validity of fard and wajib prayers when performed on a riding animal. The general rule is clear: such prayers are not valid. However, the school recognizes a narrow exception for genuine necessity. Through the source text, we will explore the evidence from the Sunnah and the practical examples that define this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of performing fard and wajib prayers on an animal. The ruling: it is invalid (batil) without necessity.
The author lists specific examples including witr, nadhr, funeral prayer, and sajdah tilawah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah, which describes the Prophet (peace be upon him) not performing prescribed prayer while riding.
Also the practice of Ibn 'Umar for witr.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's omission of prescribed prayer while riding indicates that such prayers are not to be performed on animals. The absence of evidence becomes evidence.
Hanafi usul: an action not done by the Prophet can indicate prohibition if he had the opportunity to do it.
4
Note the exception
The ruling is overridden by necessity (darurah), such as fear of a thief, predator, or muddy ground.
The source lists five specific excused conditions.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
Consider the five examples: witr, nadhr, broken nafl, funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah. All are either fard or have the force of wajib, so they fall under the prohibition except in necessity.
Nafl prayers are allowed without necessity.

دیار ہو، اور نماز جنازہ جانور پر جائز نہیں ، اور وہ سجدہ جسکی آیت زمین پر تلاوت کی گئی ہے۔ تشریح : نفلی نماز اور سنت نمازیں بغیر کسی عذر کے جانور پر پڑھنا جائز ہے لیکن جونمازیں فرض ہیں، یا واجب ہیں، یا اس کا حکم واجب کے درجے میں ہے اس کو مجبوری کے بغیر سواری پر پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مصنف نے اس کی پانچ مثالیں دی ہیں [1] وتر کی نماز واجب ہے اس لئے اس کو جانور پر نہیں پڑھ سکتا ۔ [۲] نذر کی نماز واجب ہے اس لئے اس کو سواری پر نہیں پڑھ سکتا۔[۳] نفل کو شروع کیا پھر اس کو توڑ دیا تو اس کو ادا کرنا واجب ہو گیا، اس لئے اس کو سواری پر ادا نہیں کر سکتا ۔ [۴] نماز جنازہ فرض کفایہ ہے اس لئے اس کو سواری پر ادا نہیں کرے گا۔ [۵] جو سجدہ کی آیت زمین پر تلاوت کی اس کو زمین پر اکمل طریقے پر ادا کرناواجب ہے اس لئے سواری پر اس کا سجدہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔

علوس
على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله لم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة . (بخاری شریف ، باب ينزل المكتوبة ، ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۷ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث تو جهت ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۸/۷۰۰) (۲) ان ابن عمر كان اذا اراد ان يوتر نزل عن راحلته فاوتر بالارض (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الوتر علی الدابة ، ج ثانی ص ۳۸۲، نمبر ۴۵۵۳) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ وتر زمین پر پڑھے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۸) مگرضرورت کی بنا پر [ جانور پر فرض اور واجب پڑھ سکتا ہے جیسے نیچے اترنے میں اپنی ذات ، یا چوپائے ، یا کپڑے پر چور کا خوف ہو ۔ اور پھاڑ کھانے والے کا خوف ہو، اور مکان کیچڑ والا ہو اور چوپایہ سرکش ہو اور عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے کوئی ایسا نہ ہو جو اس پر سوار کر دے۔
تشریح : اگر مجبوری ہو تو فرض نماز اور واجب نماز جانور پر پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ آگے مصنف نے مجبوری کی یہ قسمیں بیان کی ہیں۔ [1] جیسے نیچے اترنے میں اپنی ذات پر، یا چوپائے پر، یا کپڑے پر چور کا خطرہ ہو کہ وہ چرالے گا۔[۲] یا پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کا خطرہ ہو کہ نیچے اتر گا تو جانور پھاڑ ڈالے گا۔ (۳) یا جگہ کیچڑ والی ہو کہ اس میں اترنا ناممکن ہو [۴] یا جانور سرکش ہوا گراتر اتو اس پر سوار ہونا نا ممکن ہے، and کوئی دوسرا آدمی بھی نہیں ہے کہ اس پر سوار کر دے، تو ایسی صورت میں آدمی کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ جانور پر ہی فرض اور واجب نماز پڑھ لے۔ اور رکوع اور سجدے کا اشارہ کرے۔
وجه : (1) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال لا يصلى الرجل المكتوبة على الدابة مقبلا الى البيت و لا
Chapter: On fard and wajib prayer on the animal. (137): Prayer of fard and wajib prayers like witr and nadhr and what was begun as nafl then spoiled, and the funeral prayer, and the prostration whose verse was recited on the ground (638), are not valid on the animal, except for necessity like fear of a thief for himself or his animal or his clothes if he descends, fear of a beast, muddy place, the animal being unruly, and not finding someone to mount him. Explanation: Voluntary and sunnah prayers are allowed on an animal without excuse, but prayers that are fard or wajib or have the ruling of wajib are not allowed without necessity. The author gave five examples: [1] witr is wajib, so cannot be prayed on animal. [2] nadhr is wajib. [3] if one begins nafl then breaks it, its makeup becomes wajib. [4] funeral prayer is fard kifaya. [5] prostration for a verse recited on the ground has to be performed on the ground. Evidence: (1) Hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah: he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) on his camel glorifying (tasbeeh) and nodding his head, and he did not do that in the prescribed prayer. (Bukhari, 1097; Muslim, 1618/700) (2) Ibn 'Umar, when he wanted to pray witr, would dismount and pray on the ground (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, 4553). Translation: (138) But due to necessity, it is permissible to pray fard and wajib on the animal, such as fear of a thief for his life, or his animal, or his clothes, fear of a predator, muddy place, the animal being unruly, and inability to find someone to mount him. Explanation: If there is a necessity, one can pray fard and wajib on the animal. The author mentions the types of necessity: [1] fear of theft of self, animal, or clothes. [2] fear of being attacked by a predator. [3] the place is muddy. [4] the animal is unruly and no one can help him mount. Then it is allowed to pray on the animal, making gestures for ruku and sajdah. Evidence from the saying of a tabi‘i: 'Ata said: A man should not pray the obligatory prayer on an animal facing the house (Kaaba) and nor...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of obligatory prayers on a riding animal. The basic rule is that fard and wajib prayers cannot be performed on an animal; this includes witr, nadhr, the makeup of a broken nafl, funeral prayer, and sajdah tilawah when the verse was recited on land. The proof is from the hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah where the Prophet did not perform the prescribed prayer while riding. Additionally, the practice of Ibn 'Umar for witr. The exception is for dire necessity: fear of a thief, a predator, muddy ground, an unruly animal, or inability to find help to mount. In such cases, one may pray on the animal with gestures. The commentary lists five cases of necessity. The legal principle is that necessity overrides the general prohibition.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that must be performed; prayer on an animal is invalid unless necessary.
الوتر (al-witr): The witr prayer, considered wajib in Hanafi school; cannot be performed on animal without necessity.
المنذور (al-mundhūr): A prayer vowed (nadhr) by a person, which becomes wajib to fulfill.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that overrides the prohibition; examples: fear of thief, predator, muddy ground, unruly animal, inability to find help.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head for ruku and sujud when unable to perform them physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a valid necessity for performing fard prayer on an animal?
A) Fear of a thief for one's property.
B) The animal is unruly and no one can help mount it.
C) The traveler is tired and wishes to remain seated.
D) The ground is muddy making it difficult to perform sujud.

Key Takeaway
Hal: obligatory prayers are invalid on animals unless a specific dire necessity exists, in which case gestures suffice.

Ruling on Obligatory Prayers on an Animal with Exception for Necessity
States the general prohibition and exception of fard/wajib prayers on animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general prohibition of performing fard/wajib prayers on an animal, identify the valid exceptions of necessity, and explain the evidence from the hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah and other narrations.

Core Idea
Performing obligatory prayers on an animal is prohibited without a genuine necessity.

This passage addresses a practical travel scenario: can you pray your obligatory prayer (fard or wajib) while riding an animal? The general rule is that it is not allowed, because the proper pillars of prayer (standing, bowing, prostrating) cannot be fulfilled. However, Islam recognizes real-life hardship and provides an exception for genuine necessity (darurah). The text lists specific examples of necessity and provides the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
The act is performing obligatory prayers (fard, including funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah) on an animal/donkey/camel. The general ruling is prohibition (haram) because the Prophet did not do it and the pillars are compromised.
The text says: 'ولا صلوة الجنازة وسجدة تليت آيتها على الارض الا لضرورة' meaning no funeral prayer or prostration of recitation on the animal except for necessity.
2
List the exceptions (necessity cases)
The text gives five examples: fear of a thief for oneself, one's animal, or one's clothes if dismounting; fear of a wild beast; a muddy place; an unruly animal; not finding someone to help one mount.
These are all scenarios where dismounting would cause genuine harm or difficulty.
3
Examine the primary evidence
The hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah states the Prophet did not perform obligatory prayer on a mount, only supererogatory. This implies prohibition for obligatory prayers.
The Arabic phrase 'لم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة' is key.
4
Analyze supporting narrations
Ibn 'Umar dismounted to pray witr on the ground, showing witr (considered wajib) is not automatically allowed on the mount. However, another hadith shows the Prophet prayed witr on his mount, indicating witr has special leniency.
This nuance distinguishes witr from other obligatory prayers in certain contexts.
5
Apply the ruling: exception vs. witr
The exception applies to all fard/wajib prayers when necessity is present. Additionally, witr is allowed on a mount even without necessity, as per the Prophet's practice.
This is a specific ruling for witr within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلوة الفرض على الدابة. ولا صلوة الجنازة وسجدة تليت آيتها على الارض (۶۳۸) الا لضرورة كخوف لص على نفسه او دابته او ثيابـه لـو نـزل وخوف سبع و طين المكان وجموح الدابة وعدم وجدان من يُركبه

وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض سواری پر پڑھنا جائز نہیں۔ عامر بن ربيعة اخبره قال رأيت النبي الله وهو [صلى الله] [علوس] على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله لم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة . (بخاری شریف ، باب ينزل المكتوبة ، ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۷ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث تو جهت ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۸/۷۰۰) (۲) ان ابن عمر كان اذا اراد ان يوتر نزل عن راحلته فاوتر بالارض (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الوتر علی الدابة ، ج ثانی ص ۳۸۲، نمبر ۴۵۵۳)

عن عطاء قال لا يصلى الرجل المكتوبة على الدابة مقبلا الى البيت و لا لعجزه. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل يصلى المكتوبة على الدابة ، الخ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۷۷، نمبر ۴۵۲۰) (۲) عن عطاء قال ان كان انسان في ماء لا يستطيع ان يخرج منه فليصل و ليوميء برأسه ايماء ولا يسجد - (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل يصلى المكتوبة على الدابة ، الخ ج ثانی ،ص ۱۳۷۸، نمبر ۴۵۲۷) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ مجبوری ہو تو جانور پر فرض نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔(۳) وتر جانور پر پڑھے اس کے لئے پوری گنجائش ہے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر انه قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوتر على راحلته - (مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حیث تو جھت ،ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۷/۷۰۰ رابوداود شریف، باب التطوع على الراحلة والوتر ص ۱۸۲، نمبر (۱۲۲۴)
The prayer of the obligatory upon the animal. And no funeral prayer and the prostration of a verse recited on the ground except for necessity, like fear of a thief for himself, his animal, or his clothes if he descends, and fear of a wild beast, and the muddiness of the place, and the animal's being unruly, and not finding someone to mount him. Evidence: (1) This hadith states that obligatory prayer on a mount is not permissible. 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah informed him: He said, 'I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, on a mount, glorifying, nodding his head, facing any direction, and the Messenger of Allah did not do that in the obligatory prayer.' (Bukhari, chapter 'Descending for Obligatory Prayer', p. 148 no. 1097?; Muslim, chapter 'Permissibility of Supererogatory Prayer on an Animal while Traveling, Facing whichever Direction', p. 285 no. 1618/700) (2) Ibn 'Umar, when he wanted to pray witr, would descend from his mount and pray witr on the ground. ('Abd al-Razzaq's Musannaf, chapter 'Witr on an Animal', vol. 2 p. 382 no. 4553) 'Ata said: A man should not pray the obligatory prayer on an animal facing the House nor due to his inability. ('Abd al-Razzaq's Musannaf, chapter 'Is the obligatory prayer prayed on an animal?', vol. 2 p. 1377 no. 4520) (2) 'Ata said: If a person is in water and cannot get out, he should pray and indicate with his head, and not prostrate. ('Abd al-Razzaq's Musannaf, chapter 'Is the obligatory prayer prayed on an animal?', vol. 2 p. 1378 no. 4527) This statement of a tabi'i indicates that if there is compulsion, one can pray obligatory prayer on an animal. (3) For witr on an animal, there is full scope. For this, this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah used to pray witr on his mount. (Muslim, chapter 'Permissibility of Supererogatory Prayer on an Animal while Traveling, Facing whichever Direction', p. 285 no. 1617/700; Abu Dawud, chapter 'Supererogatory Prayer on a Mount and Witr', p. 182 no. 1224)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) on performing obligatory prayers on an animal. The author first states the general rule: no obligatory prayer (fard or wajib) may be performed on an animal. This includes funeral prayer (which is fard kifayah) and the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) when the verse is recited on the ground. These are all obligatory and require standing, bowing, and prostrating properly on the ground. However, an exception is made for necessity (darurah). The examples of necessity given are: fear of a thief for one's life, animal, or clothes if one dismounts; fear of a wild beast; a muddy place; an unruly animal; and not finding someone to help mount. In such cases, one may perform the obligatory prayer on the animal, indicating the movements with the head. The author then provides evidence: a hadith from 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not perform obligatory prayer on a mount, only supererogatory; and a narration of Ibn 'Umar that he dismounted to pray witr on the ground. Further evidence from 'Ata states that obligatory prayer is not prayed on an animal facing the qiblah nor due to inability, but another narration from 'Ata allows it if trapped in water. Finally, a hadith shows the Prophet prayed witr on his mount, indicating witr is allowed on a mount because it is not like fard (it is wajib but with some leniency).

Key Terms
فرض (fard): Obligatory act proven by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah). In this context, it refers to the daily prayers and funeral prayer.
ضرورة (darurah): A dire necessity that makes the prohibited permissible, such as fear of harm to life or property.
لص (liss): Thief; a person who steals, causing fear if one dismounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid necessity for performing obligatory prayer on an animal?
A) Fear of a thief for one's clothes
B) Fear of a wild beast
C) The animal is gentle and one prefers not to dismount
D) The place is muddy

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayers on an animal are prohibited except in genuine necessity, but witr is allowed based on Prophetic practice.

Prayer in a Howdah: Same Ruling as on the Animal
States equivalence of prayer in a howdah and on an animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on prayer in a howdah and identify why it shares the same status as prayer on the animal itself.

Core Idea
Prayer in a howdah is legally identical to prayer on the animal.

This short passage from Thamarat al-Najah clarifies a specific scenario: performing salah while seated in a howdah (a wooden carriage on a camel). The ruling is straightforward: whatever applies to praying directly on the animal also applies when using a howdah, whether the animal is moving or standing still. This eliminates any confusion about the howdah being considered separate from the animal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۳۹) والـصـلـوـة فـي الـمـحمل على الدابة كالصلوة عليها سواء كانت سائرة او واقفة
(639) And the prayer in the howdah on the animal is like the prayer on it, whether it is moving or stationary.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that equates the legal status of prayer performed inside a howdah (a conveyance placed on an animal) with prayer performed directly on the animal's back. The ruling applies regardless of whether the animal is in motion or at rest. The implication is that obligatory prayers (fard/wajib) are not valid in a howdah without necessity, just as they are not valid on an animal proper, due to the inability to perform the pillars (standing, bowing, prostration) properly. The howdah does not change the ruling because the person is still elevated and unable to perform the acts completely.

Key Terms
محمل (mahmil): A howdah; a wooden structure placed on an animal (camel) for a person to sit in, often used in travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, are obligatory prayers valid in a howdah when the animal is stationary (not moving)?
A) Yes, because the animal is stationary so it is like ground
B) No, because the ruling is the same as on the animal itself regardless of movement
C) Yes, but only for supererogatory prayers
D) It depends on the person's intention

Key Takeaway
Prayer in a howdah shares the exact same ruling as prayer on the animal itself — invalid for fard without necessity, valid for nafl by gesture.

Ruling on Praying in a Howdah When Stabilized
States the ruling on praying in a howdah when stabilized by a board.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on praying in a howdah when it is stabilized to the ground and identify the exceptions for sickness or fear.

Core Idea
A howdah stabilized by a board is legally like ground for obligatory prayer, except for the sick or fearful.

In this passage, the author extends the ruling on praying in a howdah. Previously, praying in a moving howdah had certain leniencies. Here, if the howdah is made stable by placing a board underneath so that it rests on the ground, it is treated as ground itself. This means obligatory prayers become valid because the worshipper can stand and perform the pillars properly. However, exemptions remain for those who are sick or fearful, allowing them to pray on the animal facing the qiblah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying obligatory prayer in a howdah (a camel litter). The ruling depends on whether the howdah is stabilized.
2
State the condition for treating the howdah like ground
A board must be placed under the howdah so that its base reaches the ground (حتى بقى قراره الى الارض). This makes it stable like a platform.
The board must fully support the howdah; partial support does not suffice.
3
Derive the consequence
Because the howdah is now like ground, obligatory prayer is valid. The worshipper must face the qiblah and perform the pillars standing.
The phrase 'مدبرا عنه' likely means one must not turn away from qiblah.
4
Note the exception
If the person is sick or fearful (e.g., of a wild animal), they may pray on the animal facing the House (qiblah) without dismounting.
This exception preserves the original concession for ease.
5
Understand the scope
This ruling expands on previous rules for prayer on animals. The key factor is stability; the howdah becomes like stationary ground.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۴۰) ولو جـعـل تـحـت الـمـحـمـل خشبة حتى بقى قراره الى الارض كان بمنزلة الارض فتصح مدبرا عنه الا ان يكون مريضا او خائفا فليصل على دابته مقبلا الى البيت غير مدبر عنه
(640) And if a board is placed under the howdah so that its base reaches the ground, it is in the status of the ground, so [obligatory] prayer is valid turning away from it [i.e., not facing qiblah?]? except if one is sick or fearful, then he should pray on his animal facing the House, not turning away from it.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage elaborates on an exception to the previous ruling: if a howdah is made stable by putting a board underneath so that it rests firmly on the ground (like a platform), then it is treated as ground itself. Therefore, obligatory prayers become valid because the person can stand and perform the pillars properly. However, if the person is sick or fears something (e.g., a wild animal), then they may still pray on the animal (i.e., without dismounting) facing the qiblah (the House), without turning away from it. The note about 'turning away from it' (مدبرا عنه) likely means if the howdah is like ground, one must face the qiblah, but in necessity, one may face whatever direction the animal faces. The commentary explains that if one can stand and perform ruku' and sujud properly, then it is like ground; if not, it remains like a howdah.

Key Terms
خشبة (khashabah): A piece of wood; a board placed under the howdah to stabilize it.
قرار (qarar): Base, resting place; the part of the howdah that touches the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The howdah must be made of wood
B) A board must be placed under it so that its base rests on the ground
C) The animal must be standing still
D) The person must be unable to stand

Key Takeaway
A howdah stabilized by a board so its base reaches the ground is treated as ground for obligatory prayer; the sick or fearful may pray on the animal facing qiblah.

Prayer on a Riding Animal and Howdah: Conditions and Proof
Ruling on obligatory prayer on animal and howdah with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which obligatory prayer on a riding animal or in a howdah is valid according to the Hanafi school, and apply the rule that if the howdah is stabilized by touching the ground, it takes the ruling of ground, provided one can perform the essential actions of prayer.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on an animal is valid only when dismounting is impossible; ability to stand, bow, and prostrate determines the ruling.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling on performing obligatory prayer while riding an animal or sitting in a howdah. It establishes that while the default is to pray on the ground, necessity permits praying on a mount, but only if the rider cannot dismount due to illness or fear. The text further explains that a howdah takes the same ruling as the animal unless it is stabilized by a plank touching the ground, in which case it is treated like the ground itself, allowing standing prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing the obligatory prayer (fard) while on a riding animal. According to the Hanafi school, this is permissible when one is unable to dismount due to illness or fear, or when performance on the ground is impossible.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray witr on his mount. This is taken as evidence for permissibility of wajib prayers on riding animals.
Witr is considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the condition for validity
The passage states that a howdah is like the animal: prayer in it is valid only if one cannot perform the essential actions (standing, bowing, prostrating) on the ground. If a plank is placed under the howdah so it rests on the ground, it becomes like ground, and standing prayer is valid.
The key is the ability to perform rukun al-salah.
4
Apply the principle to modern conveyances
The commentator extends the ruling to trains, cars, and airplanes. If one can perform ruku and sujud fully, fard prayers are valid. If not, and there is compulsion, gestures are acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلوة الفرض على الدابة لعجزه. (۶۳۹) والصلوة في المحمل على الدابة كالصلوة عليها سواء كانت سائرة او واقفة (۶۴۰) ولو جعل تحت المحمل خشبة حتى بقى قراره الى الارض كان بمنزلة الارض فتصح مدبرا عنه الا ان يكون مريضا او خائفا فليصل على دابته مقبلا الى البيت غير مدبر عنه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل يصلى المكتوبة على الدابة ، الخ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۷۷، نمبر ۴۵۲۰) (۲) عن عطاء قال ان كان انسان في ماء لا يستطيع ان يخرج منه فليصل و ليوميء برأسه ايماء ولا يسجد - (مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حیث تو جھت ،ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۷/۷۰۰ رابوداود شریف، باب التطوع على الراحلة والوتر ص ۱۸۲، نمبر (۱۲۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کوتر سواری پر پڑھتے تھے۔ نوٹ آج کل ریل موٹر اور ہوائی جہاز پر نماز پڑھنے کا اتفاق ہوتا ہے، اگر وہاں رکوع سجدہ کر سکتا ہے تو فرض وغیرہ بھی اس پر جائز ہے، اور رکوع سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا ہے اور مجبوری ہے تو اشارہ سے نماز پڑھ لے اور مجبوری نہیں ہے تو نماز بعد میں پڑھے دلیل گزر چکی ہے لغت : لص : چور دابتہ : چوپایہ، جانور ، سواری سبع: پھاڑ کانے والا جانور ۔ جموح: سرکشی کرنا، سواری کا قابو میں نہ آنا۔ ترجمه : (۶۳۹) اورنماز کجاوے میں ایسا ہے جیسے خود جانور پر نماز پڑھ رہا ہو چاہے جانور چل رہا ہو یا ٹھہرا ہوا ہو۔ تشریح : محمل کا ترجمہ ہے کجاوہ ۔ کجاوے میں کھڑے ہونے کی جگہ نہ ہو اور نہ کھڑا ہو کر رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے کی جگہ ہو تو اس پر فرض اور واجب پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے، اس کا حکم جانور کا حکم ہے، چاہے جانور چل رہا ہو چاہے ٹھہرا ہوا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس میں قیام نہیں کر سکےگا، اور نہ پورے طور پر رکوع سجدہ کر سکے گا۔ لغت : احمل : کجاوہ ، اونٹ پر دونوں جانب لکڑیا لگا کر انسان بیٹھنے کے لئے بناتے ہیں، جسکو کجاہ ، اور حمل کہتے ہیں۔ : (۶۴۰) اور اگر کجاوے کے نیچے لکڑی ڈال دی جائے کہ وہ زمین پر ٹک جائے تو کجاوہ زمین کی طرح ہو گیا اب اس میں کھڑا ہو کر فرض جائز ہے۔ تشریح : کجاوہ جانور پر ہے اور کجاوے کے نیچے لکڑی اس طرح ڈالی کہ کجاوہ لکڑی کے سہارے زمین پر ٹک گیا ،اور اس میں اتنی جگہ ہے کہ کھڑا ہو کر نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور رکوع سجدہ کر سکتا ہے تو اب گویا کہ وہ زمین پر ہے اس لئے اس کا حکم زمین کا ہے، اس لئے اس میں کھڑا ہو کر فرض پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کھڑا نہیں ہوسکتا، یا پورے طور پر رکوع سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا ہے، تو اس کا حکم کجاوہ ہی کا رہے گا ، کیونکہ فرض کا اصل قیام، رکوع اور سجدہ نہیں ہورہے ہیں۔ اصول : قیام، رکوع اور سجدہ کر سکتا ہو تو زمین کا حکم ہے ، اور یہ نہ کر سکتا ہو تو اس کا حکم کجاوے کا ہے۔
Obligatory prayer on an animal due to his inability. (639) And prayer in the howdah on the animal is like prayer on it, whether it is moving or stationary. (640) And if he places a plank under the howdah such that its base rests on the ground, it becomes like the ground, so prayer is valid in it facing away from it, unless he is sick or fearful, then he should pray on his animal facing towards the house, not away from it. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on whether obligatory prayer is prayed on an animal, etc., vol. 2, p. 1377, no. 4520) (2) From Ata who said: If a person is in water and cannot get out, then he should pray and gesture with his head without prostrating. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, same chapter, vol. 2, p. 1378, no. 4527) This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that if there is compulsion, one can pray fard on an animal. (3) Witr on an animal is fully permissible; there is hadith for it: From Abdullah ibn Umar that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray witr on his riding camel. (Muslim, chapter on permissibility of nafl prayer on an animal during travel, wherever it faces, p. 285, no. 1617/700; Abu Dawud, chapter on voluntary prayer on riding animals and witr, p. 182, no. 1224) This hadith indicates that the Prophet used to pray witr on his mount. Note: Nowadays it happens that one may pray on trains, cars, and airplanes; if one can bow and prostrate there, then fard and other prayers are permissible. And if one cannot bow and prostrate and there is compulsion, then pray with gestures; and if there is no compulsion, then pray later; the proof has passed. Vocabulary: لص: thief; دابة: quadruped, animal, mount; سبع: predatory animal; جموح: being stubborn, mount not under control. Translation: (639) And prayer in a howdah is like praying on the animal itself, whether the animal is moving or stationary. Explanation: Howdah means kijawah. In a howdah, there is no place to stand and no place to perform ruku and sujud while standing; so praying fard and wajib on it is not permissible; its ruling is like that of an animal, whether the animal is moving or stationary, because one cannot stand, nor can he fully do ruku and sujud. Vocabulary: محمل: howdah, made by attaching wood on both sides of a camel for a person to sit. (640) And if a plank is placed under the howdah so that it rests on the ground, then the howdah becomes like the ground; now it is permissible to pray fard standing in it. Explanation: The howdah is on the animal, and a plank is placed under it such that the howdah rests on the ground by the plank, and there is enough room to stand and pray, and to do ruku and sujud; then it is as if he is on the ground, so its ruling is that of the ground; therefore he can pray fard standing. But if he cannot stand, or cannot fully do ruku and sujud, then its ruling remains that of the howdah, because the essence of fard—standing, ruku, and sujud—is not being done. Principle: If one can stand, ruku, and sujud, then it is like the ground; if not, then it is like the howdah.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on praying obligatory prayer while on a riding animal or in a howdah. It begins by stating that obligatory prayer on an animal is permitted when one is unable to dismount. The text then addresses the howdah (a covered litter on a camel), equating it to the animal itself: prayer in a howdah is like praying on the animal, whether it is moving or stationary. However, if a plank is placed under the howdah so that it rests on the ground, it takes the ruling of the ground, and one may pray fard standing, provided one can stand, bow, and prostrate fully. If these are not possible, the howdah retains its original ruling. The passage also includes evidence from hadith and athar, such as the Prophet praying witr on his mount, and a note by the commentator extending the ruling to modern conveyances like trains, cars, and airplanes, with the condition that if one can perform the physical actions of prayer, it is valid; otherwise, gestures are acceptable only when necessary. The commentator emphasizes that the key is the ability to perform the essential acts of prayer (qiyam, ruku, sujud) in their proper form.

Key Terms
محمل (mihmal): A howdah: a covered litter placed on a camel for riding.
دابة (dābbah): A riding animal, specifically a quadruped like a horse, camel, or donkey.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate ruku' and sujud when one is unable to perform them normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a howdah is stabilized by a plank touching the ground, what is its ruling?
A) It remains like an animal, so prayer is not valid standing.
B) It becomes like the ground, so it is permissible to pray fard standing if one can stand, bow, and prostrate.
C) It takes the ruling of a ship, so prayer is allowed sitting.
D) It becomes like a flying object, so prayer is not valid.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayer on an animal or in a howdah is valid only when necessity prevents dismounting, and the ability to perform the pillars (standing, bowing, prostrating) determines the form of prayer.

Prayer in a Moving Ship: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer in a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on praying obligatory prayer in a moving ship and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the requirement of an excuse.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the ship's motion itself is an excuse to sit; for the Sahibayn, only actual hardship suffices.

The Hanafi school presents a nuanced internal dispute on an everyday scenario: praying fard in a moving ship. Should the ship's movement itself count as an 'udhr (excuse) to sit, or must there be specific hardship like dizziness? This lesson unpacks the two positions, their proofs from the Salaf, and the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between them, ultimately showing which view is relied upon in later Hanafi practice.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the ruling: prayer in a moving ship while sitting with full ruku and sujud is valid even without an external excuse. Note his reasoning: the ship's movement itself constitutes an 'udhr.
Evidence: action of Anas ibn Malik.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
State that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, sitting prayer without an excuse is invalid. An excuse must be a genuine hardship such as dizziness or inability to go ashore.
Evidence: athar from Ata that Companions prayed standing unless they feared drowning.
3
Analyze the proofs (athar)
Examine each athar. Note that both are from Musannaf Abdurrazzaq. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of 'udhr: is the natural motion of the ship sufficient, or must there be additional difficulty?
The Hanafi method gives weight to actions of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi) even if not Prophetic hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, one may sit in any moving ship without excuse; under the Sahibayn, one must stand unless there is actual hardship.
This difference affects millions of Muslims traveling by boat or ferry.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text explicitly states that the Sahibayn's view is 'al-azhar' (more apparent), signaling that it is the relied-upon position in the later school.
This is a classic tarjih within the madhhab: the opinion of the majority of the mujtahid imams prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (في الصلوة في السفينة) (۲۴۱) صلوة الفرض فيها و هي جارية قاعدا بلا عذر صحيحة عند ابي حنيفة بالركوع والسجود (۶۴۲) وقالا لا تصح الا من عذر وهو الاظهر والعذر كدوران الرأس وعدم القدرة على الخروج (۶۴۳) ولا تجوز فيها بالايماء اتفاقا (۲۴۴) والمربوطة فى لجة البحر وتحرّكها الريح شديدا... فصل کشتی میں نماز پڑھنے کے بیان میں ترجمه : (۴۱) چلتی ہوئی کشتی میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک بلا عذر بھی بیٹھ کر رکوع وسجود سے نماز پڑھنا صحیح ہے۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ کشتی چل رہی ہو تو اس کا چلنا ہی بیٹھنے کے لئے عذر ہے اس لئے عذر نہ بھی ہوتو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس اثر میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ حدثت عن أنس بن مالك أنه قصر في سفينة ، فصلى فيها جالسا و صلي من معه جلوسا - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل يصلى الرجل وهو ليسوق دابته؟ وقصر الصلوة ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۸۳، نمبر ۴۵۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت انس نے کشتی میں بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھائی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر عذر کے بھی کشتی میں فرض نماز بیٹھ کر پڑھی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۶۴۲) اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بلا عذر سیح نہیں ، یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے۔ اور عذر کی مثال جیسے سر گھومے ( چکرائے ) اور باہر نکلنے پر قادر نہ ہو۔ تشریح : صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ چلتی ہوئی کشتی میں کھڑا ہونا مشکل ہو مثلا سر میں چکر آتا ہو اور باہر نکلنے پر قدرت نہ ہوتو اب بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے لیکن اگر کھڑا ہو ناممکن ہو تو بیٹھ کر نماز نہ پڑھے۔ وجه : اس اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال : يصلون في السفينة قياما الا أن يخافوا أن يغرقوا ، فيصلون جلوسا يتبعون القبلة حيث ما زالت ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلوۃ فی السفییه ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۶۱ ۴۵ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ڈوبنے کا خطرہ ہوتب ہی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے۔ یا پھر کھڑا ہونا مشکل ہو تب ہی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۶۴۳) اور سب کے نزدیک کشتی میں اشارہ سے نماز جائز نہیں۔ تشریح کشتی میں بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے اس لئے اشارے سے نماز پڑھنا کسی کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔ دلیل او پرگز رچکی ۔ ترجمه : (۶۴۴) اور جوشتی سمندر کے درمیان اس طرح بندھی ہوئی ہو کہ ہوا اس کو سخت ہلا رہی ہو تو وہ چلنے والی کشتی کی طرح
Section: On prayer in a ship. (641) The obligatory prayer in a moving ship while sitting without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa, with bowing and prostrating. (642) And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid except with an excuse, and this is the more apparent view. The excuse is like dizziness and inability to go out. (643) And it is not permissible in it by gestures, by agreement. (244) And if the ship is moored in the midst of the sea and the wind shakes it violently... Section on prayer in a ship. Translation: (41) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, praying fard in a moving ship while sitting with bowing and prostration is valid even without an excuse. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's view is that the movement of the ship itself is an excuse for sitting, so even without another excuse, one can pray sitting. Evidence: This is proven by this athar: I was narrated from Anas ibn Malik that he shortened prayer in a ship, so he prayed sitting, and those with him prayed sitting. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on whether a man prays while driving his animal and shortening prayer, vol. 2, p. 1383, no. 4557) This athar shows that Hadhrat Anas led prayer sitting in a ship, from which it is understood that if someone prays fard in a ship sitting without excuse, the prayer is valid. Translation: (642) And according to the Sahibayn, it is not valid without an excuse, and this is the apparent madhhab. The excuse is like dizziness and inability to go out. Explanation: According to the Sahibayn, if standing in a moving ship is difficult, e.g., one becomes dizzy and cannot go out, then one can pray sitting; but if standing is not impossible, then one should not pray sitting. Evidence: This athar: From Ata who said: They pray in a ship standing, unless they fear drowning, then they pray sitting, following the qibla wherever it shifts. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on prayer in a ship, vol. 2, p. 1383, no. 4561) This athar shows that only when there is fear of drowning or standing is difficult can one pray sitting. Translation: (643) And everyone agrees that prayer by gestures is not permissible in a ship. Explanation: Because one can pray sitting, so gesture prayer is not allowed by anyone. The proof has passed. Translation: (644) And if the ship is moored in the midst of the sea and the wind shakes it violently, then it is like a moving ship.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on performing obligatory prayer in a moving ship. The text begins by stating Imam Abu Hanifa's position: it is valid to pray sitting with full ruku and sujud even without an excuse, as the mere movement of the ship constitutes a sufficient excuse for sitting. The evidence is the action of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) who prayed sitting in a ship. Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that it is not valid without an excuse such as dizziness or inability to go ashore, and this is considered the more apparent (azhar) position. Their evidence is the athar from Ata that the Companions would pray standing unless they feared drowning. The text further notes that all agree that prayer by gestures (ima') is not allowed in a ship because one can sit. Finally, a moored ship shaken violently by wind takes the ruling of a moving ship. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each ruling and its proof from the Salaf.

Key Terms
سفينة (safīnah): A ship or boat, used for travel by water.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesturing with head or body instead of actual bowing and prostration.
عذر (ʿudhr): A valid excuse that permits relaxation of normal prayer obligations, such as illness, fear, or inability to stand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when is it permissible to pray obligatory prayer while sitting in a moving ship?
A) At all times, just as Imam Abu Hanifa says.
B) Only when the ship is stationary.
C) When there is an excuse such as dizziness or inability to go ashore.
D) Never; one must always stand.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that obligatory prayer in a moving ship cannot be performed sitting without a genuine excuse; the ship's mere motion is insufficient.

Sitting Prayer in a Moving Ship: The Intr-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting prayer without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sitting prayer in a moving ship and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Praying sitting in a moving ship without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the relied-upon view requires an excuse.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of performing obligatory prayer while sitting in a moving ship without a valid excuse. While Imam Abu Hanifa permitted it based on the natural motion of the ship, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) required a tangible excuse such as dizziness. Understanding this difference is crucial for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed condition
The act is performing fard prayer in a moving ship while sitting. The dispute is whether a valid excuse is required for the prayer to be valid.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is valid even without an excuse, because the ship's motion itself constitutes a hardship. His evidence includes the action of Anas ibn Malik, who prayed sitting in a ship.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require a tangible excuse such as dizziness or inability to exit the ship. They rely on the general command to stand in prayer (Quran 2:238) and the statement of 'Ata that sitting is only allowed out of fear of drowning.
4
Analyse the tarjih (preference)
The text explicitly states 'wa huwa al-azhar' (this is the more apparent view), preferring the Sahibayn's position. Therefore, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that a valid excuse is required.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the proof and the caution in sacred obligations.
5
Apply the ruling: what qualifies as an excuse?
The text mentions two examples: dizziness of the head (dawarān ar-ra's) and inability to exit the ship. Any comparable hardship that prevents standing or safe exit would similarly qualify.
Agreed-upon: ima' (gesture) is never allowed in this scenario because sitting permits actual bowing and prostration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل (في الصلوة في السفينة) (۲۴۱) صلوة الفرض فيها و هي جارية قاعدا بلا عذر صحيحة عند ابي حنيفة بالركوع والسجود (۶۴۲) وقالا لا تصح الا من عذر وهو الاظهر والعذر كدوران الرأس وعدم القدرة على الخروج (۶۴۳) ولا تجوز فيها بالايماء اتفاقا
Section on prayer in a ship. (241) The obligatory prayer in it while it is moving, sitting without excuse, is valid according to Abu Hanifa, with bowing and prostration. (242) And the two said: it is not valid except with an excuse, and this is the more apparent view; the excuse is like dizziness of the head and inability to get out. (243) And it is not permissible in it by gesture, by agreement.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of performing obligatory prayer sitting in a moving ship without a valid excuse. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the very motion of the ship constitutes an excuse, making sitting prayer valid even without additional excuse. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require a tangible excuse such as dizziness or inability to exit the ship. The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is the Sahibayn's view. All scholars agree that gesturing (ima') is not allowed in ship prayer because one can perform actual bowing and prostration while sitting.

Key Terms
صلاة الفرض (salat al-fard): The mandatory obligatory prayer performed in a ship.
بالايماء (bi-l-ima'): A gesture of bowing and prostration without actual bodily movement, permissible only when unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the Sahibayn permit sitting prayer in a moving ship?
A) Always, without any excuse.
B) Only if the ship is anchored.
C) Only if there is an excuse such as dizziness or inability to exit.
D) Only when performing nafl prayers.

Key Takeaway
When praying fard in a moving ship, a valid excuse is required for sitting per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Ruling on Sitting Prayer in an Anchored Ship: Deep Sea vs. Shore
Two rulings on anchored ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting prayer in an anchored ship in two scenarios: when the ship is violently shaken in deep sea and when it is stationary at shore.

Core Idea
An anchored ship violently shaken by wind is like a moving ship; sitting prayer requires excuse. A stationary ship at shore is like land; sitting is prohibited by consensus.

This lesson distinguishes between two scenarios of an anchored ship. The Hanafi school classifies a ship anchored in deep sea that is violently shaken by wind as equivalent to a moving ship, where sitting in prayer is only allowed if one cannot stand. If the ship is not shaken, or if it is anchored at the shore, it is considered stationary, and sitting in prayer without a valid excuse is impermissible by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: a ship anchored in deep sea with violent wind, and a ship anchored at shore.
2
Apply the moving vs stationary distinction
For the deep sea case, if the wind moves the ship violently, it is treated like a moving ship (saira). If not, it is stationary (waqifa) on the correct view.
3
Determine the ruling for sitting prayer
In a moving ship (or its equivalent), sitting requires an excuse (inability to stand without falling). In a stationary ship (including at shore), sitting is not permissible unless there is an excuse, and for the shore case, it is forbidden by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴۴) والمربوطة فى لجة البحر وتحرّكها الريح شديدا كالسائرة والا فالواقفة على الاصح (۶۴۵) وان كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلوته قاعدا بالاجماع
(244) And the ship anchored in the deep sea, with the wind moving it violently, is like a moving ship; otherwise it is considered stationary on the correct view. (245) And if it is anchored at the shore, his prayer while sitting is not permissible by consensus.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings about anchored ships. First, a ship anchored in the deep sea that is violently shaken by the wind is considered like a moving ship (saira), so sitting prayer without excuse is not allowed; if it is not shaking, it is considered stationary (waqifa) like a ship at shore. Second, a ship anchored at the shore (bi-l-shatt) is not permissible for sitting prayer by consensus of the Hanafi scholars, because one can easily stand on land or on the ship since it is stable.

Key Terms
لجة البحر (lujjat al-bahr): The deep part of the sea where the ship is anchored but affected by wind.
الشط (al-shatt): The shore or bank of the sea.

D) Permissible only if part of the ship is on land.

Key Takeaway
A ship anchored in deep sea and violently shaken is like a moving ship; if still, it is like at shore where sitting prayer is prohibited by consensus.

Condition for Standing Prayer in an Anchored Ship
Condition for validity of standing prayer in anchored ship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of standing prayer on a ship and apply the exception for inability to exit.

Core Idea
Standing prayer on a ship is valid only if part of the ship touches land, unless exit is impossible.

You may find yourself on a ship anchored near the shore. Does standing for prayer require you to be on solid ground? This short ruling provides a clear condition: as long as any part of the ship is on land, standing is valid. If the ship is entirely afloat, a further exception applies when you cannot safely leave. Understanding this condition ensures your prayer remains valid in maritime contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary act and condition
The act is praying standing on a ship. The condition is that part of the ship is on solid ground (qarar al-ard).
2
Note the default ruling
If the condition is met, the prayer is valid (sahih). If not, it is not valid (la tasihh).
3
Recognize the exception
If the person cannot exit the ship (e.g., due to danger), the prayer is valid even without the condition.
Exception: 'illa idha lam yumkinuhu al-khuruj'.
4
Understand the chosen view
This is the preferred (al-mukhtar) view within the Hanafi school. A weaker view allows standing prayer even without land contact.
Authority: 'ala al-mukhtar' indicates mufta bihi status.
5
Apply the ruling to real scenarios
Test with examples: ship partly beached vs. ship afloat but person unable to leave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۴۶) فان صلى قائما وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الارض صحت الصلوة والا فلا تصح على المختار الا اذا لم يمكنه الخروج
(246) And if he prays standing and some part of the ship is on solid ground, the prayer is valid; otherwise it is not valid on the chosen view, unless he cannot exit.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage gives a condition for the validity of standing prayer on a ship that is not moving. If any part of the ship is resting on land (i.e., touching the ground), then standing prayer on the ship is valid because the ship has some stability akin to land. If the ship is not touching land at all, then standing prayer on it is not valid according to the preferred view (al-mukhtar), unless the person is unable to exit the ship (for example due to danger). In that case, the prayer is valid as a concession. The reason is that when the ship is not grounded, it might move and cause imbalance, making proper standing difficult.

Key Terms
قرار الأرض (qarar al-ard): Solid ground/land that is stable.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen/preferred view within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is never valid.
D) It is valid only if the ship is in motion.

Key Takeaway
Standing prayer on a ship is valid if part of the ship is on land, or if the person cannot exit the ship.

Facing Qibla During Ship Prayer: Continuous Obligation
Ruling on facing qibla continuously in ship prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on facing qibla during ship prayer and identify when reorientation is required.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is a condition; on a ship, you must keep turning to maintain it.

Prayer on a ship presents a unique challenge: the vessel may change direction mid-prayer. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling that the worshipper must face the qibla at the start and adjust whenever the ship turns away. Understanding this ensures your prayer remains valid even in motion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its setting
Recognize that the ruling applies to obligatory or voluntary prayer performed on a moving ship. The setting is important because the ship's movement can affect the direction of prayer.
This is not about prayer during extreme fear (khawf) where different rules apply.
2
State the initial obligation
At the beginning of prayer (takbir), the worshipper must face the qibla. This is a condition (shart) for validity.
Facing qibla is wajib based on Quran and Sunnah.
3
Apply the continuous requirement
Whenever the ship turns away from the qibla during the prayer, you must turn your body to face it again. This must be done each time until the prayer ends.
The act of turning does not break the prayer; it is required to maintain the condition.
4
Understand the rationale
Facing qibla is a pillar (or condition) for prayer. Since you are able to turn, it is obligatory. Failure to do so, if able, invalidates the prayer.
The Hanafi school emphasizes ability (istita'a) in fulfilling conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۴۷) ويتوجّه المصلى فيها الى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلوة كلما تحولت السفينة الى القبلة يتوجه اليها حتى يفرغ
(247) And the worshipper in it faces the qibla at the beginning of the prayer; whenever the ship turns away from the qibla, he turns towards it until he finishes.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage outlines the requirement of facing the qibla (direction of prayer) when performing prayer on a ship. The worshipper must initially face the qibla when beginning the prayer (takbir). If the ship changes direction during the prayer, he must adjust his body to face the qibla again, and continue to do so until the prayer is complete. This is because facing qibla is a condition for the validity of prayer according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, unless one is in a situation of fear or inability. On a ship, one is generally able to turn.

Key Terms
القبلة (al-qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only at the beginning of prayer.
B) Whenever the ship turns away from the qibla.
C) Only if the ship is in motion.
D) It is not required on a ship.

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla is a continuous condition in prayer; on a ship, you must adjust whenever the vessel changes direction.

Facing the Qibla During Prayer on a Moving Ship
Ruling on turning towards qibla during prayer on a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for facing the qibla on a moving ship and explain the Quranic proof that supports it.

Core Idea
On a moving ship, you must turn to face the qibla throughout the prayer.

When praying on a ship, the direction of the qibla may shift as the vessel turns. The Hanafi school rules that one must continually adjust orientation to face the qibla, citing the Quranic command and the practice of early Muslims. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying on a moving ship. The ruling is that one must turn towards the qibla whenever the ship turns.
This turning must be done during the prayer without breaking it.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the Quranic verse 2:150, which commands facing the Sacred Mosque wherever one is.
The secondary proof is the practice of the Tabi'i Ata, who reported that sailors followed the qibla on ships.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fawallu' indicates obligation; the phrase 'wherever you are' shows the command is general and includes all situations, even on a moving ship.
The generality of the command is a key point for the Hanafi school.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools hold that facing the qibla is only required at the beginning of prayer. The Hanafi school requires continuous orientation.
The difference leads to practical consequences for those on ships or vehicles.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the clear Quranic text and is the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah).
The mufta bihi ruling: one must turn during prayer if the ship turns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلوة وكلّما استدارت عنها يتوجه اليها في خلال الصلوة حتى يتمها مستقبلا.
وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے۔ وحیث ما كنتم فولوا وجوهكم شطره - آیت ۱۵۰، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جہاں بھی ہو قبلہ کی طرف چہرہ کرو۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال : يصلون في السفينة قياما الا أن يخافوا أن يغرقوا ، فيصلون جلوسا يتبعون القبلة حيث ما زالت - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلوة في السفينة ، ج ثانی ، ص ۳۸۳ نمبر ۴۵۶۱) کہ قبلہ کی طرف گھومتا جائے۔
Prayer: Whenever the ship turns away from the qibla, the person turns towards it during the prayer until he completes it facing the qibla. Evidence (1) This verse: And wherever you are, turn your faces towards it. (Surah al-Baqarah 2:150) (2) The saying of the Tabi'i: Ata said: They pray on the ship standing unless they fear drowning, then they pray sitting, following the qibla wherever it moves.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author states the ruling: If a person prays on a moving ship, he must start facing the qibla, and as the ship turns, he must also turn to keep facing the qibla until he completes his prayer. The proof is first from the Quran (2:150) which commands facing the Sacred Mosque everywhere. Second, from the practice of the early Muslims: Ata reported that sailors on ships pray standing if safe, but if there is a risk of drowning they pray sitting, but in all cases they follow the qibla direction as the ship moves. This is a Hanafi position that emphasizes facing the qibla as an essential condition of prayer, even on a moving vessel.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Sacred Mosque in Mecca that must be faced during prayer.
سفينة (safina): A ship or boat, the context of ruling for prayer while traveling by water.

Tarawih: A Confirmed Sunnah for Men and Women
Ruling on Tarawih as sunnah mu'akkadah with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal ruling (hukm) of Tarawih prayer in the Hanafi school and explain the three proofs that establish it as sunnah mu'akkadah for both men and women.

Core Idea
Tarawih is sunnah mu'akkadah because the Prophet performed it but stopped to prevent it becoming obligatory.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih prayer, a special nightly prayer during Ramadan. The text unequivocally states that Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for both men and women. We will explore the three key proofs: the Prophet’s own practice, his promise of forgiveness for those who pray it with faith, and the practice of Caliph Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who appointed a separate imam for women. Understanding this ruling ensures that both genders know the recommended status of this congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Tarawih is the night prayer of Ramadan performed after Isha. The text classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) for both men and women. Note the derivation from 'raha' (rest) because early Muslims rested after every four rak'ahs.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is between fard/wajib and nafl; omitting it is blameworthy.
2
Examine the primary dalil: Hadith of Aisha
The hadith reported by Aisha shows that the Prophet came out and prayed Tarawih in congregation for three nights, but on the fourth night he stayed back, saying he feared it would be made obligatory. This demonstrates that Tarawih is a sunnah and not fard.
The Prophet's fear of obligation (fard) confirms its sunnah status.
3
Analyze the second dalil: Hadith of Abu Huraira
Abu Huraira reports the Prophet’s statement: 'Whoever stands (in prayer) during Ramadan with faith and seeking reward, his past sins will be forgiven.' This includes Tarawih and encourages its performance.
The term 'qiyam Ramadan' includes Tarawih in the Hanafi school.
4
Study the third dalil: Practice of Ali for women
Urafjah reported that Caliph Ali appointed one imam for men and a separate imam for women for qiyam Ramadan. This proves that women are also encouraged to pray Tarawih in congregation, affirming its sunnah for them.
This is evidence from the practice of a Companion (qawl sahabi) and is authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Confirm the ruling and its implications
The three proofs all point to Tarawih being a sunnah mu'akkadah. The Hanafi school holds that it is equally recommended for men and women, with women allowed to attend the mosque or pray at home. The mufta bihi position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah for both.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

(3) For women specifically, the practice of Caliph Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) shows that he appointed a separate imam for women for Tarawih, proving women are also encouraged to pray it in congregation. Thus Tarawih is equally sunnah for women.

سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, but not obligatory.

Tarawih Congregation as Sunnah Kifayah
Ruling that praying Tarawih in congregation is a collective sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of sunnah kifayah and state the evidence that Tarawih congregation is a collective sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tarawih in congregation is a collective sunnah, not an individual obligation.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling: praying Tarawih in congregation is classified as sunnah kifayah. Understanding this category is critical for correctly applying the recommendation without imposing an unnecessary burden. We will see that the Hanafi school draws on the practice of the early Caliphs to establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Tarawih in congregation. The ruling is sunnah kifayah (collective sunnah). Note that the ruling is not fard or wajib, but a recommended collective practice.
The term 'sunnah kifayah' contrasts with 'sunnah 'ayn' (individual sunnah).
2
Understand the term 'sunnah kifayah'
Sunnah kifayah means that if a sufficient number of Muslims perform the act, the sunnah is fulfilled for the entire community; if no one does it, everyone is blameworthy.
It resembles fard kifayah but at a lower level of obligation.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the athar (report) that Caliph Umar and Caliph Ali each appointed an imam to lead 20 rak'ahs of Tarawih in congregation.
These reports are found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, indicating the practice of the Companions.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The fact that the Caliphs commanded congregation for Tarawih shows that congregation is a sunnah (recommended practice). However, because it was not made individually binding (unlike the five daily prayers), the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah kifayah.
The evidence establishes the recommendation, not the obligation.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Some later Hanafi authorities considered congregation wajib, but the mufta bihi (operative position) remains sunnah kifayah as per the earlier zahir al-riwayah texts.
Other schools may view congregation as individually recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah), which has a different practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۴۹) وصلوتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية .
تشريح : : تراویح کی جماعت سنت کفایہ ہے، کفایہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ محلے میں کچھ لوگ جماعت کے ساتھ تراویح پڑھ لیں تو جماعت کی سنت ادا ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) ان عمر بن خطاب امر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶۷۷ کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعتہ ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۷۶۸۸ ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قیام رمضان ج رابع ص ۲۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۶۰) اس حدیث اور عمل صحابہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح کی نماز میں رکھتیں ہیں۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے۔
(۲) ان علیا أمر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة . ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶۷۷ كم يصلى في رمضان من رکعته ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۷۶۸۰ رسن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عد در كعات القيام في شهر رمضان ج ثانی ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۲ ) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ حضرت علیؓی ہیں رکھتیں تراویح پڑھنے کا حکم دیا کرتے تھے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے۔
Translation (249): And praying it in congregation is sunnah kifayah. Explanation: Congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah, meaning if some people in the neighbourhood pray it in congregation, the sunnah of congregation is fulfilled. Evidence (1) Umar ibn al-Khattab appointed a man to lead them in 20 rak'ahs. (2) Ali appointed a man to lead them in 20 rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author states that praying Tarawih in congregation is sunnah kifayah (collective sunnah). This means that it is recommended for a group to pray together, but if some people do it, the recommendation is fulfilled for the entire community. The proofs: The practice of the Caliphs Umar and Ali, who appointed imams to lead 20 rak'ahs of Tarawih in congregation. This shows that the congregation itself is a sunnah (as the Companions did it) but it is not binding on everyone individually; it is enough that some perform it.

Key Terms
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A collective sunnah: if some Muslims perform it, the sunnah is fulfilled for the rest; otherwise all are blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory for every individual to pray in congregation.
B) It is recommended but if some perform it, the rest are not required.
C) It is forbidden to pray Tarawih alone.
D) It is only for men, not women.

Key Takeaway
Praying Tarawih in congregation is a collective sunnah (sunnah kifayah), meaning it is recommended for the community as a whole, not individually obligatory.

Time of Tarawih Begins After Isha
Ruling with proof: Time for Tarawih after Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Tarawih prayer and identify the hadith proof that establishes it.

Core Idea
The time for Tarawih is after Isha, based on the Prophet's practice in jauf al-layl.

This lesson establishes a foundational ruling regarding the time for Tarawih prayer. Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) performed in congregation during Ramadan. Its time begins immediately after the Isha prayer. The primary proof is a hadith narrated by Aisha that the Prophet prayed in the middle of the night, which is after Isha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The time for Tarawih prayer. The ruling: its time is after Isha.
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith of Aisha in Sahih al-Bukhari that the Prophet prayed in jauf al-layl (middle of the night).
Hadith: 'Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah came out one night in the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque.'
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the time? The phrase 'jauf al-layl' indicates the time is after Isha, because Isha is at the beginning of the night.
Jauf al-layl is the middle part of the night, which comes after Isha.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling is that Tarawih can be prayed any time after Isha until dawn, but it is preferable to pray it early after Isha.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۵۰) ووقتها بعد صلوة العشاء .
وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جوف اللیل، میں نماز پڑھائی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشاء کے بعد تر اویح کا وقت ہے۔ ان عائشة اخبرته ان رسول الله لا خرج ليلة من جوف الليل فصلي في المسجد وصلی رجال بصلاته ( بخاری شریف ، باب فضل من قام رمضان ،ص۱۳۲۲ نمبر۲۰۱۲ر مسلم شریف ، باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وھوالتراویح ص ۱۳۰۸ نمبر ۷۶۱ (۱۷۸۴)
Translation (650): And its time is after the Isha prayer. Evidence: In this hadith, he prayed in the middle of the night, which indicates the time for Tarawih is after Isha. Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah came out one night in the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque, and men prayed with him.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof. The ruling: The time for Tarawih prayer is after the Isha prayer, not before. The proof is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed Tarawih 'in the middle of the night' (jauf al-layl). Since the middle of the night is after Isha, this establishes the time. There is no requirement to delay it to later; it can be prayed immediately after Isha or later in the night. The Hanafi ruling is that the time for Tarawih is from after Isha until dawn, but it is preferable to pray it in the early part of the night for ease.

Key Terms
جوف الليل (jauf al-layl): The middle part of the night, after Isha and before the last third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the time for Tarawih begin?
A) Before Maghrib.
B) After Isha prayer.
C) At midnight exactly.
D) After Fajr.

Key Takeaway
The time for Tarawih prayer begins after the Isha prayer, and the proof is from the hadith of Aisha.

Witr can be performed before or after Tarawih
Ruling on the permissibility of ordering Witr before or after Tarawih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the order of Witr and Tarawih and explain why both orders are valid.

Core Idea
Both orders for Witr and Tarawih are valid—no obligatory sequence.

In Hanafi fiqh, the night prayers of Ramadan include both Tarawih and Witr. Some assume Witr must come after Tarawih. This passage clarifies that either order is permissible, giving flexibility to the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Witr before or after Tarawih. The ruling is 'sahih' (valid).
The text states يَصِحُّ (valid).
2
Determine the hukm level
This is a ruling of permissibility (ibaha). Both orders are mubah.
No evidence mandates a specific sequence.
3
Understand the basis
The permissibility stems from the general principle that supererogatory prayers have flexible order unless specified otherwise.
The primary aim is to complete the night prayers; the order is secondary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۵۱) ويصح تقديم وتر را بر تراویح مقدم کرنا اور اس سے مؤخر کرنا۔
Translation (251): And it is valid to present the Witr before Tarawih and to postpone it after it.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement without proof in this excerpt. The author states that it is permissible (sahih) to perform the Witr prayer either before Tarawih or after it. There is flexibility; one may pray Witr first and then Tarawih, or pray Tarawih first and then Witr. Both orders are valid and the prayer is accepted. This is based on the general permissibility of ordering supererogatory prayers. In practice, most Hanafis pray Witr after Tarawih, but praying Witr first is also allowed.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer prayed after the night prayer, usually 3 rak'ahs, wajib in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only if one misses Tarawih.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The order of Witr and Tarawih is flexible; both sequences are valid in Hanafi fiqh.

Tarawih in Congregation is Sunnah Kifayah
Ruling on Tarawih congregation with proofs from hadith and Companion practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Tarawih congregation as sunnah kifayah and explain its proofs from the hadith and Companion practice.

Core Idea
Tarawih in congregation is a communal sunnah, not individually obligatory, established by the Prophet's hadith and the Caliphs' practice.

This passage from the text clarifies the Hanafi ruling on offering Tarawih prayers in congregation. While Tarawih itself is a highly recommended act, performing it with the congregation is classified as sunnah kifayah—a communal sunnah that, if observed by some in a locality, fulfills the sunnah for all. The author anchors this ruling in the famous hadith of Abu Huraira and the consistent practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs 'Umar and 'Ali, who organized twenty rak'ahs in congregation.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (Tarawih congregation) and its legal classification (sunnah kifayah). Understand that sunnah kifayah means a recommended act that, if performed by some members of the community, absolves the rest.
2
Identify the proof from hadith
Locate the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'Whoever stands (in prayer) in it with faith and seeking reward, his previous sins will be forgiven.' Note how 'man qamahu' refers to night prayer in Ramadan, which includes Tarawih.
The hadith establishes the virtue and legitimacy of Tarawih.
3
Examine the Companion actions
Look at the reports that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab and 'Ali ibn Abi Talib appointed imams for twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih in congregation. This demonstrates that the practice was established and approved by the early community.
4
Understand sunnah kifayah
Grasp the communal aspect: if enough people in a locality pray Tarawih with congregation, the sunnah is fulfilled for everyone. It is not fard on each individual.
This avoids the misconception that it is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التراويح (۶۴۹) وصلوتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية
یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے۔ (۲) أن ابا هريرة قال : سمعت رسول الله الله يقول لرمضان (( من قامه ايمانا و احتسابا غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه . (بخاری شریف ، باب فضل من قام رمضان ، ص ۱۳۲۲، نمبر ۲۰۰۸ مسلم شریف ، باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وهو التراویح ج ،۳۰۸، نمبر ۷۷۹/۷۵۹ ار ابو داؤد شریف ، کتاب تفریح ابواب شہر رمضان باب فی قیام شہر رمضان ، ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۱۳۷۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایمان کے ساتھ جو تراویح پڑھے گا اسکا گناہ معاف کر دیا جائے گا۔ اس میں تراویح کا ثبوت ہے ۔ (۳) عورت کے لئے بھی تراویح سنت مؤکدہ ہے اس کی دلیل اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن عرفجة ان عليا كان يأمر الناس بالقيام في رمضان فيجعل للرجال اماما و للنساء اماما (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب قیام رمضان ج رابع ، ص ۱۹۹۱ نمبر ۷۷۵۲ رسن بیہقی ، باب قیام شهر رمضان ، ج ثانی ، ص ۶۹۵ نمبر ۴۶۰۶) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کے لئے بھی تراویح کا امام مقر ر فرماتے تھے۔
ترجمه : (۲۴۹) اور اس کی جماعت سنت کفایہ ہے۔
تشريح : : تراویح کی جماعت سنت کفایہ ہے، کفایہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ محلے میں کچھ لوگ جماعت کے ساتھ تراویح پڑھ لیں تو جماعت کی سنت ادا ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) ان عمر بن خطاب امر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶۷۷ کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعتہ ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۷۶۸۸ ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قیام رمضان ج رابع ص ۲۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۶۰) اس حدیث اور عمل صحابہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح کی نماز میں رکھتیں ہیں۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے۔ (۲) ان علیا أمر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة .
