Chapter on Tarawih (649) And its prayer in congregation is sunnah kifayah. It is also known that Tarawih should be prayed with congregation. (2) That Abu Huraira said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say regarding Ramadan: 'Whoever stands (in prayer) in it with faith and seeking reward, his previous sins will be forgiven.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) In this hadith, whoever prays Tarawih with faith, his sin will be forgiven. This proves Tarawih. (3) For women, Tarawih is also sunnah muakkadah; its proof is in this Companion's statement: From 'Arfajah that 'Ali used to order people to stand in prayer in Ramadan and would appoint an imam for men and an imam for women. (Mussanaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This companion's action shows that they would appoint an imam for women for Tarawih. Translation: (249) And its congregation is sunnah kifayah. Explanation: Tarawih congregation is sunnah kifayah; kifayah means that if some people in the neighborhood pray Tarawih with congregation, the sunnah of congregation is fulfilled. Proofs: (1) That 'Umar ibn al-Khattab appointed a man to lead them in twenty rak'ahs. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, 'Abd al-Razzaq) This hadith and companion's action show that Tarawih prayer has rak'ahs and also that it should be prayed with congregation. (2) That 'Ali appointed a man to lead them in twenty rak'ahs. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi) This effect also shows that 'Ali used to order twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih and that it should be prayed with congregation.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with supporting proofs. The author begins by stating that praying Tarawih in congregation is sunnah kifayah, meaning a communal sunnah. The Urdu commentary explains that if some people in the locality perform it with congregation, the obligation of the sunnah is lifted from the rest. The author then provides three proofs: first, the famous hadith from Abu Huraira about the virtue of standing in Ramadan (Qiyam Ramadan) which includes Tarawih; second, the actions of Caliph 'Umar who appointed an imam for twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih in congregation; third, the action of Caliph 'Ali who similarly appointed an imam for twenty rak'ahs and also appointed a separate imam for women, indicating that Tarawih is also sunnah for women. The madhhab position is that Tarawih congregation is sunnah kifayah, not fard, and this is established by the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A recommended act that, if performed by some members of the community, fulfills the sunnah for all.
تراویح (tarawih): The night prayers performed in Ramadan, typically twenty rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Witr Can Be Before or After Tarawih
States permissibility of Witr relative to Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the order of Witr and Tarawih and explain the recommended sequence with its proof.

Core Idea
It is permissible to pray Witr before or after Tarawih, but better after.

This lesson clarifies the relationship between Tarawih and Witr. The text affirms that both orders are valid, but the preferred practice follows the Sunnah of ending the night with Witr. We will examine the proof from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the ordering of Witr prayer relative to Tarawih prayer during Ramadan. The text states that it is 'correct' (sahih) to present Witr before or delay it after, meaning it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs (Tarawih) and Witr in Ramadan. This is found in Tabarani, Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abi Shaybah.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for establishing the sunna.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'twenty rak'ahs and Witr' (عشرين ركعة والوتر) implies a sequence where Witr is mentioned after the twenty. This indicates that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Witr after completing the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih.
The conjunction 'waw' (and) in Arabic can indicate sequence, especially in narrative contexts.
4
Note the preferred practice
Even though both orders are permissible, the text explicitly says 'it is better to pray Witr after Tarawih' because the hadith indicates that Witr should be the last prayer of the night. This is consistent with the general sunna of making Witr the final prayer.
Preferred practice (mustahabb) does not affect the validity; both orders are valid.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is permissible to pray Witr before or after Tarawih, but the recommended sequence is to pray Witr after Tarawih. This is based on the hadith and the broader sunna.
No ikhtilaf within the school on this point; all agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۵۱) اور صحیح ہے وتر کوتراویح پر مقدم کرنا اور اس سے مؤخر کرنا۔
تشریح : تراویح وتر کے تابع نہیں ہے اس لئے تراویح کو وتر سے پہلے بھی پڑھ سکتے ہیں اور بعد میں بھی ، البتہ وتر کو تراویح کے بعد پڑھنا بہتر ہے، کیونکہ وتر کے بارے میں حدیث ہے کہ وہ رات کی آخری نماز ہو۔
وجه : اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ وتر بعد میں پڑھے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي عله يصلي في شهر رمضان عشرين ركعة والوتر - (طبراني الكبير، باب مقسم عن ابن عباس، ج حادی عشر، ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۱۲۱۰۲ سنن سبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان، ج ثانی ،ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۱۵ رمصنف ابن ابی شیبیۃ ، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعتہ ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر (۷۶۹ ) عشرین رکعتہ والوتر ، سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ وتر بعد میں پڑھے۔
Translation: (651) And it is correct to present Witr before Tarawih and to delay it after it. Explanation: Tarawih is not subordinate to Witr, so Tarawih can be prayed before Witr and also after it; however, it is better to pray Witr after Tarawih, because according to hadith, Witr is the last prayer of the night. Proof: This hadith indicates that Witr should be prayed later. From Ibn 'Abbas: He said the Prophet used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan. (Tabarani, Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Shaybah) The phrase 'twenty rak'ahs and Witr' shows that Witr was prayed after.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This ruling addresses the order of Tarawih and Witr. The text confirms that it is permissible to pray Witr either before or after Tarawih. However, the better practice (mustahabb) is to pray Witr after Tarawih because of the hadith that Witr should be the last prayer of the night. The proof is from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs (Tarawih) and then Witr. This indicates Witr came after Tarawih. The Hanafi school holds that Tarawih and Witr are independent; there is no obligation to pray them in a specific order, but the recommended sequence is Tarawih followed by Witr.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after night prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying Witr before Tarawih according to the Hanafi school?
A) Not permissible
B) Permissible but better to pray after
C) Must be prayed before
D) Prohibited

Key Takeaway
The order of Witr and Tarawih is flexible; both are valid, but the sunna is to end the night with Witr.

Recommended Delay of Tarawih to Third or Half of Night
States recommended time for Tarawih and its permissibility later

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Tarawih according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from the Sunnah that supports delaying it.

Core Idea
Delaying Tarawih to the middle of the night follows the Prophet's practice and is mustahabb, not makruh.

This lesson explains the preferred time for performing Tarawih prayers. While the time begins after Isha, the Hanafi school considers it mustahabb to delay it until one-third or half of the night, based on the example of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who prayed in the middle of the night and even until close to suhur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Tarawih and what is its recommended timing according to the Hanafi school? The text states it is mustahabb to delay it to thuluth or nisf al-layl.
2
Locate the dalil
What hadith evidence is cited? Two hadiths: (1) 'Aisha's report that the Prophet prayed in the middle of the night, and (2) the hadith of Abu Dharr that the Prophet led Tarawih until close to suhur.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the phrase 'jauf al-layl' in the first hadith indicate the recommended time? It shows that the Prophet chose the middle part of the night, making it a recommended practice.
4
Note the scope and conditions
Does the ruling apply to all worshippers? The text adds a condition: if the worshiper has no energy, it is better to pray early after Isha.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
What is the relied-upon position regarding delaying beyond half the night? According to the correct narration (على الصحيح), it is not makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۵۲) اور تراویح کو تہائی رات تک یا آدھی رات تک مؤخر کر نا مستحب ہے، اور صحیح روایت میں اس کے بعد بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد ہے، لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ تہائی رات تک مؤخر کرے، یا آدھی رات تک مؤخر کرے۔اور اس کے بعد بھی مؤخر کرے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جب نمازی کو نشاط ہوورنہ عشاء کے فورا بعد تراویح شروع کرے
وجه : (ا) ان عائشة اخبرته ان رسول الله الا الله خرج ليلة من جوف الليل فصلي في المسجد وصلى رجال بصلاته ( بخاری شریف، باب فضل من قام رمضان، ص ۱۳۲۲، نمبر ۲۰۱۲ مسلم شریف ، باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وهو التراویح ، ص ۱۳۰۸، نمبر ۷۶۱ (۱۷۸۴) اس حدیث میں جوف اللیل سے اشارہ ہے کہ تراویح رات کے درمیانی حصے میں پڑھی ۔ (۲) اور سحری سے پہلے پہلے تک مؤخر کر سکتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ذر قال : صمنا مع رسول الله الا الله رمضان فلم يقم بنا شيئا من الشهر .... فلما كانت الثالثة جمع أهله و نسائه و الناس فقام بنا حتى خشينا أن يفوتنا الفلاح ، قال قلت : ما الفلاح ؟ قال السحور ، ثم لم يقم بنا بقية الشهر - (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی قیام شهر رمضان ، ص ۲۰۵، نمبر ۱۳۷۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سحری تک تراویح پڑھتے رہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ سحری تک وقت ہے۔ لغت: ثلث اللیل، ونصفہ : تہائی رات یعنی دس بجے رات تک، اور آدھی رات یعنی بارہ بجے رات تک مؤخر کرے۔
Translation: (652) And it is mustahabb to delay Tarawih until one-third of the night or half of the night, and according to the correct narration, delaying beyond that is not makruh. Explanation: The time for Tarawih is after Isha, but it is mustahabb to delay it to one-third or half of the night. And if one delays it beyond that, it is not makruh. But this is when the worshiper has energy; otherwise, he should start Tarawih immediately after Isha. Proofs: (1) That 'Aisha informed him that the Messenger of Allah went out one night from the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque, and men prayed with his prayer. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, 'middle of the night' indicates that Tarawih was prayed in the middle part of the night. (2) And he can delay until just before suhur; its proof is the hadith of Abu Dharr: We fasted with the Messenger of Allah in Ramadan, and he did not lead us in prayer for any part of the month... Then on the third night, he gathered his family and women and the people and led us in prayer until we feared missing al-falah. I asked: What is al-falah? He said: Suhur. Then he did not lead us for the rest of the month. (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that they prayed Tarawih until suhur, indicating that the time extends to suhur. Lexicon: 'Thuluth al-layl' and 'nisafuhu': one-third of the night, i.e., until about 10 PM, and half the night, i.e., until 12 AM.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This ruling discusses the recommended time for performing Tarawih. While the time starts after Isha, it is mustahabb to delay it to one-third or half of the night, following the practice of the Prophet who sometimes prayed in the middle of the night. The hadith of Abu Dharr shows that the Prophet prayed Tarawih with them until close to suhur, proving that the time extends until dawn. However, the text advises that if one fears drowsiness, it is better to pray early. The correct view (al-sahih) is that delaying beyond half the night is not makruh, though the earlier time is better. The commentary provides a glossary: 'thuluth al-layl' (one-third of night) is approximately 10 PM, and 'nisafuhu' (half) is midnight.

Key Terms
ثلث الليل (thuluth al-layl): One-third of the night, approximately from Isha to 10 PM.
نصف الليل (nisf al-layl): Half of the night, approximately midnight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the text, what is the ruling on delaying Tarawih beyond half the night?
A) Makruh tahrimi
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Not makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Tarawih to one-third or half of the night, and delaying further is not makruh.

Tarawih: Twenty Rak'ahs with Ten Salams
Specifies the number of rak'ahs and salams for Tarawih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih and cite the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs prayed in sets of two with ten salams — a sunnah muakkadah established by the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

This lesson clarifies the exact number of rak'ahs for Tarawih, a highly emphasized sunnah during Ramadan. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet (saw) and the Companions, holds it to be twenty rak'ahs with ten salams. The proof is a narration from Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The text explicitly states that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs with ten salams. This is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet regularly performed it and encouraged it.
2
Note the method of prayer
The prayer is performed in sets of two rak'ahs, with a salam after each pair, resulting in ten salams total.
This is the sunnah method; praying four with one salam is permissible but less meritorious.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan.' This is recorded by Tabarani and Bayhaqi.
The hadith is ahad (single chain), but its meaning is supported by the practice of the Companions.
4
Classify the proof
The hadith is classified as ahad in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but has strong acceptance due to other supporting evidence.
In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith are binding in practice if accepted by the majority of scholars.
5
Understand the authority level
This ruling is the mufta bihi (operative) position of the Hanafi school, part of zahir al-riwayah from the early Imams.
Some early reports mention eight rak'ahs, but the relied-upon position is twenty based on the hadith and Companion practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۵۳) اور تراویح دس سلام سے بیس رکعت ہیں۔
تشریح : تراویح دو دو رکعت کر کے پڑھے ، اور دس سلام کے ساتھ بیس رکعتیں پڑھے۔
وجه : بیس رکعت تراویح کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے(۱)۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي ع يصلي في شهر رمضان عشرين ركعة والوتر - (طبراني الكبیر، باب مقسم عن ابن عباس ، ج حادی عشر، ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۱۲۱۰۲ رسنن سبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی
Translation: (653) And Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs with ten salams. Explanation: Tarawih should be prayed in twos, and with ten salams, twenty rak'ahs are prayed. Proof: The proof for twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih is this hadith (1): From Ibn 'Abbas: He said the Prophet used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan. (Tabarani, Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage gives the final ruling on the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih: twenty rak'ahs prayed in sets of two, with a salam after each set, totaling ten salams. The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas stating that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed twenty rak'ahs plus Witr in Ramadan. This is the established position of the Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Companions and the Imams.

Key Terms
تسليمات (taslimat): The number of salams (concluding the prayer) given after each pair of rak'ahs.
تراويح (tarawih): The special night prayers performed in Ramadan, derived from 'tarwih' (rest).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many rak'ahs and salams are there in Tarawih according to the Hanafi school?
A) Eight rak'ahs with four salams
B) Twenty rak'ahs with ten salams
C) Twenty rak'ahs with five salams
D) Thirty-six rak'ahs with eighteen salams

Key Takeaway
Tarawih in the Hanafi school is twenty rak'ahs with ten salams, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the consensus of the Companions.

Rulings on Tarawih Prayer: Timing and Number of Rak'ahs
Explains rulings on Tarawih timing, Witr relation, and number of rak'ahs with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs for Tarawih, explain the recommended timing, and identify the evidence used by the school.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs with 10 salams, prayed after Isha, best delayed to mid-night, with Witr after.

This lesson examines the key rulings on Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school. You will learn the recommended timing, the relationship with Witr, and the foundational proofs for 20 rak'ahs. We will also address the common misunderstanding that Tarawih is only 8 rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three core rulings
The passage covers timing, Witr order, and the number of rak'ahs. Note each ruling as you read.
2
Understand the recommended timing
It is mustahabb to delay Tarawih to one-third or half of the night. Evidence is given from Aisha and Abu Dharr hadiths.
Delay beyond half is not makruh according to the correct view.
3
Clarify the Witr relation
Tarawih is independent of Witr, but it is better to pray Witr after Tarawih because the hadith says Witr is the last prayer of the night.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs then Witr.
4
Examine the evidence for 20 rak'ahs
Primary evidence: hadith of Ibn Abbas, practice of Umar and Ali, and the statement of Imam al-Tirmidhi that most scholars agree on 20.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Refute the opposing view
The hadith of Aisha (11 rak'ahs) is about Tahajjud, not Tarawih. The major hadith scholars placed it in Tahajjud chapters.
This distinction is crucial for the Hanafi argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التراويح
الـوتـر عـلـى التراويح وتأخيره عنها (۶۵۲) و يستحبّ تاخير التراويح الى ثلث الليل او نصفه ولا یکره تاخيرها الى ما بعده على الصحيح (۶۵۳) وهى عشرون ركعة بعشر تسليمات. تشریح : تراویح وتر کے تابع نہیں ہے اس لئے تراویح کو وتر سے پہلے بھی پڑھ سکتے ہیں اور بعد میں بھی ، البتہ وتر کو تراویح کے بعد پڑھنا بہتر ہے، کیونکہ وتر کے بارے میں حدیث ہے کہ وہ رات کی آخری نماز ہو۔
وجه : اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ وتر بعد میں پڑھے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي عله يصلي في شهر رمضان عشرين ركعة والوتر - (طبراني الكبير، باب مقسم عن ابن عباس، ج حادی عشر، ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۱۲۱۰۲ سنن سبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان، ج ثانی ،ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۱۵ رمصنف ابن ابی شیبیۃ ، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعتہ ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر (۷۶۹ ) عشرین رکعتہ والوتر ، سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ وتر بعد میں پڑھے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۲) اور تراویح کو تہائی رات تک یا آدھی رات تک مؤخر کر نا مستحب ہے، اور صحیح روایت میں اس کے بعد بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد ہے، لیکن مستحب یہ ہے کہ تہائی رات تک مؤخر کرے، یا آدھی رات تک مؤخر کرے۔اور اس کے بعد بھی مؤخر کرے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جب نمازی کو نشاط ہوورنہ عشاء کے فورا بعد تراویح شروع کرے وجه : (ا) ان عائشة اخبرته ان رسول الله الا الله خرج ليلة من جوف الليل فصلي في المسجد وصلى رجال بصلاته ( بخاری شریف، باب فضل من قام رمضان، ص ۱۳۲۲، نمبر ۲۰۱۲ مسلم شریف ، باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وهو التراویح ، ص ۱۳۰۸، نمبر ۷۶۱ (۱۷۸۴) اس حدیث میں جوف اللیل سے اشارہ ہے کہ تراویح رات کے درمیانی حصے میں پڑھی ۔ (۲) اور سحری سے پہلے پہلے تک مؤخر کر سکتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ذر قال : صمنا مع رسول الله الا الله رمضان فلم يقم بنا شيئا من الشهر .... فلما كانت الثالثة جمع أهله و نسائه و الناس فقام بنا حتى خشينا أن يفوتنا الفلاح ، قال قلت : ما الفلاح ؟ قال السحور ، ثم لم يقم بنا بقية الشهر - (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی قیام شهر رمضان ، ص ۲۰۵، نمبر ۱۳۷۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سحری تک تراویح پڑھتے رہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ سحری تک وقت ہے۔ لغت: ثلث اللیل، ونصفہ : تہائی رات یعنی دس بجے رات تک، اور آدھی رات یعنی بارہ بجے رات تک مؤخر کرے۔ ترجمه : (۶۵۳) اور تراویح دس سلام سے بیس رکعت ہیں۔
تشریح : تراویح دو دو رکعت کر کے پڑھے ، اور دس سلام کے ساتھ بیس رکعتیں پڑھے۔ وجه : بیس رکعت تراویح کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے(۱)۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي ع يصلي في شهر رمضان عشرين ركعة والوتر - (طبراني الكبیر، باب مقسم عن ابن عباس ، ج حادی عشر، ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۱۲۱۰۲ رسنن سبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان ، ج ثانی ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۱۵ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر (۷۶۹ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نہیں رکعتیں تراویح پڑھتے تھے۔ (۲) ان عــمــر بـن خطاب امر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، ۶۷۷ کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۷۶۸ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قیام رمضان ، ج رابع ص ۲۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۶۰) اس حدیث اور عمل صحابہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح کی نماز میں رکھتیں ہیں۔ (۳) ان عليا أمر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة . ) مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۶۷۷ کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۵ نمبر ۷۶۸۰ رسن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان ج ثانی ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۲۰ ) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ حضرت علی نہیں رکعتیں تراویح پڑھنے کا حکم دیا کرتے تھے۔ (۴) امام ترندی نے فرمایا کہ اہل مدینہ کی ایک رائے ہے کہ اہم رکعتیں تراویح پڑھے، البتہ امام شافعی کا مسلک یہ بیان فرمایا کہ وہ ہیں رکعتیں پڑھنے کے قائل ہیں۔ ترمذی شریف کی عبارت یہ ہے۔ و اختلف اهل العلم في قيام رمضان ، فرأى بعضهم
الله
أن يصلى احدى و اربعين ركعة مع الوتر ، و هو قول أهل المدينة ، و العمل على هذا عندهم بالمدينة وأكثر اهل العلم على ما روى عن علی و عمر و غيرهما من أصحاب النبي علي عشرين ركعة و هو قول سفيان الثورى و ابن المبارک و الشافعي ، و قال الشافعى و هكذا أدركت ببلدنا بمكة يصلون عشرين ركعة . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى قيام شهر رمضان ۲۰۱، نمبر ۸۰۶) اس عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام شافعی کا مسلک بھی یہی ہے کہ تراویح بیس رکعتیں پڑھی جائے۔
نوٹ: (۱) حضرت عائشہ کی ایک حدیث ہے جس سے یہ استدلال کرتے ہیں کہ تراویح کی نماز صرف آٹھ رکعتیں ہیں لیکن اس حدیث سے استدلال کرنا اسلئے صحیح نہیں ہے کہ امام بخاری، امام مسلم، امام ابو داود اور امام ترمذی نے اس حدیث کو حضور کے تہجد کے باب میں نقل کیا ہے ، جس کا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ یہ حضرات اس حدیث کو تہجد کے ساتھ خاص مانتے تھے کہ آپ مسجد میں آٹھ رکعتیں
صلى الله
پڑھا کرتے تھے تراویح میں نہیں۔ (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ سأل عائشة كيف كانت صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رمضان ؟
فقالت : ما كان رسول الله الله يزيد في رمضان و لا في غيره على احدى عشرة ركعة ، يصلى اربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ، ثم يصلى ثلاثا . ) بخاری شریف، باب قیام النبی ل بالليل في رمضان و غیره ، ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۱۱۴۷ر مسلم شریف ، باب صلوۃ اللیل وعدد ركعات النبي الله في الليل وان الوتر ركعته ،ص ۲۹۹، نمبر ۱۷۲۳٫۷۳۸ /ابو داود شریف، باب فی صلوۃ اللیل، ص ۱۹۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۱/ ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی وصف صلوة النبي ع باليل ص ۹۹ نمبر ۴۳۹) سیہ حدیث مسلم شریف ، ابوداود شریف ، ترمذی شریف میں صرف تہجد کے باب میں ذکر فرمایا ہے تراویح کے باب میں ذکر نہیں فرمایا جسکا
Chapter on Tarawih. Witr is [considered] before Tarawih and delaying it from it? [652] And it is recommended to delay Tarawih to one-third of the night or half of it, and it is not disliked to delay it beyond that according to the correct view [653]. And it is twenty rak'ahs with ten salams. Commentary: Tarawih is not dependent on Witr; therefore, Tarawih can be prayed before Witr or after it. However, it is better to pray Witr after Tarawih, because there is a hadith about Witr that it is the last prayer of the night. Reasoning: This hadith indicates that Witr should be prayed later. (Hadith) from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan.' (Al-Tabrani, Al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Shayba) This shows that Witr is prayed after. Translation [652]: It is recommended to delay Tarawih to one-third of the night or till half of the night, and in the correct narration it is not disliked even after that. Commentary: The time for Tarawih is after Isha, but it is recommended to delay it to one-third or half of the night. And if he delays beyond that, it is not disliked. However, this is when the worshiper has energy; otherwise he should begin Tarawih immediately after Isha. Reasoning: (a) Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out in the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque, and men prayed with him. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith points to praying Tarawih in the middle of the night. (b) And he can delay it until before suhur. The evidence is the hadith of Abu Dharr: 'We fasted with the Messenger of Allah in Ramadan, and he did not lead us in prayer at all during the month...' until he gathered his family, women, and the people and led them until we feared we would miss 'Al-Falah' (meaning suhur), and then he did not lead us for the rest of the month. (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that Tarawih is prayed until suhur. Lexicon: 'Thulth al-layl' and 'nisfuhu': one-third of the night means delaying until 10 pm, and half the night means until 12 pm. Translation [653]: And Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs with ten salams. Commentary: Tarawih is prayed in sets of two rak'ahs, with ten salams making twenty rak'ahs. Reasoning: The evidence for twenty rak'ahs is: (1) The hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet used to pray 20 rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan. (2) Umar ibn al-Khattab ordered a man to lead them in 20 rak'ahs. (3) Ali ordered a man to lead them in 20 rak'ahs. (4) Imam al-Tirmidhi said: 'The people of knowledge differed about Qiyam Ramadan. Some saw it as 41 rak'ahs with Witr, which is the saying of the people of Medina, and the practice there. But most scholars hold what is narrated from 'Ali, 'Umar, and others among the Companions: twenty rak'ahs. This is the saying of Sufyan al-Thawri, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i said: 'This is what I found in our land, Makkah: they pray twenty rak'ahs.'' (Al-Tirmidhi) This indicates that Imam al-Shafi'i's madhhab is also that Tarawih should be twenty rak'ahs. Note: (1) There is a hadith of Aisha which some use to argue that Tarawih is only eight rak'ahs, but this inference is incorrect because Imam Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi placed this hadith in the chapter of Tahajjud, meaning they considered it specific to Tahajjud, not Tarawih. The hadith is: 'I asked Aisha: How was the prayer of the Messenger of Allah in Ramadan? She said: He would not pray more than eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan or out of it. He would pray four - do not ask about their beauty and length - then three.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) Indeed, this hadith is mentioned in the chapters of Tahajjud, not Tarawih.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on Tarawih prayer from the Hanafi perspective. It begins by clarifying the relation between Tarawih and Witr: Tarawih is not dependent on Witr, so it may be performed before or after, but it is better to pray Witr after Tarawih because the Prophet said 'Witr is the last prayer of the night.' The author then provides evidence from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs and then Witr. Next, the recommended time for Tarawih is discussed: it is mustahabb to delay Tarawih until one-third or half of the night, and according to the correct view, it is not makruh to delay further. Evidence is given from the hadith of Aisha about praying in the middle of the night and from Abu Dharr praying until suhur. The author notes that if the worshiper lacks energy, he should pray earlier. Finally, the number of rak'ahs is confirmed as twenty, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the practice of Umar and Ali, and the consensus of many scholars including Imam al-Shafi'i. A note refutes those who claim eight rak'ahs from Aisha's hadith, explaining that hadith is about Tahajjud, not Tarawih, as the major hadith collectors placed it in the Tahajjud chapters.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): The night prayer performed in congregation during the nights of Ramadan.
الوتر (al-witr): The witr prayer is a single rak'ah (or three) closing the night prayers; considered wajib in Hanafi school.
ثُلُث الليل (thulth al-layl): The first third of the night (approximately until 10 pm according to the text).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the recommended time for Tarawih?
A) Immediately after Isha
B) After Fajr
C) After one-third of the night
D) Before Maghrib

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, best delayed to mid-night, with Witr after, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of the Companions.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Number of Rak'ahs in Tarawih Prayer (20 Rak'ahs)
Establishes the Hanafi ruling of 20 rak'ahs for Tarawih with proofs and refutes the 8-rak'ah claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih, identify the key proofs (dalil naqli) from the practice of the Sahaba, and refute the 8-rak'ah claim using hadith classification.

Core Idea
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs based on Sahaba practice; the Aisha hadith refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih.

This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that Tarawih prayer consists of twenty rak'ahs. You will learn the primary proofs from the actions of Umar and Ali, the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, and the refutation of the 8-rak'ah claim using the chapter headings of major hadith collections. The discussion clarifies the distinction between Tarawih and Tahajjud, two distinct night prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih
Identify that the Hanafi school holds Tarawih as a sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs, prayed in pairs of two with brief rests after every four.
This is the mufta bihi position with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the primary dalil naqli
Cite the reports from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and other sources: the command of Umar ibn al-Khattab and Ali ibn Abi Talib for twenty rak'ahs, and the Prophet's own practice according to one report.
The text also cites Tirmidhi's statement that the majority of scholars, including al-Shafi'i, follow twenty.
3
Examine the opposing claim from Aisha's hadith
Understand that some scholars argue for eight rak'ahs based on the hadith that the Prophet prayed only eleven rak'ahs (eight + three witr) in Ramadan.
This hadith appears in Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
4
Apply the Hanafi response using hadith classification
Note that all major muhaddithin except Bukhari placed this hadith in the chapter on Tahajjud, not Tarawih. Even Bukhari's Tarawih chapter version describes praying four rak'ahs together, which contradicts the two-by-two method of Tarawih.
This indicates the hadith is about the Prophet's private night prayer, not the congregational Tarawih.
5
Reconcile the narrations using al-Bayhaqi's approach
Present al-Bayhaqi's reconciliation: the Companions would first pray eleven rak'ahs for Tahajjud, then later pray twenty rak'ahs for Tarawih, and then pray witr with three.
This shows both practices coexisted, with separate times and purposes.

فصل في التراويح
عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان، ج ثانی ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۱۵ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۷۶۹ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور بیس رکعتیں تراویح پڑھتے تھے۔ (۲) ان عمر بن خطاب امر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۷۶۸ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قیام رمضان، ج رابع ص ۲۰۰ نمبر ۷۷۶۰) اس حدیث اور عمل صحابہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح کی نماز بیس رکعتیں ہیں۔ (۳) ان عليا أمر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة، باب کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۵ نمبر ۷۶۸۰ رسن للبیھقی، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان ج ثانی ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۲۰) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ حضرت علی بیس رکعتیں تراویح پڑھنے کا حکم دیا کرتے تھے۔ (۴) امام ترمذی نے فرمایا کہ اہل مدینہ کی ایک رائے ہے کہ ایکتالیس رکعتیں تراویح پڑھے، البتہ امام شافعی کا مسلک یہ بیان فرمایا کہ وہ بیس رکعتیں پڑھنے کے قائل ہیں۔ ترمذی شریف کی عبارت یہ ہے: و اختلف اهل العلم في قيام رمضان، فرأى بعضهم أن يصلى احدى و اربعين ركعة مع الوتر، و هو قول أهل المدينة، و العمل على هذا عندهم بالمدينة وأكثر اهل العلم على ما روى عن علی و عمر و غيرهما من أصحاب النبي علي عشرين ركعة و هو قول سفيان الثورى و ابن المبارک و الشافعي، و قال الشافعى و هكذا أدركت ببلدنا بمكة يصلون عشرين ركعة (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى قيام شهر رمضان ۲۰۱، نمبر ۸۰۶) اس عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام شافعی کا مسلک بھی یہی ہے کہ تراویح بیس رکعتیں پڑھی جائے۔

میں آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھتے تھے (۲) اس حدیث سے بھی اسکی تائید ہوتی ہے: عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي لا يصلى من الليل ثمان ركعات و يوتر بثلاث (طبرانی کبیر، باب یکی بن وثاب عن ابن عباس، ج ثانی عشر، ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۱۲۶۹۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تہجد کی نماز حضور آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھتے تھے۔ (۳) صرف امام بخاری نے اس حدیث کو تراویح کے باب میں بھی ذکر فرمایا ہے، اور تہجد کے باب میں بھی ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ تہجد کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے۔ (۴) اس حدیث میں تذکرہ ہے کہ آپ چار رکعتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے جن کے حسن کا کیا کہنا۔ اور تراویح کی نماز ایک ساتھ چار رکعت نہیں ہوتی۔ بلکہ دو دو رکعت کر کے ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے وہ حدیث تراویح رمضان میں بھی پہلے تہجد کی نماز آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھتے ہوں گے، ان کے بعد تراویح کی بیس رکعتیں پڑھتے تھے۔
Section on Tarawih. The number of rak'ahs for standing in prayer in the month of Ramadan: (reference) from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on how many to pray in Ramadan, that from this hadith it is known that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih. (2) That Umar ibn al-Khattab commanded a man to lead them in twenty rak'ahs... From this hadith and the practice of the Companions, it is known that Tarawih prayer is twenty rak'ahs. (3) That Ali commanded a man to lead them in twenty rak'ahs... In this report also, that Ali used to command praying twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih. (4) Imam Tirmidhi said that the people of Medina had a view that forty-one rak'ahs are prayed, but he explained that Imam al-Shafi'i's madhhab is that he believes in twenty rak'ahs. The text of Tirmidhi is: 'The scholars differed concerning Qiyam Ramadan. Some saw that one should pray forty-one rak'ahs with Witr, and that is the saying of the people of Medina, and the practice there is upon that. But most scholars follow what has been narrated from Ali, Umar, and others of the Prophet's companions, i.e., twenty rak'ahs, and that is the saying of Sufyan al-Thawri, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i said: Thus I found in my city, Mecca, they pray twenty rak'ahs.' From this text it is known that Imam al-Shafi'i's madhhab is also that Tarawih should be twenty rak'ahs. Note: (1) There is a hadith of Aisha which some use to argue that Tarawih is only eight rak'ahs, but using this hadith as proof is not correct because Imam Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi all narrated this hadith in the chapter on Tahajjud of the Prophet, meaning that these scholars understood it specifically for Tahajjud, that he used to pray eight rak'ahs in the mosque, not in Tarawih. The hadith is: 'Aisha was asked how the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was in Ramadan. She said: The Messenger of Allah did not increase in Ramadan or other than it beyond eleven rak'ahs. He would pray four—do not ask about their beauty and length—then he would pray three.' (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's night prayer in Ramadan and otherwise, p.183 no.1147; Muslim, chapter on night prayer and the number of rak'ahs...). This hadith in Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi is only mentioned in the chapter on Tahajjud, not in the chapter on Tarawih. This means that the Prophet used to pray eight rak'ahs in Tahajjud. (2) This is also supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet would not pray at night more than eight rak'ahs and would pray witr with three.' (Tabarani al-Kabir...). From this hadith it is also known that Tahajjud prayer was eight rak'ahs. (3) Only Imam Bukhari narrated this hadith also in the chapter on Tarawih, as well as in the chapter on Tahajjud. The hadith in the chapter on Tarawih is: 'Aisha was asked how the prayer of the Messenger of Allah was in Ramadan. She said: He did not increase in Ramadan or other than it beyond eleven rak'ahs. He would pray four—do not ask about their beauty and length—then he would pray four—do not ask about their beauty and length—then he would pray three.' (Bukhari, chapter on the virtue of one who stands in Ramadan, p.322 no.2013). So Imam Bukhari mentioned this eight-rak'ah hadith in the chapter on Qiyam Ramadan, i.e., Tarawih. (4) In this hadith, it is mentioned that he used to pray four rak'ahs together, how beautiful they are! But Tarawih prayer is not prayed four together; rather, it is prayed two by two. Therefore, this hadith is not about Tarawih but about Tahajjud. (5) Sunan al-Bayhaqi reconciled the two narrations in that they would first pray eleven rak'ahs of Tahajjud, then they would pray twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih and pray Witr with three. His statement is: 'It is possible to reconcile the narrations: they used to stand (pray) eleven (for Tahajjud), then they would stand (pray) twenty (for Tarawih) and pray Witr with three.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what has been narrated concerning the number of rak'ahs of standing in prayer in the month of Ramadan, vol.2 p.699 no.4618). From this it is known that in Ramadan, they would first pray Tahajjud (eight rak'ahs) and then after that pray the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the Hanafi position that Tarawih prayer consists of twenty rak'ahs. The author begins by citing multiple sources from hadith collections and the practice of the Rightly-Guided Caliphs: a hadith indicating the Prophet himself prayed twenty rak'ahs, the command of Umar ibn al-Khattab to pray twenty, and the command of Ali ibn Abi Talib. Then he quotes Tirmidhi's summary showing that the majority of scholars, including Imam al-Shafi'i, hold this position, though the people of Medina followed a practice of forty-one rak'ahs (including Witr). The author then addresses a common objection—the hadith of Aisha which reports the Prophet prayed only eleven rak'ah in Ramadan (interpreted as eight Tarawih plus three Witr by some). He refutes this by demonstrating that the leading hadith scholars placed this report in the chapter of Tahajjud (voluntary night prayer), not Tarawih, indicating it refers to a separate supererogatory prayer. He further supports this with the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed eight rak'ah at night for Tahajjud. He notes that only Bukhari also placed it in the Tarawih chapter, but points out that the description of praying four rak'ah at a time contradicts the method of Tarawih, which is prayed in two-rak'ah units. Finally, he presents al-Bayhaqi's reconciliation: the Companions would pray eleven rak'ah for Tahajjud and then twenty for Tarawih, each at different times. Thus, the ruling of twenty rak'ah for Tarawih is firmly established as the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarāwīḥ): The special night prayer performed during the month of Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
تہجد (tahajjud): The voluntary night prayer performed after waking from sleep, distinguished from Tarawih in this text.
قيام رمضان (qiyām ramaḍān): Literally 'standing in Ramadan', often used synonymously with Tarawih in hadith literature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many rak'ahs constitute the Tarawih prayer in Ramadan?
A) 8 rak'ahs
B) 20 rak'ahs
C) 11 rak'ahs
D) 36 rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school firmly holds that Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, based on the practice of the Sahaba and the majority of scholars; the hadith of Aisha is understood to refer to Tahajjud.

The Recommended Rest (Tarwihah) in Tarawih Prayer
States the recommended rest in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sitting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih and identify its legal status as mustahabb.

Core Idea
Resting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih is mustahabb, not wajib.

This lesson covers a specific recommended practice during Tarawih prayer: the brief rest known as tarwihah. Understanding that it is mustahabb helps avoid overburdening oneself or thinking it is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is sitting/resting after every four rak'ahs of Tarawih, and also between the fifth tarwihah and witr.
2
Identify the ruling
The text uses 'yustaḥabbu' (it is recommended), indicating the ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
Mustahabb is a level below sunnah muakkadah.
3
Understand the practice
Twenty rak'ahs are prayed in ten salams (two rak'ahs each). After every four rak'ahs (two sets), a rest is taken. This rest is called tarwihah.
The rest is for a duration similar to the time taken to pray four rak'ahs.
4
Distinguish status from wajib
Omitting this rest does not invalidate the prayer. It is a recommended, not obligatory, action.
No compensation (like sajdah sahw) is needed if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحبّ الجلوس بعد كل اربع بقدرها وكذا بين الترويحة الخامسة والوتر.
ترجمه: (۶۵۴) اور ہر چار رکعت پر اسی کے بقدر بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ اسی طرح پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بیٹھنا بھی مستحب ہے۔
تشریح: بیس رکعتیں دس سلام سے پڑھے اور دو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیرے۔ اور ہر چار رکعت کے بعد آرام کرے، جس کو ترویحہ کہتے ہیں، اور وتر اور پانچویں ترویحہ کے درمیان بھی آرام کرے۔
It is recommended to sit after every four (rak'ahs) for the duration of them, and likewise between the fifth tarwihah and witr. Translation: (654) And sitting after every four rak'ahs for a period equal to them is mustahabb. Similarly, sitting between the fifth tarwihah and witr is also mustahabb. Explanation: He prays twenty rak'ahs with ten salams, and he turns (makes salam) after every two rak'ahs. And after every four rak'ahs, he rests, which is called tarwihah, and he also rests between witr and the fifth tarwihah.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the recommended (mustahabb) actions during Tarawih prayer. The author first gives the Arabic text: 'It is recommended to sit after every four (rak'ahs) for a duration similar to them, and likewise between the fifth tarwihah and witr.' Then the Urdu translation and explanation. The explanation clarifies that the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih are prayed in ten salams (i.e., ten units of two rak'ahs each, with a salam after each two). After each set of four rak'ahs (which comprises two units of two rak'ahs), the worshipper should rest for a time equal to the time taken to pray those four rak'ahs. This rest is called tarwihah (plural tarawih). Additionally, a rest should be taken between the fifth tarwihah (which covers the last four rak'ahs, from the 17th to the 20th) and the witr prayer. The ruling is explicit that these rests are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory, so omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but is contrary to the ideal practice.

Key Terms
ترويحة (tarwīḥah): The short rest taken after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended; an action that is encouraged but not obligatory. Its omission does not require compensation.
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer (e.g., three rak'ahs) performed after Tarawih and Tahajjud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Resting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih is a recommended (mustahabb) practice, not obligatory, and includes a rest between the fifth tarwihah and witr.

The Recommended Sitting Intervals in Tarawih
Ruling on recommended sitting in Tarawih prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih and identify the proofs that establish its recommended status.

Core Idea
Sitting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih is mustahabb, not wajib — a rest to refresh the soul.

This passage addresses a structural element of Tarawih prayer: the intervals of rest known as tarweehah. While many focus on the number of rak'ahs, the Hanafi school emphasizes the recommended pauses that give the congregation ease. Understanding this ruling clarifies that the rests are a sunnah, not an obligation, and that their length is flexible.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon: sitting after every four rak'ahs and between the fifth tarweehah and witr. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
The text explicitly says 'yustahabb'.
2
Identify the number of rak'ahs
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs in 10 salams, two rak'ahs each. The rests occur after every two pairs (four rak'ahs).
The passage clarifies performing two rak'ahs at a time.
3
Analyze the proofs
The proofs include the Prophet's practice (hadith from Aisha: he prayed four rak'ahs then rested) and the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (he gave a rest as long as going to Sala').
These are dalil naqli with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the purpose
The rest (tarweehah) is to prevent hardship and allow refreshment. Its duration is flexible; the example of Umar indicates a moderate pause.
The purpose is not ritual but practical ease.
5
Distinguish fard vs mustahabb
Missing this sitting does not invalidate the prayer, nor is compensation required. It is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation.
This is a common point of confusion.

مطلب يہ ہے کہ حضور تہجد میں آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھتے تھے (۲) اس حدیث سے بھی اسکی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي لا يصلى من الليل ثمان ركعات و يوتر بثلاث۔ (طبرانی کبیر، باب یکی بن وثاب عن ابن عباس، ج ثانی عشر، ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۱۲۶۹۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تہجد کی نماز حضور آٹھ رکعتیں پڑھتے تھے۔ (۳) صرف امام بخاری نے اس حدیث کو تراویح کے باب میں بھی ذکر فرمایا ہے، اور تہجد کے باب میں بھی ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ تہجد کے بارے میں بخاری کی اوپر حدیث گزر چکی اور تراویح کے بارے میں حدیث کا باب یہ ہے۔ سأل عائشة كيف كانت صلوة رسول الله في رمضان؟ فقالت: ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا في غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة، يصلـى أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن، ثم يصلى أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلى ثلاثا. تشریح: بیس رکھتیں دس سلام سے پڑھے اور دو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیرے۔ اور ہر چار رکعت کے بعد آرام کرے، جسکو "ترویجہ" کہتے ہیں، اور وتر اور پانچویں ترویحہ کے درمیان بھی آرام کرے۔

Section on Tarawih: (654) Recommended is to sit after every four (rak'ahs) for the same duration, and similarly between the fifth tarweehah and witr. 

Request: The Prophet used to pray eight rak'ahs in tahajjud, and this hadith also supports it. ... Translation: (654) And sitting after every four rak'ahs for the same duration is recommended. Similarly, sitting between the fifth tarweehah and witr is also recommended. 

Clarification: He should pray twenty rak'ahs with ten salams, and make salam after every two rak'ahs. And after every four rak'ahs he should rest, which is called 'tarweehah', and also rest between witr and the fifth tarweehah. 

Proof: (1) The proof for praying two rak'ahs at a time is the practice of a Companion: ... (2) The proof for sitting after every four rak'ahs is the hadith: ... (3) The practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab indicates resting briefly between two tarweehahs so that people are not distressed.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the recommended (mustahabb) sitting intervals during Tarawih prayer. The author states that after every four rak'ahs, one should sit for approximately the same duration as the four rak'ahs. Similarly, one should sit between the fifth tarweehah and the witr prayer. The explanation clarifies that Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs performed in pairs (two rak'ahs each with a salam), making ten salams. After every two pairs (four rak'ahs), a rest is taken, called 'tarweehah'. The proofs provided include the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Aisha, the practice of Abu Hurairah as observed by a Companion, and the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab who would give a rest long enough for a person to go from the mosque to the area of Sala'. These all support the recommended nature of these rests.

Key Terms
ترویحہ (tarweehah): The rest interval between sets of four rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer.
مستحب (mustahabb): An action recommended but not obligatory; performing it earns reward, omitting it does not incur sin.

Completing the Qur'an Once in Tarawih: Sunnah, Not Wajib
Ruling on completing the Qur'an during Tarawih in a month

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Qur'an during Tarawih (sunnah mu'akkadah) and explain the two proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Completing the Qur'an in Tarawih is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, based on prophetic guidance and caliphal practice.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the recitation in Tarawih prayers. Many assume that completing the entire Qur'an during Ramadan is obligatory, but the correct position is that it is a confirmed Sunnah. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning that leads to this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is completing the Qur'an (khatm) during Tarawih over the entire month. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed recommended).
The word 'sunn' in Arabic indicates a sunnah, not a wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet advised reciting the Quran in a month. (2) The practice of Umar ibn Abdul Aziz ordering ten verses per rak'ah in Ramadan.
Both are from zanni al-thubut hadith and athar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith gives a general recommendation for monthly completion; the practice shows how to apply it in Tarawih. Together they indicate sunnah, not wujub.
The imperative in the hadith is interpreted as nadb (recommendation) due to context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may consider it mustahabb or even wajib. Within the Hanafi school, the correct view is sunnah.
The text explicitly says 'ala al-sahih (on the correct view).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is sunnah because the evidence supports recommendation, not obligation.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦٥٥) وسُنَّ ختم القرآن فيها مرة في الشهر على الصحيح.

ترجمه: (۶۵۵) اور تراویح میں ایک بار قرآن مجید مہینہ بھر میں ختم کرنا سیدھی روایت پر سنت ہے۔

تشریح: پورے مہینے کی تراویح میں ایک قرآن ختم کرنا سنت ہے۔

وجه: (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر قال قال لي رسول الله اقرأ القرآن في شهر قلت اني اجد قوة قال فاقرأه في سبع و لا تزد على ذلك۔ (بخاری شریف، باب فی کم یقرأ القرآن، ص ۹۰۵ نمبر ۱٫۵۰۵۴ ابوداود شریف، باب فی کم پورا القرآن، ص ۲۰۸، نمبر ۱۳۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک ماہ میں قرآن ختم کرنا چاہیے۔

(۲) كان عمر بن عبد العزيز يأمر الذين يقرأون في رمضان في كل ركعة بعشر آيات عشر آيات۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب ۶۷۶ فی صلوۃ رمضان، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۴، نمبر ۷۶۷۵)
(655) And it is sunnah to complete the Qur'an in it (Tarawih) once in the month, according to the correct view.

Translation: (655) And completing the noble Qur'an once in the month in Tarawih is sunnah according to the sound narration.

Clarification: Completing the Qur'an once in the Tarawih of the entire month is sunnah.

Proof: (1) There is an indication in this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet said to him, 'Recite the Qur'an in a month.' I said, 'I find strength.' He said, 'Then recite it in seven and do not exceed that.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that one should complete the Qur'an in a month. (2) Umar ibn Abdul Aziz used to order those who recited in Ramadan to recite ten verses per rak'ah.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage states that it is a sunnah (recommended) to complete the entire Qur'an once during the Tarawih prayers of the month of Ramadan, according to the correct position in the Hanafi school. The commentary explains that 'once in the month' means over the whole month, not necessarily in one night. The proofs are: (1) The hadith where the Prophet advised Ibn Umar to complete the Qur'an in a month, which implies a general recommendation for monthly completion. (2) The practice of Umar ibn Abdul Aziz, who instructed reciters to recite ten verses per rak'ah, which would lead to a completion over the month if done consistently.

Key Terms
ختم القرآن (khatm al-Qur'an): Completing the recitation of the entire Qur'an.

Adjusting Recitation Length in Tarawih According to Congregation's Capacity
Ruling on recitation length when congregation is wearied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation length in Tarawih when the congregation is wearied, identify the proof from Umar's practice, and distinguish the chosen view from potential alternatives.

Core Idea
The imam should recite an amount that does not bore the congregation; Umar's directive is the sunnah practice.

In Tarawih prayers, the imam leads the congregation through many rak'ahs. The Hanafi school teaches that the imam must consider the congregation's capacity and avoid causing hardship or boredom. This lesson examines the ruling from a key Hanafi text, which bases its position on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab. You will learn the preferred view (mukhtar) and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the condition
The passage states: if the people are annoyed (malla) by the recitation, the imam should recite to the extent that they are not bored. The condition is the congregation's discomfort.
The Arabic word 'malla' implies a sense of weariness or aversion.
2
Examine the proof (athar from Umar)
The author cites an athar from Abu Uthman: Umar ibn al-Khattab instructed reciters in Ramadan to recite thirty verses for fast reciters, twenty-five for medium, and twenty for slow reciters. This shows the flexibility in recitation length.
This is a sunnah action of a companion, which Hanafis consider a source of proof.
3
Understand the calculation of verses
The commentary calculates that if a slow reciter recites twenty verses per rak'ah, in twenty rak'ahs that totals four hundred verses per day, and over thirty days twelve thousand verses, which is roughly twice the number of verses in the Qur'an.
The calculation shows that the guideline allows for complete recitation multiple times, emphasizing flexibility.
4
Note the authority weight
The text says 'according to the chosen view' (على المختار), indicating that this is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The term 'mukhtar' is a technical term in Hanafi fiqh for the preferred opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦٥٦) وان ملّ به القوم قرأ بقدر ما [لا يملون] على المختار.

ترجمه: (۶۵۶) اگر قوم آزردہ ہوتی ہو تو اتنا پڑھے جس سے ان کو باعث نفرت نہ ہو، مختار روایت میں۔

تشریح: قوم کو پریشانی ہوتی ہو تو تراویح کی ہر رکعت میں اتنی آیتیں پڑھے جن سے ان کو نفرت نہ ہو مختار روایت یہی ہے، چنانچہ حضرت عمر تیز پڑھنے والوں سے دس آیتیں اور اوسط پڑھنے والے سے پچیس آیتیں، اور آہستہ پڑھنے والے سے بیس آیتیں پڑھنے کے لئے کہتے تھے۔

وجه: (۱) عن أبي عثمان قال: دعا عمر القراء في رمضان فأمر أسرعهم قراءة أن يقرأ ثلاثين آية و الوسط خمسا وعشرين آية و البطىء عشرين آية۔ (مصنف ابن ابي شبيبة، باب ۶۷۶ فی صلوۃ رمضان، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۴، نمبر ۶۷۱ے رسن بیھقی، باب قدر قراء تھم فی قیام شھر رمضان، ج ثانی، ص ۷۰۰، نمبر ۴۶۲۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ سست پڑھنے والے کو بھی بیس آیتیں پڑھنے کے لئے کہتے تھے۔ اب ہر رکعت میں بیس آیتیں پڑھے تو ایک دن کی بیس رکعتوں میں چار سو آیتیں ہو نگیں اور تیس دنوں میں بارہ ہزار آیتیں ہونگیں۔ قرآن کریم میں ۶۲۳۶ آیتیں ہیں اسلئے بارہ ہزار کو ۶۲۳۶ سے تقسیم دیں تو پورے...
(656) And if the people are annoyed by it, he should recite to the extent that they are not bored, according to the chosen view.

Translation: (656) If the people become distressed, then he should recite such that it does not cause them aversion, in the chosen narration.

Clarification: If the people are distressed, then in each rak'ah of Tarawih he should recite such verses that do not cause them aversion; this is the chosen view. Thus, Umar used to order the fast reciters to recite thirty verses, the medium reciters twenty-five verses, and the slow reciters twenty verses.

Proof: (1) From Abu Uthman: Umar called the reciters in Ramadan and ordered the fastest among them to recite thirty verses, the medium twenty-five, and the slow twenty verses. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This athar indicates that even the slow reciter was told to recite twenty verses. Now, if he recites twenty verses per rak'ah, then in twenty rak'ahs per day that would be four hundred verses, and in thirty days twelve thousand verses. The Qur'an has 6236 verses, so dividing twelve thousand by 6236 gives...
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that the imam in Tarawih should adjust the length of recitation according to the capacity of the congregation, to avoid causing them boredom or hardship. The preferred view (mukhtar) is that the imam should recite an amount that does not annoy the people. The author provides the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab as proof: he would instruct different reciters according to their speed: fast reciters recite thirty verses per rak'ah, medium reciters twenty-five, and slow reciters twenty. The commentary then calculates that if a slow reciter recites twenty verses per rak'ah in twenty rak'ahs daily, that totals four hundred verses per day, and over thirty days twelve thousand verses, which is roughly twice the number of verses in the Qur'an, implying a complete recitation more than once. However, the main point is flexibility: the imam should not exceed the congregation's endurance.

Key Terms
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred view in the Hanafi school on this ruling.
ملّ (malla): To be annoyed, bored, or weary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10 verses
B) 20 verses
C) 25 verses
D) 30 verses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling requires the imam to recite an amount that does not bore the congregation, based on the sunnah of Umar.

Completing the Quran Once in Taraweeh
Ruling on completing Quran once in Taraweeh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Quran in Taraweeh and identify the primary dalil supporting it.

Core Idea
Completing the Quran once in Taraweeh is sunnah, not fard.

During Ramadan, many Muslims aim to complete the Quran in Taraweeh prayers. But is this a requirement or simply recommended? This lesson examines the Hanafi view that completing the Quran once in the month is a sunnah muakkadah, a confirmed practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and early Muslims. We will explore the evidence and clarify common misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is completing the entire Quran during the Taraweeh prayers of Ramadan. The Hanafi ruling states it is sunnah (recommended).
The source says 'وسُنَّ ختم القرآن فيها مرة فى الشهر على الصحيح'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) advised: 'Recite the Quran in a month.'
Hadith in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'in a month' indicates the desirability of monthly completion, which is applied to Taraweeh over the 29-30 days of Ramadan.
The Prophet allowed completing in 7 days for those with strength, but the basic recommendation is monthly.
4
Consider additional support
The practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, who instructed ten verses per rak'ah in Ramadan, leading to exactly one completion, reinforces the ruling.
This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Catch the common misunderstanding
Some assume completing once is obligatory; the ruling clearly states it is sunnah. Moreover, completing more than once is permissible.
The author says 'on the correct view' (على الصحيح), indicating this is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التراويح (۶۵۵) وسُنَّ ختم القرآن فيها مرة فى الشهر على الصحيح ترجمه : (۲۵۵) اور تراویح میں ایک تم قرآن مجید مینہ بھر میں کر ناسیح روایت پرست ہے۔ تشریح : پورے مہینے کی تراویح میں ایک قرآن ختم کرنا سنت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر قال قال لى رسول الله الله اقرأ القرآن في شهر قلت اني اجد قوة قال فاقرأه في سبع و لا تزد علی ذالک ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب فی کم یقرأ القرآن، ص ۹۰۵ نمبر ۱٫۵۰۵۴ ابوداود شریف ، باب فی کم پورا القرآن، ص ۲۰۸، نمبر ۱۳۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک ماہ میں قرآن ختم کرنا چاہیئے (۲)كـان عـمـر بـن عبـد الـعـزيـز يأمر الذين يقرأون في رمضان في كل ركعة بعشر آيات عشر آيات . ( مصنف ابن ابی شبیۃ ، باب ۶۷۶ فی صلوۃ رمضان ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۶۴، نمبر ۷۶۷۵ )
Chapter on Taraweeh. (655) It is sunnah to complete the Quran in it once in the month according to the correct view. Translation: (655) And in Taraweeh, to complete the Quran once in a month is sunnah according to the correct narration. Explanation: To complete one Quran in the Taraweeh of the whole month is sunnah. Evidence: (1) This hadith indicates it: From Abdullah ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me: 'Recite the Quran in a month.' I said: 'I find strength.' He said: 'Recite it in seven and do not exceed that.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This hadith states that completing the Quran in a month is recommended. (2) Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz used to order those who recited in Ramadan to recite ten verses in each rak'ah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is sunnah (recommended) to complete the entire Quran once during the Taraweeh prayers of Ramadan, according to the correct view in the Hanafi school. The author provides two pieces of evidence: first, a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) advised finishing the Quran in a month (not exceeding seven days as a maximum), which implies the desirability of monthly completion. Second, the practice of the caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, who instructed reciters to read ten verses per rak'ah in Ramadan, leading to exactly one completion over the month. This ruling is from the Hanafi madhhab and is considered sunnah muakkadah.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarāwīḥ): The supererogatory night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed, but not obligatory.
ختم القرآن (khatm al-Qur'ān): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory (fard) to complete the Quran once.
B) It is sunnah to complete the Quran once according to the correct view.
C) It is not sunnah at all; any amount is fine.
D) It is mustahabb to complete it twice.

Key Takeaway
Completing the Quran once in Taraweeh is a sunnah muakkadah, supported by the Prophet's advice and early Muslim practice, but not fard.

Recitation Length if Congregation Is Bored
Ruling on recitation length in Taraweeh considering congregation's comfort

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation length when the congregation is bored in Taraweeh and cite the evidence from Umar's practice.

Core Idea
The imam must adjust recitation to avoid aversion; the sunnah is flexibility, not fixed length.

This lesson addresses the imam's responsibility to consider the congregation's state during Taraweeh. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, teaches that the recitation should be shortened if the people become bored. The evidence shows that the imam should prioritize the congregation's comfort over a fixed number of verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Taraweeh recitation when the congregation is bored. The ruling is that the imam should recite as much as does not cause aversion, according to the chosen view.
The chosen view is 'fī al-mukhtār'.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab, who assigned different verse amounts to reciters: fast reciters 33 verses, medium 25, slow 20.
Thubut: zanni; dalala: zanni (but accepted as practice of a Caliph).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's assignment shows that the imam should adjust recitation based on the congregation's capacity, avoiding hardship.
Wajh: the different amounts indicate flexibility, not a fixed number.
4
Note the chosen view
The Hanafi mufta bihi is to shorten recitation if people dislike long ones.
Tarjih authority: the author states 'fī al-mukhtār'.
5
Apply the principle
In modern practice, the imam should observe the congregation and reduce recitation if they appear restless.
This applies to all congregational prayers, but particularly emphasized in Taraweeh.

This passage addresses the imam's consideration for the congregation during Taraweeh. Inviolable Acts in Taraweeh: Balancing Sunnah and Congregational Comfort
Ruling on omitting elements in Taraweeh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which elements of Taraweeh prayer are inviolable (cannot be omitted) and which may be omitted when accommodating a bored congregation, according to the Hanafi chosen view.

Core Idea
In Taraweeh, salawat, thana', and tasbih are never omitted; only du'a may be dropped to ease the congregation.

The Taraweeh prayer is a cherished sunnah, but sometimes the congregation grows weary. An imam faces a dilemma: preserve the full form or shorten it to keep people engaged. This passage from our text provides clear guidance from the Hanafi school on which elements are essential and which can be set aside for the sake of the congregation. It distinguishes between firmly established sunnah acts and optional ones, teaching us that not everything can be sacrificed for convenience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and the context
The ruling applies to Taraweeh prayer, a sunnah muakkadah performed in Ramadan. The specific context is when the congregation is bored or restless ('malla al-qawm').
This is not about excusing oneself from prayer altogether, but about permissible omissions within the prayer.
2
List the elements under discussion
The passage lists four elements: (1) salawat upon the Prophet in every tashahhud, (2) thana' (opening praise), (3) tasbih in ruku' and sujud, and (4) du'a in the final tashahhud.
These are parts of the prayer that some might consider dropping to shorten it.
3
Classify each element's ruling level
Using Hanafi terminology, determine if each is sunnah muakkadah or sunnah ghayr muakkadah. Salawat, thana', and tasbih are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). Du'a is sunnah ghayr muakkadah (non-emphasized sunnah).
The ruling level determines whether omission is permitted in this context.
4
Apply the ruling: which can be omitted?
The text states that salawat, thana', and tasbih are not to be omitted, even if the people are bored. The du'a may be omitted ('la ya'ti bi al-du'a in malla al-qawm').
The criterion is the importance of the act; inviolable ones are those that are strongly established.
5
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The commentary explains that salawat, thana', and tasbih are 'very important' (bohat aham hai), while du'a is 'not as important' (utni aham nahi hai). Thus, the principle is that only less critical sunnah acts may be dropped to ease the congregation.
This reflects the Hanafi approach of prioritizing the integrity of the prayer over minor convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۵۷) ولا يترك الصلوة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل تشهد منها ولو ملّ القوم على المختار ولا يترك الثناء وتسبيح الركوع والسجود ولا يأتى بالدعاء ان مل القوم ترجمه : (۶۵۷) اور ہر تشہد میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود بھیجنا نہ چھوڑے چاہے قوم رنجیدہ ہو، اور شا، اور رکوع کی تسبیح اور سجدے کی تسبیح نہ چھوڑے، اور قوم رنجیدہ ہوتی ہو تو دعا چھوڑ دے۔ تشریح : حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود شریف پڑھنا بہت اہم ہے، اسی طرح ثنا پڑھنا، اور رکوع اور سجدے کی تسبیح بہت اہم ہیں اس لئے چاہے قوم رنجیدہ ہوں انکو تر اویح میں نہ چھوڑے، البتہ تشہد میں جو دعا پڑھتے ہیں چاہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دے، کیونکہ یہ اتنی اہم نہیں ہے
(657) And he should not leave out salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) in every tashahhud of it, even if the people are bored, according to the chosen view. And he should not leave out thana' and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud. And he should not perform du'a if the people are bored. Translation: (657) And in every tashahhud, he should not omit sending salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), even if the people are displeased; and thana', and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud, he should not omit; and if the people are displeased, he should omit du'a. Explanation: Reciting salawat upon the Prophet is very important, similarly reciting thana' and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud are very important, so even if the people are displeased, he should not omit them in Taraweeh. However, the du'a recited in tashahhud, he may omit it if he wishes, because it is not as important.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage details what parts of the Taraweeh prayer are essential and may be omitted to accommodate a bored congregation. The ruling is that the imam should never omit the salawat on the Prophet (peace be upon him) in each tashahhud, nor the thana' (opening praise), nor the tasbih (glorification) in ruku' and sujud, even if the people are bored, according to the chosen view. However, the du'a (supplication) in tashahhud may be omitted if the congregation is restless. The reasoning is that salawat, thana', and tasbih are integral sunnah acts, while the du'a is not considered as essential.

Key Terms
ثناء (thanā'): The opening praise (subhanaka allahumma...) recited in prayer.
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): Glorification of Allah in ruku' and sujud, e.g., subhana rabbiyal azim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Salawat upon the Prophet in tashahhud
B) Thana' (opening praise)
C) Tasbih of ruku' and sujud
D) Du'a in tashahhud

Key Takeaway
In Taraweeh, salawat, thana', and tasbih are inviolable sunnah muakkadah; du'a is the only element that may be omitted to ease the congregation.

Missed Taraweeh Not Made Up
Ruling on making up missed Taraweeh prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed Taraweeh prayer and explain the proof from the hadith and the general principle that sunnah prayers are not made up.

Core Idea
Missed Taraweeh is not made up because it is sunnah, not fard.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling regarding Taraweeh prayer. Many assume that since Taraweeh is emphasized during Ramadan, it must be compensated if missed. However, the Hanafi school holds that Taraweeh, being a sunnah muakkadah, is not subject to qada. We will explore the textual evidence from a hadith and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify the act: missed Taraweeh prayer. The ruling: it is not made up individually or in congregation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurayrah in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah indicating the Prophet encouraged Taraweeh without strict obligation.
Hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ghayr 'azimah' (without strict commitment) shows lack of obligation, so qada is not required.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow making up missed sunnah prayers, but the Hanafi school adheres to the general rule that sunnah prayers are not made up.

(658) And Taraweeh is not made up after it is missed, individually nor in congregation. Translation: (658) And if Taraweeh is missed, do not make it up individually nor in congregation. Explanation: Taraweeh is sunnah to pray, but if it is missed, it is not made up later individually nor in congregation. Evidence: (1) From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to encourage standing in Ramadan without strict commitment. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This hadith indicates that he did not urge it strongly, so if one does not pray it, there is no sin, and hence it is not made up. (2) Sunnah prayers are not made up; therefore if Taraweeh is missed, it is not made up.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of Taraweeh after its time has passed. The ruling is that if Taraweeh is missed, it should not be made up later, either individually or in congregation. The reason is that Taraweeh is a sunnah prayer, and in the Hanafi school, sunnah prayers are not required to be made up if missed (unlike fard prayers). The evidence is a hadith indicating that the Prophet (peace be upon him) encouraged Taraweeh but did not make it an obligation ('azimah). Therefore, missing it does not require qada. This is consistent with the general principle that sunnah prayers are not made up after their time expires.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed obligatory or sunnah prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Missed Taraweeh is not made up; this is grounded in the hadith and the general Hanafi rule that sunnah prayers are not subject to qada.

Preserving Sunan in Tarawih Despite Congregation Fatigue
Ruling on what can and cannot be omitted in Tarawih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which elements of Tarawih prayer must be retained even if the congregation is bored, and identify which element may be omitted according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In Tarawih, salat upon the Prophet, thana', and tasbih are never dropped; only du'a may be omitted when the congregation is bored.

Tarawih is a lengthy prayer, and imams sometimes face a restless congregation. This Hanafi ruling provides clear guidance: certain sunan are so strongly emphasized that they cannot be abandoned even for the sake of speed. In this lesson, you will learn exactly which elements are non-negotiable and which one can be set aside, balancing the school's commitment to sunan with practical concern for the congregation's state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four elements mentioned
List the four acts discussed: salat upon the Prophet (in tashahhud), thana' (opening praise), tasbih of ruku' and sujud, and du'a (supplication after tashahhud).
These are specific to Tarawih in the context of this ruling.
2
Determine the ruling for each
The text explicitly states 'do not leave' for the first three, and 'do not come with du'a' if bored. Thus, the first three are retained; du'a may be omitted.
The ruling for the first three is that they are mu'akkad (confirmed) sunan; omitting them unnecessarily is makruh.
3
Recognize the condition of boredom
The criterion is the congregation's boredom (malal). This condition only affects du'a, not the other elements.
Boredom does not justify dropping confirmed sunan.
4
Note the authority level
The phrase 'ala al-mukhtar' indicates this is the chosen (mufta bihi) opinion in the Hanafi school, likely from later authorities.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۵۷) ولا يترك الصلوة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل تشهد منها ولو ملّ القوم على المختار ولا يترك الثناء وتسبيح الركوع والسجود ولا يأتى بالدعاء ان مل القوم
(657) And do not leave salat upon the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, in every tashahhud of it even if the congregation is bored, according to the chosen opinion. And do not leave the thana' (praise) and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud, and do not recite du'a if the congregation is bored.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the Tarawih prayer. The text states that the imam should not omit reciting the salat (durud) upon the Prophet in every tashahhud during Tarawih, even if the congregation becomes restless or bored. Similarly, the thana' (opening praise) and the tasbih in ruku' and sujud should not be left out. However, if the congregation is bored, the imam may omit the optional du'a after tashahhud, as it is less emphasized. This ruling balances the importance of established sunan with consideration for the congregation's state.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting in prayer where one recites the testimony of faith (al-tahiyyat).
ثناء (thanā'): The opening praise (subhanaka allahumma) recited at the start of prayer.
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): Glorification of Allah, e.g., subhana rabbiya al-‘azim in ruku‘ and subhana rabbiya al-a‘la in sujud.
دعاء (du‘ā’): Supplication, here referring to the du‘a after tashahhud before taslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should the imam do if the congregation becomes bored during Tarawih?
A) Shorten the prayer by omitting salat upon the Prophet.
B) Continue reciting thana', tasbih, and salat, but may omit the optional du'a.
C) Skip all sunan to finish quickly.
D) Delay the prayer until the congregation is willing.

Key Takeaway
In Tarawih, the confirmed sunan of salat upon the Prophet, thana', and tasbih must be retained regardless of congregation boredom; only the optional du'a may be omitted.
