Qada of Missed Tarawih: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling that missed Tarawih is not made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed Tarawih and explain why it is not made up, distinguishing it from obligatory prayers.

Core Idea
Tarawih is time-bound to Ramadan nights; once missed, it is not made up.

This passage delivers a clear rule: missed Tarawih is not to be made up, neither alone nor in congregation. The Hanafi school consistently applies this based on the nature of Tarawih as a time-specific sunnah and the evidence from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary qada for non-binding acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tarawih prayer missed during Ramadan. The ruling state is that it is not made up (lā tuqḍā) after its time has passed, whether performed individually (munfaridan) or in congregation (bi-jamāʿah).
Note the absolute negation: neither form is valid for qada.
2
Understand the time-bound nature
Tarawih is specifically linked to the nights of Ramadan. Its time is fixed; once that time expires, the sunnah is considered lost. This is analogous to other time-specific sunan like the two rakʿahs before Fajr, which are not made up after sunrise.
Time-specificity is key: not all sunan are qada-able.
3
Distinguish fard from sunnah in qada
In Hanafi fiqh, obligatory prayers (fard) must be made up regardless of time, but sunnah prayers are generally not made up. Tarawih is a sunnah muʾakkadah, so it follows the rule of other sunan.
Exception: the sunnah of Fajr may be made up along with the fard; Tarawih has no such exception.
4
Review the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith that the Prophet encouraged qiyām Ramaḍān 'without determination' (min ghayri ʿazīmah), indicating it is not obligatory. As such, missing it does not necessitate compensation. The principle that sunnah acts are not generally repeated also applies.
The hadith is from Abū Hurayrah and recorded in Muṣannaf Ibn Abī Shaybah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۵۸) ولا تُقضى التراويح بفواتها منفردا ولا بجماعة.
(658) And Tarawih is not made up after its time has passed, neither individually nor in congregation.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding the missed Tarawih prayer. The Hanafi school holds that Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah for the month of Ramadan, but if a person misses it, they do not make it up (qada) later, whether alone or in congregation. The reasoning is that Tarawih is a time-specific sunnah; its time is the nights of Ramadan. Once the time is gone, the sunnah is lost. The text cites a hadith from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet encouraged qiyam Ramadan without a strict obligation, and the principle that sunnah prayers are not generally made up. This distinguishes Tarawih from obligatory prayers (fard) which must be made up if missed.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed act of worship after its designated time.
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): The night prayer of Ramadan, consisting of 20 rakʿahs, prayed in congregation during Ramadan nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on making up missed Tarawih?
A) It must be made up individually.
B) It must be made up in congregation.
C) It is not made up at all.
D) It may be made up only if missed for a valid reason.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a time-specific sunnah; once its time expires, it is not to be made up, either alone or in congregation.

Prayer Inside and On Top of the Kaaba
Ruling on validity and dislikedness of prayer in/on Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Kaaba and distinguish between validity and disliked action.

Core Idea
Prayer inside Kaaba is valid; on top it is valid but disliked for disrespect.

The Kaaba is the qibla and the most sacred site in Islam. This lesson addresses a unique scenario: what if one prays inside the Kaaba or on its roof? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the Prophet's own practice, distinguishing between the validity of the prayer itself and the etiquette of the location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? Prayer inside the Kaaba and prayer on top of the Kaaba. The text states both are valid (sahih) for fard and nafl.
The Arabic uses 'صح' (sahha) indicating validity.
2
Note the exception for on top
For prayer on top, the text adds 'لكنه مكروه' (but it is makruh). This is a makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) due to 'إساءة الأدب' (bad manners).
Hanafis distinguish between validity and dislikedness.
3
Understand the role of sutra
The text says 'وإن لم يتخذ سترة' (even if he did not take a sutra). This indicates that the absence of a sutra is not an issue because the qibla is already faced directly inside or on top.
Sutra is not a condition for validity here.
4
Connect to the dalil
The ruling for inside is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet prayed inside the Kaaba. For on top, the dislikedness stems from the act of being above the House of Allah.
The dalil is a confirmation of permissibility, not an explicit prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلوة في الكعبة (۶۵۹) صح فرض و نفل فيها (۲۶۰) وكذا فوقها وان لم يتخذ سترة لكنه مكروه لاساءة الادب
Chapter on prayer in the Kaaba. (659) The prayer of fard and nafl is valid in it. (260) And likewise on top of it, even if he did not take a sutra, but it is makruh due to bad manners.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on prayer within or upon the Kaaba. The ruling states that performing both obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers inside the Kaaba is valid. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet prayed inside the Kaaba. Similarly, praying on top of the Kaaba (i.e., on its roof) is also valid in terms of the prayer itself, but it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because it shows disrespect to the sanctity of the House of Allah. The lack of a sutra (an object in front of the prayer) is not an issue because the direction of the Kaaba is established. The makruh is due to the act of climbing and standing above the Kaaba, which is unbecoming.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of a person praying to prevent passersby from crossing directly before him.
كره (kariha): To be disliked; here it means tanzihi (slightly disliked), not prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid because a sutra is missing.
B) It is valid and recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside or on top of the Kaaba is valid, but praying on top is makruh tanzihi due to disrespect.

Ruling on Turning Away from Imam's Direction in Kaaba
Ruling on validity of prayer if worshipper's back faces other than imam's face

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer inside the Kaaba when the worshipper's back does not face the imam's direction.

Core Idea
Inside the Kaaba, alignment with the imam's back is not required—prayer remains valid.

When praying inside the sacred Kaaba or on its roof, the normal rules of congregational alignment (following in a straight line behind the imam) are eased. The Hanafi school permits a worshipper to face any direction towards the qibla, even if his back is not directly towards the imam's face. This lesson examines the textual basis and the underlying principle of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the ruling applies specifically to prayer inside the Kaaba or on top of it, not to regular mosques.
2
Identify the normal rule
Recall that in normal congregational prayer, followers are expected to stand directly behind the imam, with their backs aligned to the imam's face (i.e., facing the same direction).
3
Identify the exception
Note that the text states: 'if his back is towards other than the face of the imam, then it is permitted.' This is an explicit exception to the normal rule.
4
Determine the ruling
The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) despite the lack of alignment. There is no requirement for congruence of direction inside the Kaaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۶۱) وان كان ظهره الى غير وجه الامام فانه تجوز في جوف الكعبة او فوقها [؟]
(261) And if his back is towards other than the face of the imam, then it is permitted inside the Kaaba or on top of it.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario for prayer inside or on top of the Kaaba: the direction of the worshipper relative to the imam. Normally, followers should align their backs with the imam's face (i.e., the imam faces qibla, and followers line up behind him). However, within the Kaaba or on its roof, due to space constraints, it is permissible if a follower's back faces a different direction from the imam's face. The prayer remains valid. The text indicates that the essential condition is facing the qibla, not necessarily aligning directly behind the imam in a straight line when in constrained spaces.

Key Terms
وجه الامام (wajh al-imām): The direction the imam faces, i.e., the qibla direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid because he is not aligned with the imam.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh.
C) The prayer is valid.
D) The prayer is nullified if the difference is more than 90 degrees.

Key Takeaway
Inside the Kaaba, the normal requirement of alignment behind the imam is waived; prayer remains valid.

Prayer Inside and On Top of the Ka'bah
States rulings on prayer inside and on top of Ka'bah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid; on top is valid but disliked.

This passage addresses two related questions: Is prayer valid inside the Ka'bah? And on its roof? The Hanafi school answers both affirmatively, but with a distinction: inside is without dislike, while on top carries a slight dislike due to disrespect. The proofs are based on the Prophet's own practice and a prohibition hadith interpreted as tanzihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two rulings stated in the matn: (1) prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid (sahih); (2) prayer on top is also valid but makruh.
2
Examine the proof for inside Ka'bah
The hadith of Ibn Umar describes the Prophet praying inside the Ka'bah. This establishes permissibility. Understand why this is proof: the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the proof for on top
The hadith forbidding prayer on the back of the House of Allah is used to establish dislike (karahah), not prohibition. The Hanafi interpretation of the nahy as tanzih is key.
4
Understand the basis for validity
The commentary explains that facing the airspace (fada') of the Ka'bah is sufficient for qibla. This is why both inside and on top are valid: some part of the Ka'bah or its airspace is in front.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may rule differently, especially regarding prayer on top. The Hanafi position is distinct in considering it valid but makruh.
This is not a major dispute here, but awareness is useful.

Chapter on Prayer in the Ka'bah. (659) Fard and nafl prayer are valid in it. (260) And similarly on top of it, even if he does not take a sutra (screen), but it is makruh due to bad manners. [Urdu:] Necessary note: Praying inside the Ka'bah is permissible because some part of the Ka'bah will be in front, serving as the qibla. And that is sufficient. The proofs come later. Translation: (659) Fard and nafl prayer in the Ka'bah is valid. Proof: (1) A hadith from Abd Allah bin Umar that the Prophet entered the Ka'bah with Usama bin Zaid, Bilal, and Uthman bin Talha al-Hajabi, and closed the door, and stayed inside. When asked what the Prophet did, Bilal said he placed a pillar on his left, a pillar on his right, three pillars behind him—the house at that time had six pillars—then he prayed. (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith shows that praying inside the Ka'bah is valid. Translation: (260) Similarly, on top of the Ka'bah is valid even if no sutra, but it is makruh due to bad manners. Explanation: Praying on the roof of the Ka'bah is makruh because it is contrary to its dignity. But if one does pray, it is valid because the airspace opposite the Ka'bah will be in front, which can serve as qibla. It is not necessary to have the wall of the Ka'bah in front; rather, its airspace is sufficient, like praying in an airplane where the wall is not directly in front. However, it is makruh. (1) The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade praying in seven places: garbage dumps, slaughterhouses, graveyards, crossroads, bathrooms, camel resting areas, and on the back of the House of Allah. (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah). This shows that praying on top is makruh, but if one prays, it is valid.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings with proofs. First, prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid for both fard and nafl, supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's prayer inside. Second, prayer on top of the Ka'bah is also valid but makruh (disliked) due to disrespect, supported by the hadith prohibiting prayer on the back of the House of Allah. The commentary explains that the validity is based on facing the airspace of the Ka'bah, which is sufficient for qibla. The karahah is tanzihi (slight dislike) because of the violation of ettiquette, not because the prayer itself is invalid.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'bah that one must face during prayer. The text explains that facing the airspace (fada') opposite the Ka'bah is sufficient for qibla.
مكروه (makruh): An act that is disliked and leaving it is rewarded, but doing it does not invalidate the prayer. Here, praying on top of the Ka'bah is makruh tanzihan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying inside the Ka'bah?
A) It is invalid because the Ka'bah is a sacred place for tawaf, not prayer.
B) It is valid for both fard and nafl without any dislike.
C) It is valid only for nafl, not fard.
D) It is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid, and prayer on top is valid but disliked due to disrespect, based on the Prophet's action and a prohibition hadith interpreted as tanzih.

Four Scenarios of Follower Orientation Inside the Ka'bah
Explains four scenarios of follower orientation towards imam inside Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four possible orientations of a follower relative to the imam inside the Ka'bah and state which are valid, which is invalid, and why.

Core Idea
Inside the Ka'bah, the follower must not be ahead of the imam; turning one's back to the imam's face invalidates the prayer.

Since the Ka'bah is the qibla from all directions inside, one might think any orientation is acceptable. However, the imam serves as a reference for the congregation. This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains four possible orientations between follower and imam and their rulings, emphasizing that the follower must not be positioned ahead of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the unique situation
Understand that inside the Ka'bah, every direction is qibla, so the normal rule of facing a single direction does not apply. However, the imam's position still matters for the follower.
2
Identify the key principle
The core principle is that the follower must not be ahead of the imam. If the follower is ahead, the prayer is invalid.
This principle is derived from the general Hanafi rule that the follower must stay behind or at most level with the imam.
3
Examine the four orientations
Analyze each of the four cases: (1) follower's face to imam's back: valid because follower is behind; (2) follower's face to imam's face: valid but makruh because follower is ahead but not with back to imam; (3) follower's back to imam's back: valid because follower is behind; (4) follower's back to imam's face: invalid because follower is clearly ahead.
Only case (4) is invalid because it places the follower ahead of the imam.
4
Determine the invalid case
Confirm that the only invalid scenario is when the follower's back faces the imam's face. In all other orientations, the prayer is valid, though case (2) is makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۶۱) اور کسی نے اپنی پیٹھ کو امام کے منہ کے علاوہ کی طرف کرے تو اس کی نماز صحیح ہے کعبہ کے اندر، یا اس کے اوپر
۔ اور اگر اپنی پیٹھ کو امام کے چہرے کی طرف کرے گا تو نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ تشريح : کوئی شخص کعبہ کے اندر ہے ، یا اس کے اوپر ہے اس لئے کسی طرف بھی منہ کر کے نماز پڑھے گا تو ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ اس کے ہر طرف قبلہ ہے، لیکن اپنی پیٹھ امام کے منہ کی طرف کرے گا تو نماز نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ یہ امام سے آگے بڑھ گیا، اور امام سے آگے بڑھتا ہے تو نماز نہیں ہوتی ہے، باقی جس طرف بھی پیٹھ کرے گا نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی تفصیل اس طرح ہے۔
[1] امام کی پیٹھ کی طرف مقتدی کا چہرہ ہو۔ یہ صورت جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ امام مقتدی کے بالکل آگے ہوا۔ [۲] امام کے منہ کی طرف مقتدی کا منہ ہو۔ یہ صورت بھی جائز ہے، مگر مگر وہ ہے۔ اس لئے کہ امام سے آگے تو ہے لیکن مقتدی کی پیٹھ امام کی طرف نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو آگے رہنا نہیں کہیں گے ، اور امام کی اتباع کی وجہ سے نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ البتہ امام کے سامنے ہو نے کی وجہ سے ایسا ہو گیا کہ بت کی طرح امام کو سامنے رکھ کر نماز پڑھ رہا ہے اسلئے مکروہ ہے۔ [۳] امام کی پیٹھ کی طرف اپنی پیٹھ کر دے۔ یہ صورت جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ امام کے آگے نہیں ہے، امام کے پیچھے ہی ہے، البتہ امام کی طرف چہرہ کرنا چاہئے تو اس نے پیٹھ کر دی، تاہم جائز ہے، اور متن میں اسی صورت کو بیان کیا ہے [۴] امام کے منہ کی طرف مقتدی اپنی پیٹھ کر دے۔ تو اس صورت میں مقتدی کی نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ امام سے بالکل آگے ہو گیا۔ کعبہ کے اندر نماز پڑھنے کا نقشہ دیکھیں
بیت اللہ
یہ سہی اس کی نماز جائز ہے د مقتدی اس کی نماز جائز نہیں ہے
د امام
یہ سہہاس کی نماز جائز ہے میہ مقتدی اس کی نماز جائز ہے
Translation: (261) If someone turns his back towards other than the face of the imam inside it (the Ka'bah) or on top of it, his prayer is valid. And if he turns his back towards the face of the imam, it is not valid. Explanation: A person who is inside the Ka'bah or on top of it can face any direction and his prayer will be valid because the Ka'bah is in all directions (i.e., qibla is all around). But if he turns his back towards the imam's face, his prayer is invalid because he has gone ahead of the imam, and going ahead of the imam invalidates prayer. In other cases, it is valid. Details: [1] The follower's face is towards the imam's back. Valid because the imam is directly ahead. [2] The follower's face is towards the imam's face. This is also valid but makruh because although he is ahead, his back is not towards the imam, so he is not considered ahead. However, it is makruh as it resembles worshipping the imam like an idol. [3] The follower's back is towards the imam's back. Valid because he is behind the imam, though he should face the imam. [4] The follower's back is towards the imam's face. This invalidates the prayer because he is clearly ahead of the imam. Diagram of prayer inside the Ka'bah: [diagram labels] This arrow: his prayer is valid. Other arrow: follower's prayer is invalid. This arrow: his prayer is valid. That arrow: follower's prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with detailed commentary on the orientation of a follower (muqtadi) relative to the imam when both are inside or on top of the Ka'bah. Since the Ka'bah is qibla from all directions inside, a person can face any direction. However, the imam acts as a reference for the congregation. The key principle is that the follower must not position himself ahead of the imam. The commentary enumerates four cases: (1) face to imam's back: valid (imam ahead), (2) face to imam's face: valid but makruh (ahead but not back towards imam, resembles idol worship), (3) back to imam's back: valid (behind imam), (4) back to imam's face: invalid (ahead of imam). This demonstrates that the sole invalidating condition is when the follower's back is towards the imam's face, placing the follower in front of the imam.

Key Terms
امام (imam): The leader of congregational prayer. In this context, the imam is inside the Ka'bah and the follower's orientation relative to him determines validity.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer. The text discusses four possible orientations of the muqtadi relative to the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following scenarios is the prayer of a follower (muqtadi) inside the Ka'bah invalid?
A) The follower's face is towards the imam's back.
B) The follower's face is towards the imam's face.
C) The follower's back is towards the imam's back.
D) The follower's back is towards the imam's face.

Key Takeaway
Inside the Ka'bah, only when the follower's back faces the imam's face is the prayer invalid; all other orientations are valid.

Following an Imam Inside the Ka'bah from Outside
States ruling on validity of following imam inside Ka'bah from outside with open door

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid iqtida when the imam is inside the Ka'bah and apply it to determine validity.

Core Idea
Following an imam inside the Ka'bah is valid only if the door is open.

This lesson addresses the validity of congregational prayer when the imam leads from inside the Ka'bah building. The Hanafi school stipulates that the door must be open to maintain connection between the imam and followers. We will analyze this specific ruling and its underlying condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqtida (following the imam) when the imam is inside the Ka'bah. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
2
Identify the condition
The condition explicitly stated is that the door of the Ka'bah must be open. This is the key requirement for validity.
3
Apply the condition
If the door is open, iqtida is valid. If the door is closed, the connection is severed and iqtida is invalid.
4
Consider other possible conditions
No other conditions are mentioned. The open door presumably establishes auditory or visual connection, but the text does not require direct sight.
This distinguishes from other schools that may require direct line of sight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۶۲) اور امام کعبہ کے اندر ہو اور دروازہ کھلا ہوتو کعبہ سے باہراقتدا کرنا صحیح ہے۔
Translation: (662) And if the imam is inside the Ka'bah and the door is open, then following (iqtida) from outside the Ka'bah is valid.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement clarifying that when an imam leads prayer from inside the Ka'bah with the door open, those outside can validly follow him. The condition of an open door is essential because it establishes visual or auditory connection, allowing the congregation to follow the imam's actions. This ruling is specific to the unique situation where the imam is within the Ka'bah building.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer. The ruling specifies that this is valid when the imam is inside the Ka'bah and the door is open.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is necessary for a person outside the Ka'bah to validly follow an imam who is praying inside the Ka'bah?
A) The imam must be visible.
B) The door of the Ka'bah must be open.
C) The follower must be inside the Ka'bah as well.
D) The imam must be on top of the Ka'bah.

Key Takeaway
Following an imam inside the Ka'bah is valid only if the door is open.
